This pass continues the prior script recon by decoding EEX semantics. The package is already past the BGT1/encryptResource layer; the remaining task is naming the EEX VM/container records and proving each name with offsets, hex, and decoded payloads.

## 1. EEX Framing Still Holds

All sampled files keep the same container facts from `mod-script-recon.md`: `45 45 58 00` magic, version-like `0x00000201`, header-size at offset `0x0a`.

Native evidence from `C:\Users\Xy172\AppData\Local\Temp\ccz_apk_probe\libMyGame.so` tightens the framing:

- `_ZN13ScriptHandler12DecodeScenesEPcb` reads `bytesToInt(buf, 0x0a)` as the header size.
- It computes `(headerSize - 0x0a) / 4` section offsets.
- It reads each section offset from `0x0a + index * 4`; therefore the first section offset is usually the header size itself (`0x16`, `0x2e`, etc.), not only the later offsets after `0x0e`.
- Each section begins with `int16 scriptCount`.
- Record framing is mixed, not uniformly `prefix + cmd`. At the start of a logical subblock, `DecodeScenes` reads `u16 prefix` then `u16 cmd`; inside an open subblock it can read the next `cmd` directly at the current offset and pass `cmdOffset + 2` into `Script*::initPara`. Child/subscript mode can also skip one extra short between records. This corrects the earlier flat-record assumption.

| File | Size | Magic | Version u32@4 | Header size u32@10 | Offset table |
|---|---:|---|---:|---:|---|
| `Scenes/S_00.eex_new` | 168758 | `45 45 58 00` | `0x00000201` | 22 | `0x16`, `0x6d28`, `0x29319` |
| `Scenes/S_01.eex_new` | 238385 | `45 45 58 00` | `0x00000201` | 22 | `0x16`, `0xd850`, `0x3a314` |
| `Scenes/S_02.eex_new` | 180517 | `45 45 58 00` | `0x00000201` | 22 | `0x16`, `0xa724`, `0x2c108` |
| `Scenes/S_1010.eex_new` | 47015 | `45 45 58 00` | `0x00000201` | 22 | `0x16`, `0x3dfb`, `0xb78a` |
| `Scenes/R_00.eex_new` | 635874 | `45 45 58 00` | `0x00000201` | 46 | `0x2e`, `0x2861c`, `0x28aad`, `0x294f4`, `0x2a728`, `0x2bd23`, `0x2ca06`, `0x2d363`, `0x3c740` |
| `Scenes/R_01.eex_new` | 32489 | `45 45 58 00` | `0x00000201` | 30 | `0x1e`, `0xd5f`, `0x2672`, `0x4661`, `0x6108` |
| `Scenes/R_02.eex_new` | 49006 | `45 45 58 00` | `0x00000201` | 54 | `0x36`, `0xd34`, `0x1166`, `0x247c`, `0x3bcc`, `0x4059`, `0x4b11`, `0x6d2e`, `0x7805`, `0x833b`, `0x9ac9` |
| `Scenes/R_119.eex_new` | 143 | `45 45 58 00` | `0x00000201` | 14 | none |

Status: green for framing. This is parseable structure, not an opaque blob.

## 1.1 Native `getScriptByCmd` Ground Truth

Source: `libMyGame.so`, ARM 32-bit ELF, `.dynsym` present.

`_ZN13ScriptHandler14getScriptByCmdEs` normalizes `cmd - 2`, rejects values above `0x7a`, then dispatches through a halfword jump table at `0x006ff112`. The case blocks load vtables through signed GOT-relative offsets. Treating those offsets as unsigned creates a shifted, wrong class table; the corrected table below sign-extends the GOT offset before resolving `_ZTV*`.

| Cmd | Class | Evidence |
|---:|---|---|
| `0x0002` | `ScriptChildInfo` | case target `0x006ff208`, alloc `0x28`, vtable `_ZTV15ScriptChildInfo`; `S_00@0x18` payload `05 00 e6 88 98 e5 89 8d e8 bf 87 e6 b8 a1 00` decodes as `战前过渡`. |
| `0x0003` | `ScriptElse` | target `0x006ff22a`, vtable `_ZTV10ScriptElse`. |
| `0x0004` | `ScriptTestAsk` | target `0x006ff248`, vtable `_ZTV13ScriptTestAsk`. |
| `0x0005` | `ScriptTestValue` | target `0x006ff26a`, vtable `_ZTV15ScriptTestValue`. |
| `0x0012` | `ScriptShowChoice` | target `0x006ff41a`, vtable `_ZTV16ScriptShowChoice`; `initPara` reads `short`, NUL UTF-8 string, then two shorts. |
| `0x0013` | `ScriptCase` | target `0x006ff440`, vtable `_ZTV10ScriptCase`; `initPara` returns `payload + 6`. |
| `0x0014` | `ScriptActorTalk` | target `0x006ff45e`, vtable `_ZTV15ScriptActorTalk`; `initPara` reads `short` and NUL UTF-8 dialogue. |
| `0x0015` | `ScriptActorTalk2` | target `0x006ff484`, vtable `_ZTV16ScriptActorTalk2`; `initPara` reads five shorts then NUL UTF-8 dialogue. |
| `0x0016`-`0x001a` | `ScriptCommonInfo` | shared target `0x006ff4aa`, vtable `_ZTV16ScriptCommonInfo`; title/location/win-text labels are command variants, not separate parsers. |
| `0x0036` | `ScriptTestActorState` | target `0x006ff8c4`, vtable `_ZTV20ScriptTestActorState`; retreat/death labels fit this better than the earlier generic trigger guess. |
| `0x0038` | `ScriptSetActorAbility` | target `0x006ff900`, vtable `_ZTV21ScriptSetActorAbility`. |
| `0x0042` | `ScriptTestVictory` | target `0x006ffa2c`, vtable `_ZTV17ScriptTestVictory`. |
| `0x0043` | `ScriptTestFail` | target `0x006ffa4a`, vtable `_ZTV14ScriptTestFail`. |
| `0x0048` | `ScriptSetEnemyGoods` | target `0x006ffb94`, vtable `_ZTV19ScriptSetEnemyGoods`; fixed legacy payload length `0x18`. |
| `0x004b` | `ScriptDispatchOwn` | target `0x006ffc34`, vtable `_ZTV17ScriptDispatchOwn`; fixed legacy payload length `0x1a`. |
| `0x0053` | `ScriptBattleActorLeave` | target `0x006ffd0a`, vtable `_ZTV22ScriptBattleActorLeave`; likely the action-side leave/retreat op. |
| `0x005b` | `ScriptBattleHighlightArea` | target `0x006ffdf0`, vtable `_ZTV25ScriptBattleHighlightArea`; earlier “area condition” label was too strong. |
| `0x005c` | `ScriptBattleHighlightActor` | target `0x006ffe0c`, vtable `_ZTV26ScriptBattleHighlightActor`; earlier “spawn/select unit” label was too strong. |

Known default/unsupported commands from the native switch: `0x0010`, `0x001e`, `0x0044`, `0x0049`, `0x0051`, `0x006a`. Section 4.16 updates their corpus status: `0x001e`, `0x0044`, `0x0049`, and `0x0051` are present as zero-payload base markers; `0x0010` and `0x006a` are absent from the parsed scene records.

## 2. String Payload Ledger

Probe rule: scan for `05 00`, read bytes until NUL, accept only valid UTF-8 printable strings containing CJK or known script labels. Then count the immediate preceding u16.

| Preceding u16 before `05 00` | Total string hits | R hits | S hits | Interpretation | Status |
|---:|---:|---:|---:|---|---|
| `0x0016` | 97703 | 4129 | 93574 | `ScriptCommonInfo` text variant; includes tutorial/help/instruction text. Too broad to call a battle op by itself. | Native class known; semantic variant candidate |
| `0x0014` | 27515 | 15595 | 11920 | `ScriptActorTalk` dialogue/message text. | Strong |
| `0x0000` | 27351 | 1617 | 25734 | Not a semantic op by itself; likely false grouping from embedded list/string blocks. | Do not map |
| `0x0069` | 23256 | 20890 | 2366 | Notification/menu/info text candidate, e.g. mode messages. | Candidate |
| `0x0002` | 15339 | 4170 | 11169 | `ScriptChildInfo`; block/section label record. | Native class known |
| `0x0012` | 5404 | 5321 | 83 | `ScriptShowChoice`; choice option/prompt text with two trailing shorts. | Strong |
| `0x0018` | 1041 | 1041 | 0 | `ScriptCommonInfo` variant used as R scene title. | Strong |
| `0x0017` | 1003 | 1003 | 0 | `ScriptCommonInfo` variant used as R scene location. | Strong |
| `0x002c` | 813 | 813 | 0 | R narration/cutscene prose candidate. | Medium |
| `0x0019` | 239 | 0 | 239 | `ScriptCommonInfo` variant used as S win/lose condition display text. | Strong |
| `0x001a` | 207 | 0 | 207 | `ScriptCommonInfo` variant used as S condition success label text. | Strong |

Important boundary: `05 00` is best treated as a typed string literal marker, not as the event opcode itself. The event opcode is usually the native `cmd` immediately before it, e.g. `14 00 05 00 <dialogue>` means `ScriptActorTalk` with a string literal payload.

## 3. Candidate Opcode Ledger

| Opcode / tag | Evidence | Current meaning | Certainty | Conversion impact |
|---:|---|---|---|---|
| `0x0004` | Repeated as `04 00 <u32le>` inside deployment records, e.g. `04 00 0b 00 00 00`. | u32 integer literal/tag. | High | Needed by all structured parser work. |
| `0x0005` | Repeated as `05 00 <valid UTF-8 NUL string>`. | UTF-8 string literal/tag. | High | Enables lossless text extraction. |
| `0x0012` | Native class `_ZTV16ScriptShowChoice`; `R_00` offset `0x000276`: choice option text; `R_01` offset `0x000868`: `欣然接受\n婉言谢绝`. | `ScriptShowChoice`. | High | Choice UI text extractable; branch targets still need mapping through `ScriptCase`/flow control. |
| `0x0014` | Native class `_ZTV15ScriptActorTalk`; 27515 string hits; `R_01` offset `0x00010c`, `S_00` offset `0x0041ef`. | `ScriptActorTalk` dialogue/message text. | High | Dialogue can be dumped and later mapped to R/S script ops. |
| `0x0015` | Native class `_ZTV16ScriptActorTalk2`; `initPara` reads five shorts then a UTF-8 string. | `ScriptActorTalk2`, not a choice container. | High for parser, medium for field semantics | Prompt-like strings remain recoverable; the five leading fields need names. |
| `0x0016` | Native class `_ZTV16ScriptCommonInfo`; 97703 string hits; `S_00` offset `0x006ea7`: `移动到……`. | `ScriptCommonInfo` variant. | High for parser, medium for semantic variant | Text extractable; variant semantics need per-command labels. |
| `0x0017` | Native class `_ZTV16ScriptCommonInfo`; 1003 R hits only; `R_01` offset `0x0000ec`: location `蓟城  刺史府`. | `ScriptCommonInfo` scene-location variant. | High | R scene metadata extractable. |
| `0x0018` | Native class `_ZTV16ScriptCommonInfo`; 1041 R hits only; `R_01` offset `0x0000e1`: title `凯旋`. | `ScriptCommonInfo` scene-title variant. | High | R scene metadata extractable. |
| `0x0019` | Native class `_ZTV16ScriptCommonInfo`; 239 S hits only; `S_00` offset `0x005954` and `0x023104`. | `ScriptCommonInfo` win/lose condition display variant. | High | User-facing condition text extractable; machine condition bytes still separate. |
| `0x001a` | Native class `_ZTV16ScriptCommonInfo`; 207 S hits only; follows `0x0019`, e.g. `S_00` offset `0x0059e3` `到达村庄！`. | `ScriptCommonInfo` success-label variant. | High | User-facing victory label extractable. |
| `0x0032` | Native class `_ZTV15ScriptActorMove`; strict 30-byte payload shape has `5551` records in `209` files. Sample `S_01.eex_new@0x29a96`: `32 00 40 00 01 00 02 00 ff ff 04 00 03 00 00 00 04 00 07 00 00 00 04 00 10 00 00 00 2b 00 00 00`. | `ScriptActorMove`, scripted actor movement/update. | High for byte structure, medium for mode/facing labels | Candidate numeric `MoveUnit`/map actor move op. Actor source mode, x/y target, and direction field are separable; human labels for mode `-1/0/1` and direction `0..3/-1` are not proven. |
| `0x0036` | Native class `_ZTV20ScriptTestActorState`; appears immediately after retreat event labels: `36 00 02 00 <unit-id> ...`. | `ScriptTestActorState`, usually actor-property predicate in those samples. | High for class/property enum, medium for actor namespace | Key trigger condition is structurally separable; actor selector namespace still needs proof. |
| `0x0037` | Native `ScriptMoneyTest::initPara@0x00715e25` reads tag/source, tag/int threshold, tag/comparator and returns `payload + 0x0e`; strict old-EEX tuple `(28,04,24)` has `23` raw-canonical records. Sample `R_43.eex_new@0x6887`: `37 00 28 00 00 00 04 00 10 27 00 00 24 00 00 00`. | `ScriptMoneyTest`, money / counter comparison condition. | High for byte structure, medium for source namespaces | Source `0` uses `History::GetMoney`; sources `1/2` use global counter fields still unnamed. Comparator `0/1/2` is native-proven as `>=`, `<`, `==`. |
| `0x0038` | Native `ScriptSetActorAbility::initPara@0x007163b1` reads seven shorts plus one int and returns `payload + 0x12`; canonical tag tuple `(02,23,34,04)` has `266953` records, matching the exact-end command count. Sample `S_00.eex_new@0x7dc9`: `38 00 02 00 00 00 23 00 0a 00 34 00 01 00 04 00 05 00 00 00`. | `ScriptSetActorAbility`, actor stat/HP/MP/level/image-field mutation. | High for byte structure and native setter targets, medium for actor namespace / property-15 label | Candidate numeric `SetActorAbility` op. Property selectors `0..15` are separated; C++ setter symbols name most stat/HP/MP/level targets. |
| `0x000b` | Native `ScriptSetValue::initPara@0x0070fa4d` returns `payload + 0x0a`; canonical tag tuple `(04,00,27)` has `71834` records, matching the exact-end command count. Sample `R_00.eex_new@0x5743c`: `0b 00 04 00 2d 01 00 00 27 00 00 00`. | `ScriptSetValue`, write condition/global flag byte by id. | High for byte structure, medium for variable-id labels | Pairs with `ScriptTestValue` flag-list reads. Preserve variable ids numerically until condition namespace labels are proven. |
| `0x003a` | Native `ScriptMoneyChange::initPara@0x0071667d` reads five shorts plus one int and returns `payload + 0x0e`; strict tuple `(28,34,04)` has `108` records. Sample `R_01.eex_new@0x08a6`: `3a 00 28 00 00 00 34 00 01 00 04 00 d0 07 00 00`. | `ScriptMoneyChange`, money / counter assignment-add-subtract. | High for byte structure, medium for non-money source labels | Source `0` reaches `History::SetMoney`; source `2` appears bounded `0..100`; op enum `0/1/2` is assign/add/subtract. |
| `0x003b` | Native `ScriptArmyChange::initPara@0x00716eb1` reads six shorts and returns `payload + 0x0c`; canonical tag tuple `(02,0e,3e)` has `4072` records, matching exact-end command count. `HandleRScript@0x0071672c` calls `History::ArmyCome@0x00680e40`, `History::ArmyComeReturnToLeave@0x0067d8c8`, or `History::ArmyLeave@0x00681404`; battle `HandleScript@0x007167d8` writes actor state bytes `+0x89/+0x8a` as `0/1/2`. Sample `R_00.eex_new@0x2e08b`: `3b 00 02 00 e7 03 0e 00 ff 00 3e 00 00 00`. | `ScriptArmyChange`, army/party actor availability and battle-list state change. | High for byte structure and come/leave direction, medium for mode/order policy labels | Retained fields are `#0x22 actor`, `#0x26 state/action`, `#0x2a mode/order`. R-side roster direction is no longer opaque; actor `0`, mode/order labels, and S-side high-level battle-list naming remain fail-closed. |
| `0x003d` | Native `ScriptGetGood::initPara@0x00716f93` reads eight shorts and returns `payload + 0x10`; strict tuple `(17,49,26,02)` has `8474` records, matching exact-end command count. Update for `0x0048`: the row above predates the `HandleScript@0x00718d11` trace in section 4.5. Slot order is now runtime-proven: `#0x26/#0x2a` weapon/id-level policy, `#0x2e/#0x32` armor/id-level policy, `#0x36` third equipment slot. The remaining uncertainty is default/random level policy, not slot byte shape.

## 4. Evidence Blocks

### 4.1 R Scene Metadata and Dialogue

`Scenes/R_01.eex_new`

- Offset `0x0000e1`
- Hex: `18 00 05 00 e5 87 af e6 97 8b 00`
- UTF-8: `凯旋`
- Interpretation: `0x0018` scene title.
- Status: strong.

`Scenes/R_01.eex_new`

- Offset `0x0000ec`
- Hex: `17 00 05 00 e8 93 9f e5 9f 8e 20 20 e5 88 ba e5 8f b2 e5 ba 9c 00`
- UTF-8: `蓟城  刺史府`
- Interpretation: `0x0017` scene location.
- Status: strong.

`Scenes/R_01.eex_new`

- Offset `0x00010c`
- Hex before text: `1c 00 09 00 04 00 05 00 00 00 14 00 05 00 26`
- UTF-8: `&刘焉\n玄德果然不负我望。`
- Interpretation: `0x0014` dialogue message; leading `&` is embedded speaker marker.
- Status: strong.

### 4.2 Choice Prompt and Options

`Scenes/R_00.eex_new`

- Prompt marker offset: `0x000228`
- Hex before text: `00 00 04 00 03 00 00 00 01 00 15 00 02 00 fc 03 02 00 fc 03 05 00`
- UTF-8: `你已完成低难度4周目挑战，\n是否愿意挑战地狱难度？`
- Interpretation: `0x0015` is native `ScriptActorTalk2`; the prompt text is recoverable, but the five leading shorts are not yet named.
- Status: class high, field semantics medium.

`Scenes/R_00.eex_new`

- Option marker offset: `0x000276`
- Hex before text: `e5 9c b0 e7 8b b1 e9 9a be e5 ba a6 ef bc 9f 00 01 00 12 00 05 00`
- UTF-8: `不了，我还是继续【现在的模式】\n好吧，我尝试挑战【地狱模式】`
- Interpretation: `0x0012` is native `ScriptShowChoice` choice option text; branch target still needs `ScriptCase`/flow-control mapping.
- Status: strong.

`Scenes/R_01.eex_new`

- Option marker offset: `0x000868`
- Hex before text: `ff 00 09 00 04 00 05 00 00 00 24 00 09 00 0b 00 01 00 12 00 05 00`
- UTF-8: `欣然接受\n婉言谢绝`
- Interpretation: another native `ScriptShowChoice` block.
- Status: strong.

`Scenes/S_01.eex_new`

- Hex before text: `... 00 00 00 00 00 00 00 19 00 05 00`

`Scenes/S_1010.eex_new`

- Hex before text: `4f 00 02 00 00 00 02 00 ff ff 2b 00 00 00 26 00 00 00 26 00 00 00 26 00 01 00 19 00 05 00`
- UTF-8: `胜利条件\n★·击退张勋或纪灵。\n\n失败条件\n☆·刘备死亡。\n☆·我军鹿砦被占领。`
- Interpretation: `S_1010` is a real stage script, not a stray test blob.
- Status: strong.

### 4.4 Player Deployment Records: `0x004b`

Offsets in this section point at the `cmd` word (`4b 00`), not the full record start. The full EEX record has a 2-byte prefix immediately before the command, e.g. `Scenes/S_00.eex_new@0x001a19` begins `72 00 4b 00 ...`.

Record shape observed after `HEX我军设定`:

```text
4b 00
04 00 <slot-or-index u32>
04 00 <x-like u32>
04 00 <y-like u32>
2b 00 <side/group-like u16>
26 00 <flag-like u16>
```

Native parser evidence:

- `ScriptDispatchOwn::initPara` starts at payload offset after `4b 00`.
- It reads `short`, `int`, `short`, `int`, `short`, `int`, `short`, `short`, `short`, `short`, then returns `payload + 0x1a`.
- `ScriptDispatchOwn::saveScript` writes the command id and only the semantic values corresponding to the three ints plus two shorts; the interleaved `04 00`, `2b 00`, and `26 00` values are legacy field tags, not separate battle ops.

`Scenes/S_00.eex_new`

- Label offset: `0x001a07`, text `HEX我军设定`
- Records: 15 fixed-length records, start `0x001a1b`, end `0x001bbf`
- First record hex: `4b 00 04 00 00 00 00 00 04 00 00 00 00 00 04 00 03 00 00 00 2b 00 02 00 26 00 01 00`
- Parsed fields: slot/index `0`, x-like `0`, y-like `3`, tag `0x002b=2`, tag `0x0026=1`
- Last shown record offset `0x001ba3`: slot/index `14`, x-like `3`, y-like `0`
- Map check: `terrainMap_1.json` has `map_width=23`, `map_height=16`; all shown x/y fields are inside range.
- Status: high-confidence deployment slots.

`Scenes/S_01.eex_new`

- Label offset: `0x001a07`, text `HEX我军设定`
- Records: 16 fixed-length records, start `0x001a1b`, end `0x001bdb`
- First record hex: `4b 00 04 00 00 00 00 00 04 00 0b 00 00 00 04 00 12 00 00 00 2b 00 00 00 26 00 00 00`
- Parsed fields: slot/index `0`, x-like `11`, y-like `18`, tag `0x002b=0`, tag `0x0026=0`
- Other records show x-like `7..13`, y-like `17..19`.
- Map check: `terrainMap_2.json` has inferred dimensions `21x20`; x/y values are inside range if S_01 corresponds to map 2. This correspondence needs formal proof, but the coordinate shape is plausible.
- Status: high-confidence deployment slots; battle-to-map binding still needs a separate lookup.

`Scenes/S_1010.eex_new`

- Label offset: `0x0015e9`, text `HEX我军设定`
- Records: 10 fixed-length records, start `0x0015fd`, end `0x001715`
- First record hex: `4b 00 04 00 00 00 00 00 04 00 02 00 00 00 04 00 17 00 00 00 2b 00 00 00 26 00 00 00`
- Parsed fields: slot/index `0`, x-like `2`, y-like `23`, tag `0x002b=0`, tag `0x0026=0`
- Status: special-numbered stage also uses the same deployment layout.

### 4.5 Equipment Records: `0x0048`

Offsets in this section point at the `cmd` word (`48 00`), not the full record start. The full EEX record has a 2-byte prefix immediately before the command, e.g. `Scenes/S_00.eex_new@0x001bd0` begins `50 00 48 00 ...`.

Record shape observed after `AI装备`, `装备设定`, or `个人装备设定`:

```text
48 00 02 00 <hero-like u16>
3b 00 <item-like u16> 49 00 00 00
3c 00 <item-like u16> 49 00 00 00
3d 00 <item-like u16>
```

The first value often resolves against `dic_hero.hid`; the later values resolve against `dic_item.good_id`. Slot order is not yet proven.

Native parser evidence:

- `ScriptSetEnemyGoods::initPara` starts at payload offset after `48 00`.
- It reads 12 shorts and returns `payload + 0x18`.
- `ScriptSetEnemyGoods::saveScript` writes the command id and only six value fields (`#0x22`, `#0x26`, `#0x2a`, `#0x2e`, `#0x32`, `#0x36`). The interleaved `02 00`, `3b 00`, `49 00`, `3c 00`, `49 00`, `3d 00` values are legacy field tags/markers.

Runtime execution evidence from `ScriptSetEnemyGoods::HandleScript@0x00718d11`:

| Native address | Instruction hex | Decoded instruction | Runtime meaning |
|---:|---|---|---|
| `0x00718d48` | `26 21` / `52 5e` | `movs r1,#0x26`; `ldrsh r2,[r2,r1]` | Reads field `#0x26` as weapon instruction/id. |
| `0x00718d58` | `77 f7 80 fa` | `bl HistoryActor::SetDefaultGood` with `r1=1` | `#0x26 <= 0` means default weapon. |
| `0x00718d92` | `26 21` / `59 5e` / `02 39` | `movs r1,#0x26`; `ldrsh r1,[r3,r1]`; `subs r1,#2` | `#0x26 > 1` becomes weapon `good_id = field - 2`. |
| `0x00718d98` | `7b f7 1c fa` | `bl HistoryGood::SetGoodID` | Applies decoded weapon item id. |
| `0x00718de8` | `2a 22` / `9a 5e` | `movs r2,#0x2a`; `ldrsh r2,[r3,r2]` | Reads field `#0x2a` as weapon level / level policy. |
| `0x00718dee` | `7b f7 8f fe` | `bl HistoryGood::init` | Initializes weapon with decoded level when explicit. |
| `0x00718e02` | `2e 25` / `5d 5f` | `movs r5,#0x2e`; `ldrsh r5,[r3,r5]` | Reads field `#0x2e` as coat/armor instruction/id. |
| `0x00718e10` | `77 f7 24 fa` | `bl HistoryActor::SetDefaultGood` with `r1=2` | `#0x2e <= 0` means default armor. |
| `0x00718e52` | `2e 21` / `59 5e` / `02 39` | `movs r1,#0x2e`; `ldrsh r1,[r3,r1]`; `subs r1,#2` | `#0x2e > 1` becomes armor id base, then adds item-table offset. |
| `0x00718e64` | `7b f7 b6 f9` | `bl HistoryGood::SetGoodID` | Applies decoded armor item id. |
| `0x00718ede` | `32 22` / `9a 5e` | `movs r2,#0x32`; `ldrsh r2,[r3,r2]` | Reads field `#0x32` as armor level / level policy. |
| `0x00718ee4` | `7b f7 14 fe` | `bl HistoryGood::init` | Initializes armor with decoded level when explicit. |
| `0x00718ef8` | `36 21` / `59 5e` | `movs r1,#0x36`; `ldrsh r1,[r3,r1]` | Reads field `#0x36` as third equipment item instruction/id. |
| `0x00718f02` | `04 21` / `77 f7 a9 f9` | `movs r1,#4`; `bl HistoryActor::SetDefaultGood` | `#0x36 <= 0` means default third equipment slot. |
| `0x00718f20`-`0x00718f34` | `28 1c ... 02 39 7b f7 4e f9` | add table offsets, `subs r1,#2`, `bl HistoryGood::SetGoodID` | `#0x36 > 1` maps through weapon+armor table counts into the third slot id namespace. |
| `0x00718f46` / `0x00718f4c` / `0x00718f54` | `01 22`; `7b f7 e0 fd`; `76 f7 f6 fb` | `movs r2,#1`; `bl HistoryGood::init`; `bl HistoryActor::UpdataGoodEffect` | Third slot level is fixed to `1`, then actor good effects are refreshed. |

Status: weapon/armor/third-slot structure is green. Remaining uncertainty is policy detail, not byte shape: when level fields are `<= 0`, runtime derives a level from actor level and equipment metadata/random helpers.

`Scenes/S_00.eex_new`

- Label offset: `0x001bc5`, text `AI装备`
- Record offset `0x001bd2`
- Hex: `48 00 02 00 b5 00 3b 00 00 00 49 00 00 00 3c 00 00 00 49 00 00 00 3d 00 3a 00`
- ID evidence: `0x00b5=181` resolves to `dic_hero.hid=181` `速仆丸`; `0x003a=58` resolves to `dic_item.good_id=58` `硬皮甲`.
- Status: medium-high.

`Scenes/S_01.eex_new`

- Label offset: `0x001be1`, text `AI装备`
- Record offset `0x001bee`
- Hex: `48 00 02 00 76 00 3b 00 0c 00 49 00 00 00 3c 00 0d 00 49 00 00 00 3d 00 3a 00`
- ID evidence: `0x0076=118` resolves to `dic_hero.hid=118` `刘虞`; `0x000c=12` resolves to `dic_item.good_id=12` `凤嘴刀`; `0x003a=58` resolves to `硬皮甲`.
- Status: medium-high.

`Scenes/S_1010.eex_new`

- Label offset: `0x00171b`, text `个人装备设定`
- Record offset `0x001732`
- Hex: `48 00 02 00 89 00 3b 00 26 00 49 00 00 00 3c 00 00 00 49 00 00 00 3d 00 06 00`
- ID evidence: `0x0089=137` resolves to `dic_hero.hid=137` `袁术`; `0x0026=38` resolves to `dic_item.good_id=38` `铁蒺藜骨朵`; `0x0006=6` resolves to `虎头枪`.
- Status: medium-high as cross-table id evidence; slot semantics are now governed by the runtime trace above.

### 4.6 Retreat / Defeat Condition Candidate: `0x0036` / `ScriptTestActorState`

Offsets in the hex samples point at the `cmd` word (`36 00`), not the full record start.

Native parser evidence:

- `ScriptTestActorState::initPara` starts at payload offset after `36 00`.
- It reads nine shorts in the legacy stream and returns `payload + 0x12`.
- `ScriptTestActorState::saveScript` writes the command id and four semantic fields (`#0x22`, `#0x26`, `#0x2c`, `#0x32`). The remaining words in the legacy stream are field tags/markers or ignored compatibility values.

`Scenes/S_01.eex_new`

- Label marker offset: `0x03746e`
- Label hex before text: `49 00 0e 00 0d 00 00 00 09 00 02 00 05 00`
- Label UTF-8: `关羽撤退`
- Following hex: `36 00 02 00 01 00 23 00 07 00 04 00 00 00 00 00 24 00 02 00 05 00 35 00 00 00 35 00 01 00 79 00 00 00 61 00 14 00 05 00 26 ...`
- Native class: `ScriptTestActorState`.
- Interpretation: in this label context, the condition tests actor selector `1`, property `7` current HP, comparator `2` equals, threshold `0`; followed by other condition/action records and a dialogue block.
- Status: class/property high, actor id namespace medium.

`Scenes/S_01.eex_new`

- Label marker offset: `0x037512`
- Label UTF-8: `张飞撤退`
- Following hex: `36 00 02 00 02 00 23 00 07 00 04 00 00 00 00 00 24 00 02 00 05 00 35 00 00 00 35 00 01 00 7a 00 00 00 66 00 14 00 05 00 26 ...`
- Native class: `ScriptTestActorState`.
- Interpretation: same current-HP-zero pattern, actor selector `2`.
- Status: class/property high, actor id namespace medium.

`Scenes/S_1010.eex_new`

- Label marker offset: `0x009619`
- Label UTF-8: `纪灵撤退1`
- Following hex: `36 00 02 00 89 00 23 00 07 00 04 00 00 00 00 00 24 00 02 00 05 00 35 00 01 00 46 00 ...`
- ID evidence: `0x0089=137` resolves to `dic_hero.hid=137` `袁术`, but this event label says `纪灵`. Therefore the field may be battle-local actor id, not global `hid`. Do not silently map it as `dic_hero.hid`.
- Status: class high, with a critical uncertainty about id namespace.

### 4.7 `DecodeScenes` Flow-Control Probe

`Scenes/S_00.eex_new`, first section at `0x16`:

- Section count at `0x16`: `01 00`.
- First full record at `0x18`: `e9 02 02 00 05 00 e6 88 98 e5 89 8d e8 bf 87 e6 b8 a1 00`.
- Parsed with native table:
  - prefix `0x02e9`
  - cmd `0x0002` = `ScriptChildInfo`
  - payload tag `0x0005`
  - UTF-8 text `战前过渡`
- `ScriptChildInfo::initPara` returns after the string at offset `0x2b`.
- `DecodeScenes` child-mode path then advances by an additional 2 bytes before the next record; the next plausible record begins at `0x2d`.

Follow-on offsets with that extra 2-byte child-mode advance:

| Offset | Prefix | Cmd | Native class | Evidence |
|---:|---:|---:|---|---|
| `0x002d` | `0x3e44` | `0x0044` | default/base `Script(cmd)` | `44 3e 44 00`; native `getScriptByCmd` has no class for `0x0044`. |
| `0x0031` | `0x0045` | `0x0026` | `ScriptTestActorArea` | `45 00 26 00 ...`; native `initPara` payload length is `0x1c`. |
| `0x0053` | `0x0000` | `0x0047` | `ScriptDispatchEnemy` | reached after `ScriptTestActorArea` payload plus another 2-byte child-mode advance. |

Interpretation: EEX is not a flat linear list. A safe dumper must emulate the `DecodeScenes` child/subscript flow-control, including default/base commands, before it can claim complete command coverage. This does not weaken the structural verdict; it explains why a naive linear parser appears to desync.

### 4.8 Native Field Retention and Roster Shape

`saveScript` is useful but must be interpreted conservatively. It proves which fields the original engine retains when serializing a `Script*` object, but it is not a guarantee that every retained field is gameplay semantic; roster child records in particular retain old field tags as well as values.

Selected `saveScript` signatures:

| Native class | Retained fields after command id | Evidence |
|---|---|---|
| `ScriptShowChoice` | string at object `#0x24`, short `#0x2a` | `saveScript@0x00711841` writes short cmd, string, short. |
| `ScriptCase` | int `#0x24` | `saveScript@0x007118bf` writes short cmd, int. |
| `ScriptActorTalk` | string `#0x24` | `saveScript@0x00711af1` writes short cmd, string. |
| `ScriptActorTalk2` | shorts `#0x22`, `#0x26`, string `#0x2c` | `saveScript@0x007121f9` writes short cmd, short, short, string. |
| `ScriptTestActorPos` | short `#0x22`, ints `#0x28`, `#0x30` | `saveScript@0x00713343`. |
| `ScriptTestActorArea` | short `#0x22`, ints `#0x28`, `#0x30`, `#0x38`, `#0x40` | `saveScript@0x0071351b`. |
| `ScriptTestActorState` | shorts `#0x22`, `#0x26`, int `#0x2c`, short `#0x32` | `saveScript@0x0071545d`. |
| `ScriptSetMaxRound` | short `#0x22`, int `#0x28` | `saveScript@0x0071d1e9`. |
| `ScriptDispatchOwn` | ints `#0x24`, `#0x2c`, `#0x34`, shorts `#0x3a`, `#0x3e`, then global own-force list | `saveScript@0x00719781`; the global list write means not all trailing data is local to one record. |
| `ScriptSetEnemyGoods` | six shorts: `#0x22`, `#0x26`, `#0x2a`, `#0x2e`, `#0x32`, `#0x36` | `saveScript@0x00719083`. |
| `ScriptBattleActorTurn` | shorts `#0x22`, `#0x26`, `#0x2a`, `#0x2e`, `#0x32`, `#0x36` | `saveScript@0x0071b591`; writes command id, then these six retained fields. |
| `ScriptBattleActorAction` | shorts `#0x22`, `#0x26`, `#0x2a`, `#0x2e` | `saveScript@0x0071b76f`; writes command id, then these four retained fields. |
| `ScriptBattleActorLeave` | shorts `#0x22`, `#0x26`, ints `#0x2c`, `#0x34`, `#0x3c`, `#0x44`, shorts `#0x4a`, `#0x4e` | `saveScript@0x0071ba49`. |
| `ScriptBattleHighlightArea` | ints `#0x24`, `#0x2c`, `#0x34`, `#0x3c`, short `#0x42` | `saveScript@0x0071d061`. |
| `ScriptBattleHighlightActor` | short `#0x22` | `saveScript@0x0071d179`. |

Roster parent evidence from `getScriptByCmd` case blocks:

Important correction: the native object stride is not the old EEX file payload length. The parent `initPara` methods walk child objects in memory, but the file cursor is chained through each child object's own `initPara` return value.

| Cmd | Native class | Object stride | Child count | File child length | File parent payload | Native evidence | Current status |
|---:|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---|---|
| `0x0046` | `ScriptDispatchFriend` | `0x5c` | `0x14` = 20 | `0x34` | `0x410` | case target `0x006ffa86` allocates children at object stride `0x5c`; parent `initPara@0x0071859b` chains child parse returns; `ScriptDispatchOneFriend::initPara@0x0071dd00` returns `payload + 0x34`. | Friend roster file boundary known; `HandleScript@0x007185dd` names actor id, x/y, and level-related fields. |
| `0x0047` | `ScriptDispatchEnemy` | `0x60` | `0x50` = 80 | `0x38` | `0x1180` | case target `0x006ffb0e` allocates children at object stride `0x60`; parent `initPara@0x0071896b` chains child parse returns; `ScriptDispatchOneEnemy::initPara@0x0071da92` returns `payload + 0x38`. | Enemy roster file boundary known; `HandleScript@0x007189ad` names actor id and level-related fields, with remaining AI/team fields unresolved. |

Child record evidence:

| Child class | Old EEX file payload length | Old read type | Retained fields from `saveScript` | Status |
|---|---:|---|---|---|
| `ScriptDispatchOneFriend` | `0x34` | all `bytesToShort` reads | shorts/ints stored at `#0x22`, `#0x26`, `#0x2c`, `#0x34`, `#0x3a`, `#0x3e`, `#0x42`, `#0x46`, `#0x4a`, `#0x50`, `#0x58` | Record boundary known; field semantics unknown. |
| `ScriptDispatchOneEnemy` | `0x38` | all `bytesToShort` reads | shorts/ints stored at `#0x22`, `#0x26`, `#0x2a`, `#0x30`, `#0x38`, `#0x3e`, `#0x42`, `#0x46`, `#0x4a`, `#0x4e`, `#0x54`, `#0x5c` | Record boundary known; field semantics unknown. |

`Scenes/S_00.eex_new` roster sample:

- Boundary correction: raw `47 00` near offset `0x0055` is not accepted as a standalone parent without the native cursor. The stronger byte-boundary evidence is the deployment chain where each native payload length lands exactly on the next deployment parent or known script boundary.
- Chain evidence:
  - `0x0046@0x005d` + `2 + 0x410` = `0x046f`; first child actor/id words include `-1` defaults and late ids `958/956/957/955/954`.
  - `0x0046@0x046f` + `2 + 0x410` = `0x0881`.
  - `0x0047@0x0881` + `2 + 0x1180` = `0x1a03`, immediately before the next `ScriptChildInfo` player-deployment block.
- `0x0046@0x046f` child 0 hex (`0x34` bytes): `02 00 8a 02 26 00 01 00 04 00 03 00 00 00 04 00 0a 00 00 00 2b 00 03 00 3e 00 00 00 45 00 02 00 07 00 01 00 02 00 ff ff 04 00 00 00 00 00 04 00 00 00 00 00`.
- `0x0046@0x046f` first child words: `[2, 650, 38, 1, 4, 3, 0, 4, 10, 0, 43, 3, 62, 0, 69, 2, 7, 1, 2, -1, 4, 0, 0, 4, 0, 0]`.
- `0x0047@0x0881` child 0 hex (`0x38` bytes): `02 00 54 02 26 00 01 00 26 00 00 00 04 00 14 00 00 00 04 00 05 00 00 00 2b 00 02 00 3e 00 00 00 45 00 02 00 07 00 04 00 02 00 ff ff 04 00 0d 00 00 00 04 00 0b 00 00 00`.
- `0x0047@0x0881` first child words: `[2, 596, 38, 1, 38, 0, 4, 20, 0, 4, 5, 0, 43, 2, 62, 0, 69, 2, 7, 4, 2, -1, 4, 13, 0, 4, 11, 0]`.
- Interpretation: the chain proves useful parent boundaries and 16-bit child shape for this block. It still does not name every child field; numeric collisions with table ids are not enough.

Runtime deployment evidence:

| Native address | Instruction hex | Decoded instruction | Runtime meaning |
|---:|---|---|---|
| `0x007185f4` / `0x007185f6` | `22 22`; `9a 5e` | `movs r2,#0x22`; `ldrsh r2,[r3,r2]` | `ScriptDispatchFriend` reads child field `#0x22` and bounds-checks it against the actor count. |
| `0x007187fe` / `0x00718800` | `db 6a`; `23 82` | `ldr r3,[r3,#0x2c]`; `strh r3,[r4,#0x10]` | Friend child field `#0x2c` is written to `HistoryActor+0x10`. |
| `0x00718806` / `0x0071880a` | `5b 6b`; `63 82` | `ldr r3,[r3,#0x34]`; `strh r3,[r4,#0x12]` | Friend child field `#0x34` is written to `HistoryActor+0x12`. |
| `0x0067e8f4`-`0x0067e8f8` | `09 8a`; `5a 8a`; `ff f7 48 ff` | `ldrh r1,[actor,#0x10]`; `ldrh r2,[actor,#0x12]`; `bl History::CheckPos` | `HistoryActor+0x10/+0x12` are battle map x/y positions, not just copied data. |
| `0x00633738`-`0x00633742` | `01 8a`; `42 8a`; `53 f0 8f fb` | `ldrh r1,[actor,#0x10]`; `ldrh r2,[actor,#0x12]`; `bl HistoryActor::GenerateDefaultMove` | Default movement also consumes the same x/y fields. |
| `0x007187aa`-`0x007187b2` | `3e 21`; `...`; `70 f7 4d f8` | load child `#0x3e`; `bl HistoryActor::SetActorLv` | Friend child field `#0x3e` participates in actor level calculation. |
| `0x007189da` / `0x007189dc` | `22 23`; `d1 5e` | `movs r3,#0x22`; `ldrsh r1,[r2,r3]` | `ScriptDispatchEnemy` reads child field `#0x22` as the enemy actor id/index entry point. |
| `0x00718ad4` | `59 8d` | `ldrh r1,[r3,#0x2a]` | Enemy child field `#0x2a` is copied into a runtime actor slot before level setup; exact semantic name still needs cross-stage proof. |
| `0x00718b36` / `0x00718b3e` | `3e 22`; `71 f7 87 fe` | load child `#0x3e`; `bl HistoryActor::SetActorLv` | Enemy child field `#0x3e` participates in actor level calculation. |
| `0x00718c3e` | `60 33` | `adds r3,#0x60` | `ScriptDispatchEnemy` iterates embedded children at stride `0x60`. |

Player deployment evidence from `ScriptDispatchOwn::HandleScript@0x0071964d`:

| Native address | Instruction hex | Decoded instruction | Runtime meaning |
|---:|---|---|---|
| `0x00719666`-`0x0071966c` | `41 6a`; `1b 01`; `cb 18`; `43 62` | load `#0x24`, add scenario/list offset, store back to `#0x24` | Field `#0x24` is the selected own-force list index, adjusted by battle mode. |
| `0x00719686` / `0x00719688` | `83 8d`; `23 82` | `ldrh [script,#0x2c]`; `strh [actor,#0x10]` | `#0x2c` is player unit x coordinate. |
| `0x0071968a` / `0x0071968c` | `83 8e`; `63 82` | `ldrh [script,#0x34]`; `strh [actor,#0x12]` | `#0x34` is player unit y coordinate. |
| `0x0071968e` / `0x00719690` | `43 8f`; `a3 80` | `ldrh [script,#0x3a]`; `strh [actor,#4]` | `#0x3a` writes actor side/group slot; exact enum values need naming. |
| `0x00719692` / `0x00719696` | `c3 8f`; `23 81` | `ldrh [script,#0x3e]`; `strh [actor,#8]` | `#0x3e` writes another actor-side/config slot; exact enum values need naming. |
| `0x007196a4`-`0x007196d8` | `bl GetTotalHp`; `bl SetCurHpEx`; `bl GetTotalMp`; `bl SetCurMpEx`; `bl UpdateSkills` | runtime refresh after placement | The op mutates a real deployed actor, not display-only metadata. |

Own-force list evidence from `ScriptConfigOwnForce::HandleScript@0x00719125`:

- Calls `History::AddBattleOwn(short)` at `0x00719278`, `0x0071929a`, `0x007192be`, `0x007192e2`, `0x00719306`, and `0x007193be`.
- Therefore `0x004a / ScriptConfigOwnForce` is the selectable/forced own roster configuration path.
- It also calls `History::CalcBaseLevel@0x007193d6` or `History::SpecialCalcBaseLevel@0x007193dc` after populating the list.

`ScriptConfigOwnForce` field layout and runtime behavior:

| Native address | Instruction hex | Decoded instruction | Runtime meaning |
|---:|---|---|---|
| `0x0071941c`-`0x0071942c` | `26 f7 63 fe`; `a1 1c`; `68 62` | read short at payload `+0`, then int at payload `+2`, store int to `#0x24` | File shape begins with old tag `0x0004` and an int count/limit field. |
| `0x00719430`-`0x0071952e` | repeated `bytesToShort`, stores alternating tags and values through object `#0x4e` | reads 20 shorts after the int | The retained values are every second short: `#0x2a/#0x2e/#0x32/#0x36/#0x3a/#0x3e/#0x42/#0x46/#0x4a/#0x4e`. |
| `0x00719550`-`0x007195bc` | `ldrsh [#0x2a]`, `[#0x2e]`, ..., `[#0x4e]`; writer calls | `saveScript` writes `#0x24` plus the ten retained values | Confirms interleaved `0x38/0x39` words are legacy tags, not separate commands. |
| `0x00719126`-`0x00719244` | repeated load from `#0x2a..#0x4e`; store to `#0x50..#0x62` | normalize ten configured own actor selectors | Direct values `>= -1` are retained; values `<= -2` are remapped through `History* + (0x102e - selector) * 4` before use. |
| `0x0071925e`-`0x00719306` | five guarded calls to `History::AddBattleOwn` | add normalized `#0x50/#0x52/#0x54/#0x56/#0x58` when valid | First five configured values are forced/priority own roster entries. |
| `0x00719332`-`0x007193be` | compare current count against `#0x24`; compare candidate against `#0x50..#0x62`; call `AddBattleOwn` | auto-fill from the broader own list until the count/limit is reached, skipping all ten configured values | Last five configured values are not directly added; they act as exclusion/skip candidates in the auto-fill loop. |

Old EEX payload shape:

```text
00: 04 00                      old int tag
+02: <count-or-limit:u32>       stored at #0x24
+06: 38 00 <force0:s16>
+0a: 38 00 <force1:s16>
+0e: 38 00 <force2:s16>
+12: 38 00 <force3:s16>
+16: 38 00 <force4:s16>
+1a: 39 00 <skip0:s16>
+1e: 39 00 <skip1:s16>
+22: 39 00 <skip2:s16>
+26: 39 00 <skip3:s16>
+2a: 39 00 <skip4:s16>
```

Corpus evidence from a strict shape scan (`4a 00 04 00 <u32>`, five `38 00 <s16>` pairs, five `39 00 <s16>` pairs):

| Metric | Value | Evidence |
|---|---:|---|
| R files with strict `0x004a` | `0` | Raw `4a 00` collisions in R files fail the `04 + five 38 + five 39` payload shape. |
| S files with strict `0x004a` | `16` | `S_04`, `S_18`, `S_20`, `S_22`, `S_24`, `S_30`, `S_32`, `S_33`, `S_38`, `S_39`, `S_72`, `S_73`, `S_88`, `S_89`, `S_119`, `S_120`. |
| Strict `0x004a` records | `51` | All have fixed native payload `0x2e` and tag sequence `[0x38]*5 + [0x39]*5`. |
| Count/limit distribution | `5=17`, `8=8`, `3=8`, `6=6`, `1=3`, `2=3`, `10=2`, `15=2`, `9=2` | Parsed from payload int at `+0x02`. |
| Most common selector values | `-1=385`, `0=19`, `2=9`, `1=6`, `26=5` | `-1` is the empty sentinel; values `<= -2` are runtime-indirect selectors, not byte corruption. |

Negative selector remap evidence:

| Evidence | Offset / address | Hex / value | Decoded result |
|---|---:|---|---|
| Global `history` slot | GOT slot `0x011c6108` | `74 32 1e 01` | Relocated pointer to global object `history@0x011e3274`; `ScriptConfigOwnForce` loads this slot into `r5`, then loads `History*` from `[r5]`. |
| Remap constant | literal `0x007193ec` | `2e 10 00 00` | Constant `0x102e` used in every own-force negative-selector remap. |
| First own-force remap | `0x0071913a`-`0x00719142` | `ac 4b`; `9b 1a`; `2a 68`; `9b 00`; `d1 5a` | `idx = (0x102e - selector) << 2`; read `u16` from `History* + idx`; store normalized selector to `#0x50`. |
| Second own-force remap | `0x00719156`-`0x0071915e` | `a5 4a`; `52 1a`; `29 68`; `92 00`; `8a 5a` | Same formula for `#0x2e -> #0x52`; repeated for all ten `#0x2a..#0x4e` configured selectors. |
| Alias backing array clear | `History::InitHistory@0x006855b0`-`0x006855b8` | `7d 4b` -> literal `0x40c0`; `7d 4a` -> literal `0x9c3c`; `bl 0x007f00a0` | Clears `History+0x40c0` for `0x9c3c` bytes. This is `0x270f` int-sized slots. |
| Alias backing array save copy | `History::getHistory@0x00684ef0`-`0x00684ef8` | `27 4b` -> literal `0x40c0`; `17 4a` -> literal `0x270f`; `bl DArray<int>::copyFrom@0x0065d460` | Copies `0x270f` ints from `History+0x40c0` into a `DSaveHistory` int array at `DSaveHistory+0x124`. |
| Alias save parser read | `DHistoryParser::DSaveHistory::parseData@0x0065f568`-`0x0065f576` | `16 4b` -> literal `0x0434`; `f1 6a`; `b2 6a`; `e1 f7 3d fe` | After `r6 = DSaveHistory+0xfc`, save versions `> 0x0434` read a size-prefixed int array with `r1=[r6,#0x2c]=[DSaveHistory+0x128]` and `r2=[r6,#0x28]=[DSaveHistory+0x124]`. This is the persisted alias array storage. |
| Alias backing array restore | `History::ParseHistory@0x00686096`-`0x006860ac` | `38 1c`; `25 30`; `ff 30`; `aa 4b` -> literal `0x40c0`; `aa 4a` -> literal `0x270f`; `fb f7 23 fb` | Sets `r0 = DSaveHistory+0x124`, `r1 = History+0x40c0`, `r2 = 0x270f`, then calls `DArray<int>::copyTo@0x006816f6`. This restores the saved alias array into live `History`. |
| `ScriptValueOperation` op dispatch | `ScriptValueOperation::HandleScript@0x0070f066` | switch table `06 00 4e 00 96 00 ed 00 30 01 78 01` | Field `#0x2e` is the operation enum. Table targets decode as `0 -> add`, `1 -> subtract`, `2 -> assign`, `3 -> multiply`, `4 -> integer divide`, `5 -> integer modulo`. Divide calls imported `__aeabi_idiv`; modulo calls imported `__aeabi_idivmod` and stores returned `r1`. |
| Alias add writer | `ScriptValueOperation::HandleScript@0x0070f0f0`-`0x0070f0fe` | `b3 6a`; `9b 00`; `aa 4a` -> literal `0x40c0`; `99 58`; `08 18`; `98 50` | For `#0x2e=0` and `#0x22=2`, `#0x28` is an int slot index: `slotAddr = History + (#0x28 * 4) + 0x40c0`; this branch reads the current slot, adds `getNum2()`, and writes it back. |
| Alias subtract writer | `ScriptValueOperation::HandleScript@0x0070f17a`-`0x0070f18e` | `b3 6a`; `9b 00`; `86 4a` -> literal `0x40c0`; `99 58`; `08 1a`; `98 50` | For `#0x2e=1` and `#0x22=2`, writes `slot = slot - getNum2()` to `History+0x40c0 + #0x28*4`. |
| Alias assign writer | `ScriptValueOperation::HandleScript@0x0070f22e`-`0x0070f23c` | `ff f7 b5 fe`; `5c 4b` -> literal `0x1030`; `e4 18`; `a4 00`; `60 51` | For `#0x2e=2` and normal `#0x22=2`, writes `slot = getNum2()` to `History + (#0x28 + 0x1030) * 4`, equivalent to `History+0x40c0 + #0x28*4`. A special `#0x28 == 0x1396` branch updates `History+0x13f50` and is not used by the alias slot `51..64` records. |
| Alias multiply writer | `ScriptValueOperation::HandleScript@0x0070f2ae`-`0x0070f2c2` | `b3 6a`; `39 4a` -> literal `0x40c0`; `99 58`; `41 43`; `99 50` | For `#0x2e=3` and `#0x22=2`, writes `slot = slot * getNum2()`. |
| Alias divide writer | `ScriptValueOperation::HandleScript@0x0070f33a`-`0x0070f352` | `18 4d` -> literal `0x40c0`; `60 59`; `e0 f0 b7 fe`; `60 51` | For `#0x2e=4` and `#0x22=2`, calls the PLT veneer `0x007f00c0 -> 0x003f9b80`, which maps through `.rel.plt` entry `16` to `__aeabi_idiv`; stores quotient `r0`. |
| Alias modulo writer | `ScriptValueOperation::HandleScript@0x0070f3e6`-`0x0070f3fe` | `bd 4d` -> literal `0x40c0`; `60 59`; `e0 f0 2d ff`; `61 51` | For `#0x2e=5` and `#0x22=2`, calls the PLT veneer `0x007f0258 -> 0x003f9c4c`, which maps through `.rel.plt` entry `33` to `__aeabi_idivmod`; stores remainder `r1`. |
| `getNum2` RHS literal source | `ScriptValueOperation::getNum2@0x0070efa0`-`0x0070efbe` | switch table `03 05 0f 18 21 2f`; `c1 5e`; `83 6b`; case `0` target `0x0070efbe`: `18 1c`; `30 e0` | Field `#0x32` selects the RHS source. Case `#0x32=0` returns the raw int field `#0x38`. Cases `#0x32=1/2/3/5` read pointer/address namespaces under `History`; they are native-structural but not exercised by the current likely-record corpus scan. |
| `getNum2` RHS value-table source | `ScriptValueOperation::getNum2@0x0070effa`-`0x0070f014` | `0c 49` -> GOT offset; `0d 49` -> literal `0x13a1`; `0b 49` -> literal `0x1030`; `98 58` | Case `#0x32=4` normally returns `*(History + (#0x38 + 0x1030) * 4)`, equivalent to reading `History+0x40c0 + #0x38*4`. Special `#0x38 == 0x13a1` reads a short from `History+0x13f5a`. |
| `0x0077` corpus distribution | broad raw scan of `Scenes/*.eex_new` with stable tag shape `#0x20=81`, `#0x24=4`, `#0x2c=83`, `#0x30=82`, `#0x34=4` | `36,998` likely records; `#0x22=2` in all; op counts `#0x2e`: assign `30,614`, add `6,208`, subtract `64`, divide `62`, modulo `45`, multiply `5`; RHS counts `#0x32`: literal `36,658`, value-table read `340` | In this package, `ScriptValueOperation` is overwhelmingly an integer history/value-table operation. No likely records with RHS selectors `#0x32=1/2/3/5` were observed by this scan, so those remain structurally decoded from native code but corpus-unexercised here. |
| Alias table clear loop | `ScriptValueOperation::HandleScript@0x0070f6a2`-`0x0070f6d8` | `10 4b` -> literal `0x40c0`; `21 4a` -> literal `0x270f`; `14 60`; loop to `0x0070f6ae` | Iterates over the `History+0x40c0` int-slot table and writes zero to selected slots while skipping native-reserved ranges. This proves `ScriptValueOperation` can mutate the same live alias/value table outside save/load. |
| `ScriptArmyChange` alias consumer | `0x0071672e`-`0x00716748` / `0x007167f2`-`0x007167f8` | `41 8c ... 9b 1a 2a 68 9b 00 d1 5a`; `d1 4a`; `52 1a`; `92 00`; `82 5a` | Both `HandleRScript` and battle `HandleScript` normalize negative actor selectors through the same `History* + (0x102e - selector) * 4` formula. Current `0x003b` corpus has no negative selector values, but the consumer path is native-proven. |
| `ScriptArmyChange` R roster branches | `0x0071674a`-`0x007167a4` | `e3 8c a1 85 00 2b ... 6a f7 55 fb ... 2a 22`; `2a 22 a3 5e ... 6a f7 2b fe` | R-side `#0x26=0` calls `History::ArmyCome(actor, #0x2a, false)`. `#0x26=1` either calls `History::ArmyComeReturnToLeave(actor)` when the current army count plus one equals `#0x2a`, or calls `History::ArmyCome(actor, 0, true)`. Other values, including observed `255`, call `History::ArmyLeave(actor, #0x2a != 1)`. |
| `ScriptArmyChange` battle state-byte branches | `0x00716800`-`0x0071680e`; stores at `0x007169e4`, `0x00716baa`, `0x00716d8a` | branch `26 25 55 5f 01 2d 55 d0 ff 2d 00 d1 8a e0 00 2d`; state stores `89 30 07 70 ... 8a 30 07 70 ... c8 80`, `89 36 30 70 ... 8a 36 30 70 ... c8 80`, `02 26 ... 89 30 06 70 ... 8a 30 06 70 ... c8 80` | Battle-side `#0x26` branches on `0`, `1`, and `255`. The branch bodies move actor pointers between internal lists, write `HistoryActor+0x89` and `+0x8a` to `0`, `1`, or `2` respectively, and set actor field `+6` to `1`. |
| Reused actor-selector mechanism | selected `0x102e` literal xrefs | `ScriptActorMove`, `ScriptActorDisappear`, `ScriptTestActorState`, `ScriptDispatchEnemy`, `ScriptArmyChange`, `ScriptValueIntValuation`, `ScriptBattleActorAction`, `ScriptBattleActorRelive`, `ScriptRelaReviveOrMove` | The same `0x102e - selector` table is not private to `0x004a`; it is the native script actor-selector alias table. Several non-own handlers guard on `selector + 2`, so `-2` is likely a separate special selector there. |

The formula can be rewritten as an array index:

```text
byteOffset = (0x102e - selector) * 4
           = 0x40c0 + ((-selector) - 2) * 4
aliasIndex = (-selector) - 2
```

For example, selector `-53` is alias index `51` and reads `History+0x418c`; selector `-66` is alias index `64` and reads `History+0x41c0`. `ScriptConfigOwnForce` reads the low 16 bits from each int-sized slot (`ldrh`), so the array is stored/copied as int-sized slots but this handler consumes a short actor id.

`S_71` and `S_118` each contain `15` consecutive `0x0077` records spaced by `0x1a` bytes (`cmd` + fixed `0x18` payload), assigning literal `2000` to alias slots `50..64`. The observed `0x004a` negative own selectors consume the subset `51..64` through selector values `-53..-66` in `S_72/S_73/S_119/S_120`; no `0x004a` consumer for slot `50` is proven yet. A full `Scenes/*.eex_new` raw scan for selector `-52` (`cc ff`) returned `0` hits, so slot `50` currently has no direct script-selector consumer evidence.

Surrounding text evidence:

| File / offset | Hex | UTF-8 decoded result | Boundary interpretation |
|---|---|---|---|
| `S_71.eex_new@0x4ae8` | `e5 87 ba e6 88 98 e4 ba ba e5 91 98` | `出战人员` | Immediately precedes the slot `50..64` assignment run at `0x4af7..0x4c63`. Nearby dialogue speakers include Zhang Fei, Liu Bei, and Guan Yu, so this block is roster/list related, but per-slot names are not proven. |
| `S_118.eex_new@0x6103` | `e5 87 ba e6 88 98 e4 ba ba e5 91 98` | `出战人员` | Immediately precedes the slot `50..64` assignment run at `0x6112..0x627e`. Nearby dialogue is the later Ye battle context; this confirms the assignment block recurs in a battle roster/list section, not a random arithmetic blob. |

Interpretation: own-force low ids are now structurally separated from deployment coordinates. `0x004a` selects or constrains which own actors enter the battle list; `0x004b` then places selected own actors by list index and coordinates. Negative own selectors are not byte loss and no longer point to an unknown global blob: they are entries in a persisted and script-mutated `History+0x40c0` int-slot alias array. The observed `0x004a` negative values use alias indices `51..64`, read at `History+0x418c..0x41c0`. The save/load round-trip path, live arithmetic writer, op enum, and literal RHS source for the observed alias-slot assignments are now located; the remaining unresolved part is how to name the route/party semantics of those slots and how to label non-literal RHS namespaces.

Battle leave evidence from `ScriptBattleActorLeave::HandleScript@0x0071bbcd`:

- `0x0071bbe2` (`22 21`) reads field `#0x22` to choose between a prebuilt actor list and direct field `#0x26`.
- `0x0071bc24` (`19 f7 6e fe`) calls `BattleControler::getBattleActor`.
- `0x0071bc3c` (`17 f7 84 fd`) calls `BattleActor::setState`; field `#0x4e` chooses state `0x0e` vs `0x10`.
- Status: action-side leave/retreat op is structurally decoded, but actor-list source and state enum names are still not complete.

Battle action records `0x004f`, `0x0050`, and `0x0053` are now byte-shaped enough to separate actor selectors, state/direction fields, timing fields, and direct-vs-area leave mode. The scan below used only `Scenes/S_*.eex_new` and required the native tag layout at fixed word positions; raw `50 00` / `53 00` byte hits that did not match these layouts were rejected as payload collisions.

Native field and runtime evidence:

| Cmd | Native address | Instruction hex | Decoded instruction | Proven meaning |
|---:|---:|---|---|---|
| `0x004f` | `0x0071b510` | `68 84` | `strh r0, [r5,#0x22]` | Payload word at file `+0x02` becomes actor selector `#0x22`. |
| `0x004f` | `0x0071b524` | `e8 84` | `strh r0, [r5,#0x26]` | Payload word at file `+0x06` becomes target/second actor selector `#0x26`. |
| `0x004f` | `0x0071b53c` | `68 85` | `strh r0, [r5,#0x2a]` | Payload word at file `+0x0a` becomes fallback direction `#0x2a`. |
| `0x004f` | `0x0071b56a`-`0x0071b572` | `03 27`; `78 43`; `68 86` | `movs r7,#3`; `muls r0,r7,r0`; `strh r0,[r5,#0x32]` | File word at `+0x12` is multiplied by `3` before becoming timing field `#0x32`. |
| `0x004f` | `0x0071b586`-`0x0071b588` | `78 43`; `e8 86` | `muls r0,r7,r0`; `strh r0,[r5,#0x36]` | File word at `+0x16` is multiplied by `3` before becoming timing/focus field `#0x36`. |
| `0x004f` | `0x0071b45e`-`0x0071b466` | `1e 8a`; `0d 8a`; `4a 8a`; `5b 8a` | load x/y from two actors | If target actor is valid, facing is computed from actor coordinates, not from the fallback direction byte. |
| `0x004f` | `0x0071b4c4`-`0x0071b4ca` | `63 8d`; `03 2b`; `8b 80` | load `#0x2a`; compare to `3`; store actor direction | If target actor is invalid, `#0x2a <= 3` is used as a fallback direction. |
| `0x0050` | `0x0071b720` | `68 84` | `strh r0, [r5,#0x22]` | Payload word at file `+0x02` becomes actor selector `#0x22`. |
| `0x0050` | `0x0071b734` | `e8 84` | `strh r0, [r5,#0x26]` | Payload word at file `+0x06` becomes state/action enum `#0x26`. |
| `0x0050` | `0x0071b74a`-`0x0071b752` | `03 23`; `58 43`; `68 85` | `movs r3,#3`; `muls r0,r3,r0`; `strh r0,[r5,#0x2a]` | File word at `+0x0a` is multiplied by `3` before becoming start delay `#0x2a`. |
| `0x0050` | `0x0071b644`-`0x0071b658` plus literals `0x0071b6e0` / `0x0071b6e8` | `26 4b`; `98 42`; `1a 68`; `25 4b`; `d3 58`; `18 88`; literals `03 04 00 00`, `8c 44 01 00` | compare actor selector to `0x0403`; if equal, load `History+0x1448c`, then read that actor pointer's first halfword | Selector `0x0403` is a native-supported active-actor cursor selector in this handler. Current package has `0` strict `0x0050` records using `#0x22=0x0403`; this is native-only evidence here. |
| `0x0050` | `0x0071b6a4`-`0x0071b6aa` | `26 23`; `e1 5e`; `18 f7 4b f8` | load `#0x26`; call `BattleActor::setState` | The state/action field drives `BattleActor::setState(#0x26)`. |
| `0x0050` | `0x0071b6b2`-`0x0071b6b8` | `2e 22`; `a3 5e`; `30 18`; `c0 18` | load `#0x2e`; add setState return and delay | `#0x2e` is an extra wait/tail timing value, not an actor id. |
| `0x0053` | `0x0071b98e` / `0x0071b9a2` | `68 84`; `e8 84` | store `#0x22`; store `#0x26` | File words at `+0x02/+0x06` become mode `#0x22` and direct actor/id `#0x26`. |
| `0x0053` | `0x0071b9ba`, `0x0071b9d2`, `0x0071b9ea`, `0x0071ba04` | `e8 62`; `68 63`; `e8 63`; `68 64` | store ints `#0x2c/#0x34/#0x3c/#0x44` | Four int fields form the rectangle iterated by `getActorList`. |
| `0x0053` | `0x0071ba22` / `0x0071ba40` | `18 80`; `28 80` | store `#0x4a`; store `#0x4e` | `#0x4a` is actor-list side/filter selector; `#0x4e` chooses the leave state. |
| `0x0053` | `0x0071bbe2`-`0x0071bbf6` | `22 21`; `43 5e`; `00 2b`; `ff f7 89 ff` | read `#0x22`; direct path or call `getActorList` | `#0x22 <= 0` uses direct actor `#0x26`; `#0x22 > 0` builds an area actor list. |
| `0x0053` | `0x0071bb10`-`0x0071bb2c` | `45 6b`; `63 6c`; `e6 6a`; `e3 6b`; `62 f7 38 fa` | iterate y/x rectangle and call `FindActorPosition` | Area mode scans map positions `x1..x2`, `y1..y2`. |
| `0x0053` | `0x0071bc30`-`0x0071bc3c` | `9b 5e`; `10 21`; `0e 21`; `17 f7 84 fd` | read `#0x4e`; call `setState` with `0x10` or `0x0e` | `#0x4e == 0` maps to state `0x0e`; nonzero maps to state `0x10`. |

Battle actor id namespace probe:

This pass compared deployment parent chains against strict battle action records. The scanner was a temporary read-only probe; it is evidence for the ledger, not a submitted parser. The important guardrail is that raw `46 00` cannot be trusted alone, because `0x0046` also appears as a retained old-field value inside other payloads. A deployment candidate was counted only when its native payload length landed on the next candidate parent or a known script boundary.

| Probe | Result | Evidence / caveat |
|---|---:|---|
| Chained `0x0046` parents | `203` | Native length `2 + 0x410`; accepted only when the end offset chained to another candidate or known boundary. |
| Chained `0x0047` parents | `204` | Native length `2 + 0x1180`; accepted by the same boundary rule. |
| Non-negative child actor/id entries in chained parents | `9668` | Reads child payload `+2` into object `#0x22`; not tag/value parsing. |
| Strict battle action records scanned | `16917` | `0x004f`, `0x0050`, `0x0053` shapes from the native field table above. |
| Direct action actor refs (`0 <= id < 0x0400`) | `20578` | Includes `0x004f` actor/target, `0x0050` actor, and direct-mode `0x0053` actor. |
| Direct refs found in same-file chained `0x0046/0x0047` roster ids | `12746 / 20578` (`61.9%`) | Overall denominator includes low own-force ids such as `0/1/2`. |
| Direct refs with id `>= 32` found in same-file chained roster ids | `12372 / 13796` (`89.7%`) | Stronger enemy/friend signal after avoiding likely own-force low slots. |

Representative cross-checks:

| File / offset | Hex | Decoded relation | Status |
|---|---|---|---|
| `S_00.eex_new@0x046f` | `46 00 02 00 8a 02 26 00 01 00 04 00 03 00 00 00 ...` | `0x0046` child 0 stores `#0x22=650`; same parent list also includes `651/310/309/654/655/181/953`. | Chained parent boundary. |
| `S_00.eex_new@0x044a2` | `50 00 02 00 8b 02 46 00 08 00 26 00 01 00 26 00 01 00` | `0x0050` actor `651`, state `8`; actor `651` is present in `0x0046@0x046f`. | Same battle-actor namespace, high confidence. |
| `S_00.eex_new@0x0881` | `47 00 02 00 54 02 26 00 01 00 26 00 00 00 ...` | `0x0047` child 0 stores `#0x22=596`; same parent list includes `226` and `225`. | Chained parent boundary. |
| `S_00.eex_new@0x4274` | `4f 00 02 00 e2 00 02 00 e1 00 2b 00 ff ff 26 00 00 00 26 00 01 00 26 00 01 00` | `0x004f` actor `226`, target `225`; both appear in `0x0047@0x0881`. | Same battle-actor namespace, high confidence. |
| `S_1010.eex_new@0x0463` | `47 00 02 00 89 00 26 00 ff ff 26 00 ff ff 04 00 0b 00 00 00 ...` | `0x0047` child 0 stores `#0x22=137`; same list includes `214/260/262`. | Chained parent boundary. |
| `S_1010.eex_new@0x1d26` | `4f 00 02 00 04 01 02 00 d6 00 2b 00 ff ff 26 00 00 00 26 00 01 00 26 00 00 00` | `0x004f` actor `260`, target `214`; both appear in `0x0047@0x0463`. | Same battle-actor namespace, high confidence. |

Interpretation: action-side actor fields are battle-actor ids, not global `dic_hero.hid`. `0x0046/0x0047` child `#0x22` and `0x004f/0x0050/0x0053` direct actor fields share that namespace for enemy/friend actors. Player-side ids remain less direct: `0x004b #0x24` is a selectable own-force list index adjusted by `ScriptConfigOwnForce`, so low action ids such as `0/1/2` must not be silently equated with `0x004b` slot numbers.

`BattleActor::setState(int)@0x00633748` is the runtime state machine behind `0x0050 ScriptBattleActorAction`, `0x0053 ScriptBattleActorLeave`, and several non-script battle paths. It writes the state byte to the runtime actor at `HistoryActor+0xe0`, normalizes `-1` / `0xff` back to `0`, clears runtime animation fields, and returns a wait/duration value consumed by callers such as `ScriptBattleActorAction` (`#0x18 = delay + setState_return + tail`) and `ScriptBattleActorLeave` (`#0x18 = setState_return`).

Native `setState` evidence:

| Native address | Instruction hex | Decoded instruction | Runtime meaning |
|---:|---|---|---|
| `0x00633752`-`0x0063375e` | `e0 32`; `13 78`; `0e 3b`; `02 2b`; `c0 e0` | load byte at actor `+0xe0`; if current state is `14..16`, return `0` | Existing terminal/leave-like states block state replacement. |
| `0x00633760`-`0x00633772` | `0e 3b`; `02 2b`; `d1 23`; `db 00`; `c3 58`; `01 2b`; `b6 e0` | if requested state is `14..16` and actor flag at `0xd1 << 3` is `1`, return `0` | Leave-like state requests have an additional runtime guard. |
| `0x00633778`-`0x00633784` | `11 70`; `ff 29`; `13 70` | store requested state byte; if byte is `0xff`, write `0` | Script state `-1` normalizes to state `0`. |
| `0x00633786`-`0x0063378e` | `13 81`; `6b 60`; `ab 60`; `eb 60` | clear actor short `+8` and BattleActor fields `+4/+8/+0xc` | State change resets animation/action scratch fields. |
| `0x006337a4`-`0x006337ac` | `05 38`; `16 28`; `bc f1 02 fd` | switch on `state - 5`, range `0..22`; call Thumb jump helper | States `5..27` use inline jump table at `0x006337b0`. |
| `0x006337b0` | `97 26 0c 31 0e 1a 33 3d 48 97 97 95 99 97 99 97 97 97 97 99 99 99 8a` | jump-table bytes | Each byte maps to `target = 0x006337b0 + byte * 2`. |

`0x0050` state-context probe:

This temporary read-only corpus probe used strict `0x004f`, `0x0050`, `0x0053`, and zero-payload `0x0051` shapes to look at neighboring battle-action records. It does not name animation states by guesswork; it only proves that the script corpus exercises a closed numeric state set and that repeated choreography patterns can be preserved numerically.

| State arg | `0x0050` count | Native wait evidence | Representative context evidence | Current status |
|---:|---:|---|---|---|
| `-1` | `6` | normalized to state `0`, return `0` | `S_01@0x32fef` hex `50 00 02 00 dd 00 46 00 ff ff 26 00 00 00 26 00 01 00`; context follows actor `221` states `8,9`, then turns actor `222`. | Reset/no-op numeric state; no human label. |
| `0` | `1062` | return `0` | `S_00@0x458d` hex `50 00 02 00 e2 00 46 00 00 00 26 00 00 00 26 00 01 00`; in the same chain after actor `226` state `6`, before actor `651` state `3/0`. | Common zero-wait state; likely reset/idle-like but label unproven. |
| `1` | `733` | return `0` | `S_00@0x2597a` hex `50 00 02 00 01 00 46 00 01 00 26 00 01 00 26 00 01 00`; preceded by turn records actor `1`/`225`, followed by actor `0` state `6/0`. | Numeric action state; label unproven. |
| `2` | `698` | return `0` | `S_00@0x241fe` hex `50 00 02 00 01 00 46 00 02 00 26 00 01 00 26 00 00 00`; surrounded by mutual turn records involving actor `1` and `309`. | Numeric action state; label unproven. |
| `3` | `294` | return `0` | `S_00@0x45b3` hex `50 00 02 00 8b 02 46 00 03 00 26 00 01 00 26 00 00 00`; appears in the same local chain as actor `226` states `7/6/0` and actor `651` states `8/3/0`. | Numeric action state; label unproven. |

| `9` | `1236` | return `48` or `40` depending on runtime flag | `S_00@0x50ff` hex `50 00 02 00 b5 00 46 00 09 00 26 00 01 00 26 00 01 00`; often appears after state `6/0` or around `0x0051` separators. | Common timed state; label unproven. |
| `10` | `284` | return `48` or `8` depending on runtime flag | `S_00@0x49ad` hex `50 00 02 00 54 02 46 00 0a 00 26 00 01 00 26 00 01 00`; often paired with state `7/8` chains. | Timed state; label unproven. |

| `12` | `50` | return `48` or `45` depending on runtime flag | `S_01@0x34f9c` hex `50 00 02 00 dd 00 46 00 0c 00 26 00 00 00 26 00 01 00`; followed by actor `221` states `1/0`. | Rare timed state; label unproven. |

Interpretation: battle action state bytes are recoverable as numeric enum values. A converter can fail closed on unmapped state numbers and can map some runtime contexts (`13` movement, `15` disappear, `20` get item, `14/16` leave variants) with evidence. It still cannot safely invent human animation names for `0..12` without more visual/runtime correlation.

`ScriptBattleActorLeave::getActorList` selector behavior is separable and mostly labeled for side bytes `0..2`. Native dispatch code writes `HistoryActor+0x89` as `0` for own actors, `1` for friend actors, and `2` for enemy-side actors; enemy-side actors are further split by `HistoryActor+0x668` (`0` enemy, `1` assist). Side byte `4` is accepted by one native branch. Its script-side source is now partly proven: `ScriptValueIntValuation::valuation2` can reclassify matching actors into side byte `4`, but the human label for that class is still not proven.

`getActorList` side/filter evidence:

| Selector / field | Native evidence | Corpus evidence | Current interpretation |
|---:|---|---|---|
| side byte `0` | `ScriptDispatchOwn::HandleScript@0x007196ca`-`0x007196d0`: `88 33`; `1d 70`; `5d 70` writes zero through `r5` to actor `+0x88/+0x89`. `getActorList` selector `0` reaches `0x0071bb4c` and compares loaded `+0x89` against `0` at `0x0071bb6c`. | Native-supported selector; no `0x0053` area-mode hit for selector `0` in this package. | own side byte. |
| side byte `1` | `ScriptDispatchFriend::HandleScript@0x007186d8`-`0x007186e0`: `01 22`; `89 33`; `1a 70`; `5a 70` writes `1` to actor `+0x89/+0x8a`. `getActorList` selector `1` reaches `0x0071bb54` and compares loaded `+0x89` against `1` at `0x0071bb82`. | Native-supported selector; no `0x0053` area-mode hit for selector `1` in this package. | friend side byte. |
| side byte `2` | `ScriptDispatchEnemy::HandleScript@0x00718be4`-`0x00718bea`: `02 23`; `89 32`; `13 70`; `53 70` writes `2` to actor `+0x89/+0x8a`. `getActorList` selector `5` reaches `0x0071bb94` and accepts `+0x89 == 2`. | `0x0053` area mode selector `5` has `13` hits, e.g. `S_11.eex_new@0x2268d` hex `53 00 2c 00 01 00 02 00 ff ff 04 00 00 00 00 00 04 00 00 00 00 00 04 00 17 00 00 00 04 00 13 00 00 00 03 00 05 00 26 00 00 00`. | enemy+assist side byte. |
| secondary field `0` | `getActorList` selector `2` reaches `0x0071bb5c`-`0x0071bb6c`: `89 32`; `12 78`; `02 2a`; `cd 22`; `d2 00`; `9a 5e`; `00 2a`, requiring side byte `2` and `HistoryActor+0x668 == 0`. `History::getBattleEnemyNum@0x0067e9b2`-`0x0067e9b8` reads the same `+0x668` field and counts the zero case. | `0x0053` area mode selector `2` has `18` hits, e.g. `S_04.eex_new@0x27b23` hex `53 00 2c 00 01 00 02 00 ff ff 04 00 00 00 00 00 04 00 00 00 00 00 04 00 13 00 00 00 04 00 07 00 00 00 03 00 02 00 26 00 00 00`. | enemy subset of side byte `2`. |
| secondary field `1` | `getActorList` selector `3` reaches `0x0071bb72`-`0x0071bb82`: `89 32`; `12 78`; `02 2a`; `cd 22`; `d2 00`; `9a 5e`; `01 2a`, requiring side byte `2` and `HistoryActor+0x668 == 1`. `History::getBattleAssistNum@0x0067e9f2`-`0x0067e9f8` reads the same field and counts the one case. | Native-supported selector; no `0x0053` area-mode hit for selector `3` in this package. | assist subset of side byte `2`. |
| selector `4` | `getActorList@0x0071bb88`-`0x0071bb90`: load `+0x89`, compare `1`, branch on higher. | Native-supported selector; no `0x0053` area-mode hit for selector `4` in this package. | own+friend combined. |
| selector `6` | Switch table byte `0x33` maps selector `6` directly to accept path `0x0071bbaa` without side-byte comparison. | `0x0053` area mode selector `6` has `73` hits, e.g. `S_109.eex_new@0x238ff` hex `53 00 2c 00 01 00 02 00 39 00 04 00 00 00 00 00 04 00 00 00 00 00 04 00 23 00 00 00 04 00 11 00 00 00 03 00 06 00 26 00 00 00`. | any actor found in the rectangle. |
| selector `7` / side byte `4` | `getActorList@0x0071bba0`-`0x0071bba8`: load `+0x89`, compare `4`, reject on mismatch. `ScriptValueIntValuation::valuation2` has native write paths to `+0x89 = 4` (see below). | Native-supported selector; no `0x0053` area-mode hit for selector `7` in this package. | side-byte-4 class; source path partly proven, human label still unproven. |

`ScriptValueIntValuation` side-byte reclassification evidence:

| Evidence item | Value |
|---|---|
| Field shape | `ScriptValueIntValuation::initPara@0x0070fac7` reads payload as `#0x20 short`, `#0x24 int`, `#0x28 short`, `#0x2a short`, `#0x2c short`, `#0x2e short`, `#0x30 short`, `#0x32 short`; `saveScript@0x0070fb2f` preserves only `#0x24`, `#0x2a`, `#0x2e`, `#0x32`. |
| `valuation2` entry | `ScriptValueIntValuation::HandleScript@0x0071098e`-`0x00710998`: when `#0x2a != 0`, it calls `valuation2@0x00710241`. |
| Outer switch | `valuation2@0x00710262`-`0x0071026a` reads `#0x32`; the halfword switch table at `0x0071026e` maps `#0x32=32` to target `0x0071068c`. |
| Runtime classifier | `0x00710696`; `0x00710714`; `0x00710788`; `0x007107fe` compare a resolved runtime value against `7`, `8`, `9`, and `10`. This value is loaded from the runtime history/value table, not directly from the command byte. |
| Classifier `7` | `0x007106ce`-`0x007106e0`: `00 27`; `89 34`; `27 70`; `8a 34`; `27 70`, then `0x007106ea`-`0x007106ec`: `01 25`; `e5 80` | Reclassifies the matching actor to `+0x89 = 0`, `+0x8a = 0`, and actor field `+6 = 1`. |
| Classifier `8` | `0x0071074c`-`0x0071075c`: `01 27`; `89 34`; `27 70`; `02 25`; `e5 80` | Reclassifies the matching actor to `+0x89 = 1` and actor field `+6 = 2`. |
| Classifier `9` | `0x007107ca`-`0x007107da`: `04 24`; `89 33`; `1c 70`; `00 24`; `dc 80` | Reclassifies the matching actor to `+0x89 = 4` and actor field `+6 = 0`. |
| Classifier `10` | `0x00710842`-`0x00710852`: `04 24`; `89 33`; `1c 70`; `00 24`; `dc 80` | Same side-byte-4 reclassification as classifier `9`. |
| Corpus support | Canonical `0x0078` records (`04` / `0x54` / `02` / `0x55` tags) count `15054` in `269` files. Records with `#0x2a=1` and `#0x32=32`, which enter `valuation2` side-reclassification path, count `296` in `35` files. Sample: `S_00.eex_new@0x26d7b` hex `78 00 04 00 00 00 00 00 54 00 01 00 02 00 b5 00 55 00 20 00`. |

Status: side byte `4` is no longer source-opaque. It is a native-supported, script-writable runtime classification reached through `ScriptValueIntValuation::valuation2` and a resolved classifier value `9/10`. It is still not safe to assign a human faction label, and this package does not exercise `0x0053` area selector `7`.

### 4.8.1 Scripted Actor Movement: `0x0032 ScriptActorMove`

`ScriptActorMove::initPara` proves a fixed 30-byte payload after the `0x0032` command. It is a numeric movement/update record, not a text record; no `0x0005` string field occurs in this shape.

| File bytes after `32 00` | Native field | Decode result | Evidence |
|---|---:|---|---|
| `40 00 <mode:s16>` | `#0x20` tag, `#0x22` mode | source/mode selector | `initPara@0x00714c54`-`0x00714c64` stores first tag then mode. |
| `02 00 <actor:s16>` | `#0x24` tag, `#0x26` actor/direct selector | direct actor id / selector candidate | `initPara@0x00714c68`-`0x00714c78`; direct-mode `HandleScript` reads `#0x26`. |
| `04 00 <listIndex:i32>` | `#0x28` tag, `#0x2c` list index/int | list source index when mode `> 0` | `initPara@0x00714c7e`-`0x00714c90`; list path reads `#0x2c`. |
| `04 00 <x:s16> 00 00` | `#0x30` tag, `#0x34` target x | target x coordinate | `initPara@0x00714c96`-`0x00714ca8`; `HandleScript@0x00714b9a` loads `#0x34`. |
| `04 00 <y:s16> 00 00` | `#0x38` tag, `#0x3c` target y | target y coordinate | `initPara@0x00714cae`-`0x00714cc0`; `HandleScript@0x00714b9e` loads `#0x3c`. |
| `2b 00 <direction:s16>` | `#0x40` tag, `#0x42` direction/facing | numeric direction/facing field | `initPara@0x00714cc6`-`0x00714cda`; `saveScript@0x00714d22`-`0x00714d26` preserves `#0x42`. |

Native handler evidence:

| Native address | Hex | Decode result | Interpretation |
|---:|---|---|---|
| `ScriptActorMove::initPara@0x00714cdc`-`0x00714ce0` | `20 1c`; `1e 30`; `70 bd` | returns `payload + 0x1e` | Fixed file payload length is `30` bytes. |
| `ScriptActorMove::saveScript@0x00714cf2`-`0x00714d26` | `22 23`; `e1 5e` ... `26 23`; `e1 5e` ... `e1 6a` ... `61 6b` ... `a1 6b` ... `3e 23`; `e1 5e` | writes semantic fields `#0x22`, `#0x26`, `#0x2c`, `#0x34`, `#0x3c`, `#0x42` | Tags `#0x20/#0x24/#0x28/#0x30/#0x38/#0x40` are retained parse tags, not saved semantic values. |
| `HandleScript@0x00714b26`-`0x00714b2c` | `22 22`; `83 5e`; `00 2b`; `1d dc` | read `#0x22`; branch if mode `> 0` | mode `> 0` enters list-index source path; mode `<= 0` enters direct actor/selector path. |
| `HandleScript@0x00714b3c`-`0x00714b52` | `26 23`; `c1 5e`; `8b 1c`; `39 4b`; `5b 1a`; `9b 00`; `9b 58`; `38 4a`; `93 42`; `c3 84` | read `#0x26`, normalize some negative selectors through the `0x102e - selector` table unless the resolved value is `2000` | Direct actor path reuses the proven actor-selector alias mechanism. |
| `HandleScript@0x00714b6a`-`0x00714b86` | reads `#0x2c`, checks `0 <= index < listCount`, loads actor id from list[index] | mode `> 0` path | List-index actor source is native-proven; the human name of that list is not yet proven. |
| `HandleScript@0x00714b88`-`0x00714b98` | `20 f7 b4 fe`; null/dead checks | actor id lookup, reject missing or inactive/dead actor | Movement target actor is resolved before any x/y move. |
| `HandleScript@0x00714b9a`-`0x00714ba4` | `61 6b`; `e2 6b`; compares with actor `+0x10/+0x12` | read target x/y and compare to current actor coordinates | x/y are movement target coordinates. |
| `HandleScript@0x00714baa`-`0x00714bd2` | `6b f7 b1 f9`; then `61 63`; `e2 63` | call native helper with x/y pointers, then write possibly normalized x/y back to `#0x34/#0x3c` | Target coordinates may be adjusted before movement; preserve post-helper numeric fields if replaying native behavior. |
| `HandleScript@0x00714bdc`-`0x00714bea` | `30 1c`; `1e f7 9b fd`; `0d 21`; `1e f7 a7 fd`; `a0 61` | call `BattleActor::GenerateDefaultMove(targetX,targetY)`, then `BattleActor::setState(13)`, store wait/return in `#0x18` | Battle-side effect is scripted movement/path animation state `13`. |
| `HandleScript@0x00714bf4` | `28 f7 6d f8` | call `BattleReplay::setScriptToSave` | Scripted movement participates in replay/save context. |
| `HandleRScript@0x00714d92`-`0x00714dac`; `0x00714f54`-`0x00714f58` | mode/list branch; `04 35`; `eb 8f`; `e3 80` | R-side map actor update path; writes `#0x42` to an actor/list-object facing field | R-side also consumes this record shape for map-scene actor movement/update. Direction values remain numeric labels only. |

Corpus shape scan over `Scenes/*.eex_new` using exact tag sequence `32 00 40 00 <mode> 02 00 <actor> 04 00 <listIndex:i32> 04 00 <x> 00 00 04 00 <y> 00 00 2b 00 <direction>`:

|---|---:|
| Strict records | `5551` |
| Files | `209` |
| Prefix split | `R=3535`, `S=2016` |
| Mode split | mode `0=4961`, mode `-1=432`, mode `1=158` |
| R mode split | mode `0=3103`, mode `-1=432` |
| S mode split | mode `0=1858`, mode `1=158` |
| Direction/facing values | `2=1468`, `0=1416`, `1=1363`, `3=1288`, `-1=16` |
| Coordinate ranges | mode `-1`: x `6..96`, y `7..99`; mode `0`: x `0..99`, y `0..100`; mode `1`: x `0..30`, y `0..33` |

Representative byte evidence:

| Sample | Hex | Decoded fields | Status |
|---|---|---|---|
| `Scenes/R_00.eex_new@0x28e31` | `32 00 40 00 00 00 02 00 36 01 04 00 00 00 00 00 04 00 3a 00 00 00 04 00 2a 00 00 00 2b 00 02 00` | mode `0`, actor/direct selector `310`, list index `0`, target `(58,42)`, direction `2` | Direct-mode move/update record. |

Status: `0x0032` is not movement-opaque anymore. It can be preserved as a fail-closed numeric movement op with source mode, actor/direct selector or list index, target x/y, and direction/facing value. Do not assign human labels to mode `-1/0/1` or direction `0..3/-1` until visual/runtime correlation proves them.

### 4.8.2 Battle Relive / Re-entry: `0x0055` and `0x006d`

`0x0055 ScriptBattleActorRelive` is the absolute-position relive/re-entry form. Its file shape is the same 30-byte tag skeleton as `0x0032`, but the handler only accepts actors that are dead/inactive or in leave states, then clears/reinitializes them and places them on the map.

`0x0055 ScriptBattleActorRelive` field shape:

| File bytes after `55 00` | Native field | Decode result | Evidence |
|---|---:|---|---|
| `40 00 <mode:s16>` | `#0x24` tag, `#0x26` mode | source mode selector | `initPara@0x0071bdf0`-`0x0071be00`; `HandleScript@0x0071bcd0`-`0x0071bcda` reads `#0x26` and branches on `> 0`. |
| `02 00 <actor:s16>` | `#0x28` tag, `#0x2a` actor/direct selector | direct actor id / alias selector | `initPara@0x0071be02`-`0x0071be14`; direct path normalizes negative selectors through the proven `0x102e - selector` table. |
| `04 00 <listIndex:i32>` | `#0x2c` tag, `#0x30` list index/int | list source index when mode `> 0` | `initPara@0x0071be18`-`0x0071be2c`; list path reads `#0x30` at `0x0071bd26`-`0x0071bd2a`. |
| `04 00 <x:s16> 00 00` | `#0x34` tag, `#0x38` target x | absolute x coordinate | `initPara@0x0071be30`-`0x0071be44`; handler writes it to `HistoryActor+0x10`. |
| `04 00 <y:s16> 00 00` | `#0x3c` tag, `#0x40` target y | absolute y coordinate | `initPara@0x0071be48`-`0x0071be5c`; handler writes it to `HistoryActor+0x12`. |
| `2b 00 <direction:s16>` | `#0x44` tag, `#0x46` direction/facing | numeric direction/facing | `initPara@0x0071be60`-`0x0071be78`; handler writes it to actor field `+4`. |

`0x0055` native handler evidence:

| Native address | Hex | Decode result | Interpretation |
|---:|---|---|---|
| `ScriptBattleActorRelive::initPara@0x0071be7a`-`0x0071be82` | `00 23`; `2b 62`; `1e 30`; `70 bd` | initializes `#0x20=0`, returns `payload + 0x1e` | Fixed EEX payload length is `30`; `#0x20` is runtime/save state, not an EEX file field. |
| `saveScript@0x0071be94`-`0x0071bed2` | reads `#0x26`, `#0x2a`, `#0x30`, `#0x38`, `#0x40`, `#0x46`, then `#0x20` | saved semantic fields omit parse tags | Same tag/semantic split as `0x0032`; `#0x20` is not populated by legacy EEX init. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071bcd0`-`0x0071bd2a` | mode read, direct negative-alias path, or list-index path | resolves the target actor | Actor source is structurally separable: direct/alias or list-index. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071bd30`-`0x0071bd44` | `08 22`; `a3 5e`; then reads actor `+0xe0` and compares `state-14 <= 2` | accepts actors with dead/inactive flag `+8 == 1`, or battle state `14..16` | This is a relive/re-entry gate, not a normal movement op. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071bd4a`-`0x0071bd6a` | call `History::CenterActor`; clear actor `+0xe0`; write `#0x38/#0x40` to actor `+0x10/+0x12`; call `History::FindNearestBlackPos` | places the actor at/near requested absolute coordinates | Coordinates are gameplay fields, not display-only bytes. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071bd70`-`0x0071bd74` | `db 8f`; `a3 80` | write `#0x46` to actor field `+4` | Direction/facing is numeric and separable; human direction names remain unproven. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071bda0`-`0x0071bdbe` | calls `InitAbility`, `InitAbilityForRevive`, `recoverState`, restores actor byte `+0x88`, then `History::CheckPosActor` | ability/state cleanup and position validation after relive | Confirms the semantic class as relive/re-entry. |
