`0x006d ScriptRelaReviveOrMove` is the relative-position form. It carries both the actor to move/relive and a reference actor whose current x/y are used as the base for offsets.

`0x006d ScriptRelaReviveOrMove` field shape:

| File bytes after `6d 00` | Native field | Decode result | Evidence |
|---|---:|---|---|
| `40 00 <mode:s16>` | `#0x20` tag, `#0x22` mode | actor source mode | `initPara@0x0070afc2`-`0x0070afd2`; handler reads `#0x22`. |
| `02 00 <actor:s16>` | `#0x24` tag, `#0x26` actor/direct selector | target actor id / alias selector | `initPara@0x0070afd4`-`0x0070afe6`; direct paths normalize negative aliases through the same selector table. |
| `04 00 <listIndex:i32>` | `#0x28` tag, `#0x2c` list index/int | list source index when mode `> 0` | `initPara@0x0070afea`-`0x0070affe`; list path is native-supported but not used in this package's strict `0x006d` records. |
| `02 00 <refActor:s16>` | `#0x30` tag, `#0x32` reference actor selector | reference actor id / alias selector | `initPara@0x0070b002`-`0x0070b016`; handler resolves `#0x32` before coordinate calculation. |
| `04 00 <dx:i32>` | `#0x34` tag, `#0x38` x offset | x offset from reference actor | `initPara@0x0070b01a`-`0x0070b02e`; native normalizes values `>39` as `40 - value` before use. |
| `04 00 <dy:i32>` | `#0x3c` tag, `#0x40` y offset | y offset from reference actor | `initPara@0x0070b032`-`0x0070b046`; same normalization rule as `dx`. |
| `2b 00 <direction:s16>` | `#0x44` tag, `#0x46` direction/facing | numeric direction/facing | `saveScript@0x0070b0ce`-`0x0070b0da`; movement path writes this into replay/context before `GenerateDefaultMove`. |
| `26 00 <flag:s16>` | `#0x48` tag, `#0x4a` branch flag | `0` = relative move path, nonzero = `ActorRevive` path | `HandleScript@0x0070b4cc`-`0x0070b4dc` reads `#0x4a`; if nonzero it calls `ActorRevive@0x0070b348`. |

`0x006d` native handler evidence:

| Native address | Hex | Decode result | Interpretation |
|---:|---|---|---|
| `initPara@0x0070b082`-`0x0070b086` | `26 30`; `70 bd` | returns `payload + 0x26` | Fixed EEX payload length is `38`. |
| `saveScript@0x0070b098`-`0x0070b0e4` | reads `#0x22`, `#0x26`, `#0x2c`, `#0x32`, `#0x38`, `#0x40`, `#0x46`, `#0x4a` | saved semantic fields omit parse tags | Confirms field layout and final branch flag. |
| `HandleScript@0x0070b4cc`-`0x0070b4dc` | `4a 32`; `52 5e`; `00 2a`; call `ActorRevive` if nonzero | final `#0x4a` selects revive path | This is a real semantic branch, not an unused tail field. |
| `HandleScript@0x0070b4f0`-`0x0070b554` | resolve target actor from direct/alias or list source, then `BattleControler::getBattleActor` | target actor resolution for relative move path | Same actor namespace mechanics as `0x0032`/`0x0055`. |
| `HandleScript@0x0070b55a`-`0x0070b572` | if `#0x38/#0x40 > 0x27`, rewrite as `0x28 - value` | offset normalization | Observed `dx=41` therefore becomes `-1` at runtime; preserve raw and decoded-normalized forms. |
| `HandleScript@0x0070b572`-`0x0070b5b8` | resolve reference actor `#0x32`; read its `+0x10/+0x12`; add `#0x38/#0x40` | target = reference actor coordinate plus offset | `#0x32` is the anchor/reference actor field. |
| `HandleScript@0x0070b5dc`-`0x0070b610` | call `History::FindNearestBlackPos`; call `BattleActor::GenerateDefaultMove`; call `BattleActor::setState(13)`; store wait in `#0x18` | relative move execution | Relative move path is not opaque; it maps to a numeric move op. |
| `ActorRevive@0x0070b3c6`-`0x0070b492` | center actor, clear `+0xe0`, normalize offsets, compute coordinate from reference actor, call `FindNearestBlackPos`, clear actor `+8`, write direction to actor `+4`, call `InitAbilityForRevive`, then `History::CheckPosActor` | relative relive/re-entry execution | Nonzero `#0x4a` is a relative revive/re-entry branch. |

Representative `0x006d` byte evidence:

| Sample | Hex | Decoded fields | Status |
|---|---|---|---|
| `Scenes/S_00.eex_new@0x239b5` | `6d 00 40 00 00 00 02 00 35 01 04 00 00 00 00 00 02 00 36 01 04 00 00 00 00 00 04 00 00 00 00 00 2b 00 ff ff 26 00 00 00` | mode `0`, actor `309`, reference actor `310`, dx/dy `(0,0)`, direction `-1`, flag `0` | Relative move path: move actor 309 to reference actor 310's coordinate. |
| `Scenes/S_01.eex_new@0x30390` | `6d 00 40 00 00 00 02 00 e0 00 04 00 00 00 00 00 02 00 d9 00 04 00 00 00 00 00 04 00 00 00 00 00 2b 00 ff ff 26 00 01 00` | mode `0`, actor `224`, reference actor `217`, dx/dy `(0,0)`, direction `-1`, flag `1` | Relative relive/re-entry path: nonzero flag calls `ActorRevive`. |
| `Scenes/S_06.eex_new@0x24ffe` | `6d 00 40 00 00 00 02 00 13 00 04 00 00 00 00 00 02 00 04 00 04 00 07 00 00 00 04 00 00 00 00 00 2b 00 00 00 26 00 00 00` | mode `0`, actor `19`, reference actor `4`, dx/dy `(7,0)`, direction `0`, flag `0` | Relative move with nonzero x offset. |
| `Scenes/S_107.eex_new@0x227e8` | `6d 00 40 00 00 00 02 00 18 00 04 00 00 00 00 00 02 00 0b 00 04 00 00 00 00 00 04 00 01 00 00 00 2b 00 00 00 26 00 01 00` | mode `0`, actor `24`, reference actor `11`, dx/dy `(0,1)`, direction `0`, flag `1` | Relative revive with nonzero y offset. |

Status: revival/re-entry is no longer a pure reinforcement/spawn blocker. `0x0055` gives absolute-coordinate relive/re-entry, and `0x006d` gives reference-actor-relative move or relive/re-entry depending on the final flag. Remaining uncertainty is human-facing labels for direction values, rare list-source mode semantics, and whether separate spawn/reinforcement commands exist beyond relive/re-entry and the already decoded deployment records.

### 4.8.3 Actor HP / State Change: `0x004d ScriptChangeActorState`

`0x004d ScriptChangeActorState` is not an opaque status blob. It has a fixed `0x42` payload and a repeatable typed-tag shape across `1969` strict records. It contains actor source selection, optional rectangle targeting, side filtering, an operation enum, a status mask, and HP/MP numeric deltas. Human labels for the status bits are not proven yet.

Text-field status: this opcode has no string/DString payload in the fixed `0x42` shape. Text corruption is therefore not part of the `0x004d` judgement; the question here is numeric structure, not mojibake.

`0x004d ScriptChangeActorState` field shape:

| File bytes after `4d 00` | Native field | Decode result | Evidence |
|---|---:|---|---|
| `41 00 <sourceMode:s16>` | `#0x20` tag, `#0x22` source mode | `0` direct actor, `1` list index, `2` area scan | `initPara@0x00719b40`-`0x00719b50`; `HandleScript` branches on `#0x22`. |
| `02 00 <actor:s16>` | `#0x24` tag, `#0x26` actor | direct actor id / alias selector | `initPara@0x00719b52`-`0x00719b64`; direct mode uses the same actor-selector normalization family as movement/relive handlers. |
| `04 00 <listIndex:i32>` | `#0x28` tag, `#0x2c` list index/int | list-source index when source mode `1` | `saveScript@0x00719cc0` writes `#0x2c`; corpus has only `3` strict source-mode-`1` records. |
| `04 00 <x1:s16> 00 00` | `#0x30` tag, `#0x34` x1 | rectangle start x | `initPara@0x00719b78`-`0x00719b8c`; `getActorList@0x00719f74` compares x against `#0x44`. |
| `04 00 <y1:s16> 00 00` | `#0x38` tag, `#0x3c` y1 | rectangle start y | `initPara@0x00719b90`-`0x00719ba4`; `getActorList@0x00719f6c` compares y against `#0x4c`. |
| `04 00 <x2:s16> 00 00` | `#0x40` tag, `#0x44` x2 | rectangle end x | `initPara@0x00719ba8`-`0x00719bbc`; `getActorList` scans x1..x2. |
| `04 00 <y2:s16> 00 00` | `#0x48` tag, `#0x4c` y2 | rectangle end y | `initPara@0x00719bc0`-`0x00719bd4`; `getActorList` scans y1..y2. |
| `03 00 <sideSelector:s16>` | `#0x50` tag, `#0x52` side selector | area-mode side filter `0..7` | `getActorList@0x00719f90`-`0x00719f9a` reads selector; branch logic matches the decoded `0x0053` side filters. |
| `2f 00 <opRaw:s16>` | `#0x54` tag, `#0x56` op | numeric operation enum; raw `1`/`2` are swapped in native save/load semantics | `initPara` stores `#0x56`; `setScript@0x00719d70` also swaps `1 <-> 2`. Human labels are not proven. |
| `18 00 <animB:s16>` | `#0x58` constant `24`, `#0x5a` anim/effect code | visual/effect selector fields | Corpus has `#0x58=24` for all strict records; `#0x5a` values are enumerable but not human-named. |
| `30 00 <mask:s16>` | `#0x5c` tag, `#0x5e` mask | status/state bit mask; `-1` sentinel observed | Handler tests mask bits and writes actor bytes such as `+0xc2`, `+0xc3`, `+0xc4`, `+0xc5`, `+0xc8`, `+0x460`, and `+0xcc`. Exact ailment names remain unknown. |
| `04 00 <hpDelta:s16> 00 00` | `#0x62` tag, `#0x64` HP delta | HP change amount; observed positive values reduce HP through `SetCurHp` | `HandleScript@0x0071a3c6`-`0x0071a44a` reads runtime delta and calls `HistoryActor::SetCurHp`. |
| `04 00 <mpDelta:s16> 00 00` | `#0x68` tag, `#0x6c` MP delta | MP change amount; native-supported but unused in this package | `HandleScript@0x0071a44e`-`0x0071a4b2` reads runtime delta and calls `HistoryActor::SetCurMp`; all strict records have `mpDelta=0`. |

Native handler evidence:

| Native address | Hex / instruction evidence | Decode result | Interpretation |
|---:|---|---|---|
| `initPara@0x00719cac`-`0x00719cb8` | stores zero to `#0x70/#0x74/#0x78/#0x7c`; tail returns `payload + 0x42` | fixed legacy payload length `0x42` | The four later fields are runtime/effect fields, not EEX bytes. |
| `saveScript@0x00719cc0`-`0x00719d5e` | writes `#0x22/#0x26/#0x2c/#0x34/#0x3c/#0x44/#0x4c/#0x52/#0x56/#0x5a/#0x5e/#0x64/#0x6c/#0x70/#0x74/#0x78/#0x7c` | saved semantic fields omit parse tags | Confirms tag/value split and semantic field retention. |
| `getActorList@0x00719f6c`-`0x0071a00c` | reads rect fields, calls `History::FindActorPosition`, increments count at `script+0x210`, stores ids at `script+(count+0x20)*4` | area source builds an actor-id list | Area targeting is structural, not a display-only highlight. |
| `getActorList@0x00719f90`-`0x00719f9a` | reads `#0x52`; branch table covers selectors `0..7` | side selector matches own/friend/enemy/assist/any/side-byte-4 filters | Same side-filter vocabulary as decoded `0x0053`; side-byte-4 human label remains open. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071a3c6`-`0x0071a44a` | reads HP delta from `script+0x218`, clamps against current/total HP, calls `HistoryActor::SetCurHp` | HP delta is executable gameplay state | This is the first byte-level proof for HP-changing script ops. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071a44e`-`0x0071a4b2` | reads MP delta from `script+0x21c`, clamps against current/total MP, calls `HistoryActor::SetCurMp` | MP delta path exists | Package corpus does not exercise nonzero MP deltas. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071aa80`-`0x0071abc0` | tests `#0x5e` mask bits and writes actor state bytes | status/state mask is separable from HP/MP deltas | Structure is green; human status labels are still undecoded. |

Strict corpus scan for `0x004d` using tag sequence `4d 00 41 00 <sourceMode> 02 00 <actor> 04 00 <listIndex:i32> 04 00 <x1> 00 00 04 00 <y1> 00 00 04 00 <x2> 00 00 04 00 <y2> 00 00 03 00 <sideSelector> 2f 00 <opRaw> 18 00 <animB:s16> 30 00 <mask> 04 00 <hpDelta> 00 00 04 00 <mpDelta> 00 00`:

| Measure | Result |
|---|---:|
| Strict records | `1969` |
| Files | `146` |
| Prefix split | `S=1969`, `R=0` |
| Source mode split | `2=1180`, `0=786`, `1=3` |
| Side selector split | `6=538`, `2=488`, `5=383`, `0=329`, `4=162`, `3=47`, `1=22` |
| opRaw split | `0=488`, `1=390`, `5=279`, `4=258`, `3=244`, `2=190`, `-1=107`, `6=13` |
| constant `#0x58` split | `24=1969` |
| anim/effect `#0x5a` split | `2=1453`, `0=396`, `-1=104`, `3=8`, `1=8` |
| mask split | `-1=1493`, `0=256`, `8=57`, `2=26`, `16=25`, `138=20`, `30=20`, `158=17`, `20=14`, other values lower count |
| HP delta split | `0=1852`, `50=49`, `100=46`, `80=6`, `150=4`, `20=3`, `200=2`, `300=2`, `30/5/250/160/600=1` |
| MP delta split | `0=1969` |
| Coordinate ranges | x1 `0..33`, y1 `0..34`, x2 `0..39`, y2 `0..39` |

|---|---|---|---|

Status: `0x004d` can be represented fail-closed as a numeric actor state-change op with source mode, direct/list/area targeting, side selector, operation enum, mask, HP delta, and MP delta. HP conversion is structurally viable at the byte level; status conversion must remain numeric/unlabeled until mask bits are correlated with visible ailment/status names.

### 4.8.4 Actor AI Change: `0x004e ScriptChangeActorAI`

`0x004e ScriptChangeActorAI` changes low-level AI/strategy fields on one direct actor or on actors selected by rectangle plus side/list selector. It has a fixed `0x38` payload and a stable typed-tag shape in `1060` strict S-script records. The byte structure is green; human labels for AI mode enum `0..6` are not yet proven.

Text-field status: this opcode has no string/DString payload. There is no text-decoding question for `0x004e`; the recoverability question is numeric structure and AI enum labels.

`0x004e ScriptChangeActorAI` field shape:

| File bytes after `4e 00` | Native field | Decode result | Evidence |
|---|---:|---|---|
| `2c 00 <mode:s16>` | `#0x20` tag, `#0x22` mode | observed `0` direct actor, `1` area/list mode | `initPara@0x0071b1e4`-`0x0071b1f4`; `HandleScript@0x0071ac70`-`0x0071ac7c` branches on `#0x22 <= 0`. |
| `02 00 <actor:s16>` | `#0x24` tag, `#0x26` actor | direct actor id / selector | `initPara@0x0071b1f8`-`0x0071b208`; direct branch computes actor pointer from `#0x26`. |
| `04 00 <x1:s16> 00 00` | `#0x28` tag, `#0x2c` x1 | rectangle x1 / first area bound | `initPara@0x0071b20c`-`0x0071b222`; area branch passes `#0x2c` to `HistoryActor::inArea`. |
| `04 00 <y1:s16> 00 00` | `#0x30` tag, `#0x34` y1 | rectangle y1 / second area bound | `initPara@0x0071b226`-`0x0071b238`; area branch passes `#0x34` to `HistoryActor::inArea`. |
| `04 00 <x2:s16> 00 00` | `#0x38` tag, `#0x3c` x2 | rectangle x2 / third area bound | `initPara@0x0071b23e`-`0x0071b250`; area branch passes `#0x3c` to `HistoryActor::inArea`. |
| `04 00 <y2:s16> 00 00` | `#0x40` tag, `#0x44` y2 | rectangle y2 / fourth area bound | `initPara@0x0071b256`-`0x0071b26a`; area branch passes `#0x44` via stack to `HistoryActor::inArea`. |
| `03 00 <selector:s16>` | `#0x48` tag, `#0x4a` selector | area/list side selector; observed `0..6` | `HandleScript@0x0071ac7e`-`0x0071acbe` rejects `#0x4a > 7`; switch body iterates actor lists and applies area checks. |
| `07 00 <aiMode:s16>` | `#0x4c` tag, `#0x4e` AI mode enum | first AI field; observed enum `0..6` | Handler writes `#0x4e` to `HistoryActor+6` in direct and area branches. |
| `02 00 <aiTarget:s16>` | `#0x50` tag, `#0x52` AI target actor/selector | second AI field, actor-like namespace | Handler writes `#0x52` to `HistoryActor+0x0a`; tag `02` and observed values include actor ids, `-1`, `1025`, `1026`. |
| `04 00 <aiX:s16> 00 00` | `#0x54` tag, `#0x58` AI arg x / numeric arg | third AI field | Handler writes `#0x58` to `HistoryActor+0x0c`; observed values mostly `0`, otherwise coordinate-like `1..34`. |
| `04 00 <aiY:s16> 00 00` | `#0x5c` tag, `#0x60` AI arg y / numeric arg | fourth AI field | Handler writes `#0x60` to `HistoryActor+0x0e`; observed values mostly `0`, otherwise coordinate-like `1..33`. |

Native handler evidence:

| Native address | Hex / instruction evidence | Decode result | Interpretation |
|---:|---|---|---|
| `initPara@0x0071b302`-`0x0071b306` | `20 1c`; `38 30`; `70 bd` | returns `payload + 0x38` | Fixed EEX payload length is `56`. |
| `saveScript@0x0071b318`-`0x0071b382` | writes `#0x22/#0x26/#0x2c/#0x34/#0x3c/#0x44/#0x4a/#0x4e/#0x52/#0x58/#0x60` | saved semantic fields omit parse tags | Confirms the split between typed file tags and runtime AI values. |
| `setScript@0x0071b390`-`0x0071b3f8` | reads the same fields back from `DMemoryReader` | save/load shape matches parsed semantic fields | These fields are intentionally persisted, not transient parser scratch. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071ac70`-`0x0071ac8a` | reads `#0x22`; if mode is positive, reads `#0x4a` and rejects values above `7` | mode and selector control direct vs multi-actor application | Strict corpus uses mode `0/1`; selector values are `0..6`. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071ac8a`-`0x0071acb4` | computes actor pointer from `#0x26`, then writes `#0x4e -> +6`, `#0x52 -> +0x0a`, `#0x58 -> +0x0c`, `#0x60 -> +0x0e` | direct actor AI field update | This is a gameplay state mutation, not a display-only marker. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071ad0e`-`0x0071ad1a` and repeated area cases | loads `#0x2c/#0x34/#0x3c/#0x44`; calls `HistoryActor::inArea` | rectangle filter for area/list mode | Area bounds are structurally real and used before AI field writes. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071ad22`-`0x0071ad38` and repeated area cases | writes the same four AI fields to the selected actor | selected actors receive the AI change | Direct and area modes share the same target field writes. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071ad9e`-`0x0071ae1c` | tests `HistoryActor+0x668` against `0` / `1` in adjacent list cases | selector switch includes enemy/assist-style subfilters | This mirrors the known side-selector split, but exact human selector labels should stay tied to separately proven side-filter evidence. |

Strict corpus scan for `0x004e` using tag sequence `4e 00 2c 00 <mode> 02 00 <actor> 04 00 <x1> 00 00 04 00 <y1> 00 00 04 00 <x2> 00 00 04 00 <y2> 00 00 03 00 <selector> 07 00 <aiMode> 02 00 <aiTarget> 04 00 <aiX> 00 00 04 00 <aiY> 00 00`:

| Measure | Result |
|---|---:|
| Strict records | `1060` |
| Files | `122` |
| Prefix split | `S=1060`, `R=0` |
| Mode split | `1=575`, `0=485` |
| Selector split | `5=449`, `6=278`, `2=262`, `3=38`, `1=14`, `0=14`, `4=5` |
| AI mode enum split | `1=619`, `2=179`, `6=95`, `3=57`, `0=49`, `4=31`, `5=30` |
| AI target split | `-1=628`, `0=271`, then actor-like values including `36=25`, `256=19`, `1025=9`, `1026=4` |
| AI arg x split | `0=881`; nonzero values are `1..34` with top values `17=22`, `29=21`, `19=20`, `5=15` |
| AI arg y split | `0=903`; nonzero values are `1..33` with top values `1=24`, `29=22`, `10=14` |
| Area coordinate ranges | x1 `0..38`, y1 `0..39`, x2 `0..99`, y2 `0..99` |

Status: `0x004e` can be preserved as a fail-closed numeric `SetActorAi`-style operation: target mode, actor id, optional rectangle, selector, AI mode enum, target actor/selector, and two extra numeric/coordinate arguments are all recoverable. What remains undecoded is human naming for AI modes `0..6`, exact selector labels through the switch helper, and semantic labels for the last two numeric arguments.

### 4.8.5 Battle Barrier / Map Element Change: `0x0058 ScriptSetBattleBarrier`

`0x0058 ScriptSetBattleBarrier` is a timed map-element/barrier mutation. It has a fixed `0x20` payload and a stable typed-tag shape in `924` strict S-script records. Native execution either constructs a `MapElem` at x/y and appends it to the battle map-element list, or finds an existing x/y map element and removes it. The byte structure is green; human labels for the element id / tile byte are not proven.

Text-field status: this opcode has no string/DString payload. The recoverability question is numeric structure and map-element semantics, not text encoding.

`0x0058 ScriptSetBattleBarrier` field shape:

| File bytes after `58 00` | Native field | Decode result | Evidence |
|---|---:|---|---|
| `42 00 <kind:s16>` | `#0x20` tag, `#0x22` kind/type | map element / barrier kind id | `initPara@0x0071c260`-`0x0071c270`; handler passes `#0x22` as an argument to `MapElemC2Eiiiii`. |
| `43 00 <flag:s16>` | `#0x24` tag, `#0x26` action flag | `0` add path, nonzero remove/find-existing path | `HandleScript@0x0071c0f2`-`0x0071c104` branches on `#0x26`; nonzero scans existing elements by x/y, zero creates a new `MapElem`. |
| `44 00 <tile:s16>` | `#0x28` tag, `#0x2a` tile/element byte | retained map-element value / tile byte | `HandleScript@0x0071c142`-`0x0071c156` passes `#0x2a` to the `MapElem` constructor; `0x0071c1d2`-`0x0071c1da` writes it into a map byte table when that table is present. |
| `04 00 <x:s16> 00 00` | `#0x2c` tag, `#0x30` x | x coordinate | `saveScript@0x0071c35e` writes `#0x30`; handler compares existing `MapElem[0]` with `#0x30` and passes it to `MapElemC2Eiiiii`. |
| `04 00 <y:s16> 00 00` | `#0x34` tag, `#0x38` y | y coordinate | `saveScript@0x0071c366` writes `#0x38`; handler compares existing `MapElem[4]` with `#0x38` and passes it to `MapElemC2Eiiiii`. |
| `26 00 <delay:s16>` | `#0x3c` tag, `#0x3e` delay | stage counter / initial wait gate | `HandleScript@0x0071c0ac`-`0x0071c0f0` compares runtime stage `#0x14` to `#0x3e`; save/load persists `#0x3e`. |
| `26 00 <postDelay:s16>` | `#0x40` tag, `#0x42` post delay | additional wait after mutation | `HandleScript@0x0071c1dc`-`0x0071c1e8` sets wait `#0x18 = #0x3e + #0x42`; save/load persists `#0x42`. |

Native handler evidence:

| Native address | Hex / instruction evidence | Decode result | Interpretation |
|---:|---|---|---|
| `initPara@0x0071c326`-`0x0071c32a` | `28 1c`; `20 30`; `70 bd` | returns `payload + 0x20` | Fixed EEX payload length is `32`. |
| `saveScript@0x0071c340`-`0x0071c380` | writes `#0x22/#0x26/#0x2a/#0x30/#0x38/#0x3e/#0x42` | saved semantic fields omit parse tags | Confirms the seven gameplay fields retained from the typed payload. |
| `setScript@0x0071c38e`-`0x0071c3ce` | reads the same fields back from `DMemoryReader` | save/load shape matches parsed semantic fields | Barrier/map-element mutation is persistent across saved script state. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071c0b2`-`0x0071c0f0` | reads `#0x3e`; initializes/computes wait; plays sound id `0x13` or `0x12` around the delay gate | `#0x3e` gates when the mutation fires | Delay fields are control-flow timing, not unused padding. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071c0f2`-`0x0071c12c` | if `#0x26 != 0`, scan vector entries and compare entry x/y with `#0x30/#0x38` | nonzero flag finds an existing map element at x/y | This is the remove/update path. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071c132`-`0x0071c15a` | allocates `0x3c`; passes `#0x30`, `#0x38`, `#0x22`, `#0x2a`, and `-1` to `MapElemC2Eiiiii` | zero flag constructs a new map element | Confirms x/y/kind/tile fields are gameplay fields. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071c1a6`-`0x0071c1b4` | appends the new `MapElem` pointer to a vector and increments vector count | add path mutates the battle map-element list | The op changes runtime battle map state. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071c1d2`-`0x0071c1da` | indexes a map byte table by y and x, then stores `#0x2a` as a byte | optional map-grid byte update | `#0x2a` is not cosmetic; it can affect map tile byte state. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071c1f6`-`0x0071c230` | calls `MapElemD2`, frees the found element, compacts vector entries, decrements vector count | remove path deletes the matched map element | Nonzero `#0x26` is structurally a remove/find-existing branch. |

Strict corpus scan for `0x0058` using tag sequence `58 00 42 00 <kind> 43 00 <flag> 44 00 <tile> 04 00 <x> 00 00 04 00 <y> 00 00 26 00 <delay> 26 00 <postDelay>`:

| Measure | Result |
|---|---:|
| Strict records | `924` |
| Files | `42` |
| Prefix split | `S=924`, `R=0` |
| Flag split | `0=608`, `1=316` |
| Kind top values | `0=271`, `3=204`, `2=136`, `1=37`; `100` unique kind values, range `0..112` |
| Tile value split | `26=271`, `17=160`, `0=134`, `16=118`, `14=81`, `15=59`, `27=37`, `5=26`; `16` unique values, range `0..27` |
| Coordinate ranges | x `0..39`, y `0..33` |
| Delay split | `0=814`, `1=110` |
| Post-delay split | `1=494`, `0=430` |

Status: `0x0058` can be preserved as a fail-closed numeric map-element/barrier mutation with kind, add/remove flag, tile value, x/y, delay, and post-delay. What remains undecoded is human naming for kind/tile values and whether every kind affects movement, visuals, terrain bytes, or a mix of those.

### 4.8.6 Battle Bonus / Reward Goods: `0x0059 ScriptSetBattleBonus`

`0x0059 ScriptSetBattleBonus` is a battle reward operation. It has a fixed `0x22` payload and a stable typed-tag shape in `377` strict S-script records. Native execution contributes money through `History::SetMoney`, creates up to three `HistoryGood` objects from decoded good ids, then opens battle bonus / booty UI paths. The byte structure for money and goods is green; per-good extra fields and the final tail field are retained but not yet named.

Text-field status: this opcode has no string/DString payload. The recoverability question is numeric reward structure, not text encoding.

`0x0059 ScriptSetBattleBonus` field shape:

| File bytes after `59 00` | Native field | Decode result | Evidence |
|---|---:|---|---|
| `04 00 <moneyLow:s16> <moneyHigh:s16>` | `#0x20` tag, `#0x24` money | configured money bonus; current corpus has high word `0` in all strict records | `initPara@0x0071c3ee` stores tag `#0x20`; `initPara@0x0071c3f8` stores `#0x24`; `saveScript@0x0071c4be` writes `#0x24` through `DMemoryWriter::writeInt`. |
| `17 00 <good1:s16>` | `#0x28` tag, `#0x2a` good1 | first reward good id, `-1` sentinel for empty | `HandleScript@0x0071ca74` reads `#0x2a`; bounds-checks it against the good table; `0x0071caba` passes it to `HistoryGood::init`. |
| `49 00 <extra1:s16>` | `#0x2c` tag, `#0x2e` extra1 | retained per-good field, label unknown | `saveScript@0x0071c4d0` writes `#0x2e`; `setScript@0x0071c52e` reads it back. No current handler-side semantic label is proven. |
| `17 00 <good2:s16>` | `#0x30` tag, `#0x32` good2 | second reward good id, `-1` sentinel for empty | `HandleScript@0x0071caf8` reads `#0x32`; `0x0071cb3c` passes it to `HistoryGood::init`. |
| `49 00 <extra2:s16>` | `#0x34` tag, `#0x36` extra2 | retained per-good field, label unknown | `saveScript@0x0071c4e4` writes `#0x36`; `setScript@0x0071c540` reads it back. |
| `17 00 <good3:s16>` | `#0x38` tag, `#0x3a` good3 | third reward good id, `-1` sentinel for empty | `HandleScript@0x0071cb78` reads `#0x3a`; `0x0071cbbc` passes it to `HistoryGood::init`. |
| `49 00 <extra3:s16>` | `#0x3c` tag, `#0x3e` extra3 | retained per-good field, label unknown | `saveScript@0x0071c4ee` writes `#0x3e`; `setScript@0x0071c554` reads it back. |
| `26 00 <tail:s16>` | `#0x40` tag, `#0x42` tail | retained tail flag/value, label unknown | `saveScript@0x0071c506` writes `#0x42`; `setScript@0x0071c560` reads it back. |

Native handler evidence:

| Native address | Hex / instruction evidence | Decode result | Interpretation |
|---:|---|---|---|
| `initPara@0x0071c4a8`-`0x0071c4ac` | `20 1c`; `22 30`; `70 bd` | returns `payload + 0x22` | Fixed EEX payload length is `34`. |
| `saveScript@0x0071c4be`-`0x0071c50a` | writes `#0x24` via `writeInt`, then `#0x2a/#0x2e/#0x32/#0x36/#0x3a/#0x3e/#0x42` via `writeShort` | saved semantic fields omit parse tags | Confirms money plus three good/extra pairs plus tail are retained. |
| `setScript@0x0071c518`-`0x0071c562` | reads `#0x24` via `tryReadInt`, then the same seven short fields | save/load shape matches retained fields | Battle bonus script state is persistent. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071ca64`-`0x0071ca70` | loads `#0x24`, adds it to a computed reward base, calls `History::SetMoney` with `r1=-1` | money field contributes to the reward-money mutation | Exact base-money policy is separate from file byte recovery and remains open. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071ca74`-`0x0071cac0` | reads `#0x2a`, checks nonnegative and `< goodCount`, allocates `HistoryGood`, calls `HistoryGood::init(goodId, -1)` | first explicit good slot | `-1` and out-of-range values are skipped/fail-closed by native code. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071caf8`-`0x0071cb42` | same pattern for `#0x32` | second explicit good slot | Confirms the second good id is not a tag or text artifact. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071cb78`-`0x0071cbc2` | same pattern for `#0x3a` | third explicit good slot | Confirms three explicit reward good slots. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071c9a4`-`0x0071c9bc` / `0x0071cc00`-`0x0071cc10` | constructs `Booty` / `BattleBonus` with money and `HistoryGood*` values | reward UI/display path | The op is a battle reward operation, not a generic item-table edit. |

Strict corpus scan for `0x0059` using tag sequence `59 00 04 00 <money:u32-le/current low word> 17 00 <good1> 49 00 <extra1> 17 00 <good2> 49 00 <extra2> 17 00 <good3> 49 00 <extra3> 26 00 <tail>`:

### 4.8.7 Battle Presentation Highlight: `0x005b ScriptBattleHighlightArea` / `0x005c ScriptBattleHighlightActor`

`0x005b` and `0x005c` are presentation highlight operations, not currently evidence for win-condition areas, spawn, or reinforcement. Native execution creates `FogElem` presentation objects, writes/centers screen highlight state, calls `History::CheckPos`, or centers on an existing `HistoryActor`. No traced path mutates battle HP, actor state, deployment, inventory, win/lose state, or trigger variables.

Text-field status: neither opcode has a string/DString payload. The recoverability question is numeric target structure and presentation role, not text encoding.

`0x005b ScriptBattleHighlightArea` field shape:

| File bytes after `5b 00` | Native field | Decode result | Evidence |
|---|---:|---|---|
| `04 00 <x1:s16> 00 00` | `#0x20` tag, `#0x24` x1 | rectangle start x | `initPara@0x0071cfe8` stores tag `#0x20`; `initPara@0x0071cff2` stores int `#0x24`; handler uses `#0x24` as the outer x loop start. |
| `04 00 <y1:s16> 00 00` | `#0x28` tag, `#0x2c` y1 | rectangle start y | `initPara@0x0071d008` stores int `#0x2c`; handler uses `#0x2c` as the inner y loop start. |
| `04 00 <x2:s16> 00 00` | `#0x30` tag, `#0x34` x2 | rectangle end x | `initPara@0x0071d020` stores int `#0x34`; handler compares x cursor against `#0x34`. |
| `04 00 <y2:s16> 00 00` | `#0x38` tag, `#0x3c` y2 | rectangle end y | `initPara@0x0071d038` stores int `#0x3c`; handler compares y cursor against `#0x3c`. |
| `26 00 <tail:s16>` | `#0x40` tag, `#0x42` tail flag | presentation flag/timing selector, label unknown | `saveScript@0x0071d094` writes `#0x42`; handler checks `#0x42 + 1 <= 1` before writing global highlight rectangle slots. |

`0x005c ScriptBattleHighlightActor` field shape:

| File bytes after `5c 00` | Native field | Decode result | Evidence |
|---|---:|---|---|
| `02 00 <actor:s16>` | `#0x20` tag, `#0x22` actor id/selector | actor-centered highlight target | `initPara@0x0071d164` stores tag `#0x20`; `initPara@0x0071d16e` stores `#0x22`; handler reads `#0x22` then calls `History::FindBattleActor`. |

| `ScriptBattleHighlightActor::HandleScript@0x0071d11c`-`0x0071d13e` | reads actor x/y from `HistoryActor+0x10/+0x12`, writes `0x30`-scaled screen rectangle, calls `History::CenterActor` | centers/highlights the target actor | Native role is presentation focus on an existing actor. |

These opcodes should not be used as evidence for win-condition conversion, reinforcement, spawn, or gameplay state mutation.

### 4.8.8 Battle Round Limit: `0x005d ScriptSetMaxRound`

`0x005d` is a battle max-round operation. Native execution routes through `History::SetMaxRound`, not text display, reward, actor state, deployment, or map mutation. The file payload is fixed at `0x0a` bytes after the command id.

Field shape in old EEX:

```text
5d 00
  <tag0:s16>
  <mode:s16>
  04 00
  <value:s16> 00 00
```

Native field retention:

| Native address | Hex | Decoded behavior | Interpretation |
|---:|---|---|---|
| `ScriptSetMaxRound::initPara@0x0071d1be` | `22 f7 92 ff` | `bytesToShort(payload+0)` -> object `#0x20` | Old tag/control field, retained in memory but not used by `HandleScript`. |
| `ScriptSetMaxRound::initPara@0x0071d1c8` / `0x0071d1ce` | `22 f7 8d ff`; `68 84` | `bytesToShort(payload+2)` -> object `#0x22` | Mode field. |
| `ScriptSetMaxRound::initPara@0x0071d1d2` / `0x0071d1d8` | `22 f7 88 ff`; `a8 84` | `bytesToShort(payload+4)` -> object `#0x24` | Old value tag; strict corpus uses `0x0004`. |
| `ScriptSetMaxRound::initPara@0x0071d1dc` / `0x0071d1e0` | `22 f7 83 ff`; `a8 62` | `bytesToShort(payload+6)` -> object `#0x28` int slot | Numeric round value; payload `+8/+9` are the zero high half of the old int-shaped field. |
| `ScriptSetMaxRound::initPara@0x0071d1e2`-`0x0071d1e6` | `20 1c`; `0a 30`; `70 bd` | returns `payload + 0x0a` | Fixed old-EEX payload length is `0x0a`. |
| `ScriptSetMaxRound::saveScript@0x0071d1f8`-`0x0071d206` | `e9 5e`; `a9 6a`; calls `writeShort`, then `writeInt` | serializes object `#0x22`, `#0x28` after command id | Native save format keeps mode and value, not old tag fields `#0x20/#0x24`. |

Runtime mode behavior:

| Mode | Native evidence | Behavior | Corpus count |
|---:|---|---|---:|
| `0` | `HandleScript@0x0071d24c`-`0x0071d260`: load `#0x28`, call `History::GetExtraMaxRound`, add it to value, then fall through to `History::SetMaxRound`. | Set max round to `value + extraMaxRound`. | `23` |
| `1` | `HandleScript@0x0071d262`-`0x0071d27a`: load `#0x28`, set first `SetMaxRound` arg to `-1`, call `History::SetMaxRound`. `History::SetMaxRound@0x0068407e`-`0x00684094` treats negative first arg as `currentMaxRound + delta`. | Increase current max round by `value`. | `5` |
| `2` | `HandleScript@0x0071d26c`-`0x0071d274`: load `#0x28`, negate it, then uses the same negative-first-arg `SetMaxRound` path. | Decrease current max round by `value`. | `0` observed in this package |

Strict shape scan over `Scenes/*.eex_new`:

| Shape | Matches | Files | Distribution |
|---|---:|---:|---|
| `5d 00 <tag0> <mode> 04 00 <value:s16> 00 00`, with `tag0 in {0x0026,0x0034}` and `mode in {0,1,2}` | `28` | `18` S files | `tag0 0x0034=24`, `0x0026=4`; mode `0=23`, `1=5`, `2=0`; values range `5..80`. |

Representative records:

| File offset | Hex | Decoded fields | Interpretation |
|---|---|---|---|
| `Scenes/S_00.eex_new@0x230f6` | `5d 00 34 00 00 00 04 00 0f 00 00 00` | tag0 `0x0034`, mode `0`, value `15` | Set battle max round to `extraMaxRound + 15`. |
| `Scenes/S_04.eex_new@0x00193` | `5d 00 26 00 01 00 04 00 13 00 00 00` | tag0 `0x0026`, mode `1`, value `19` | Increase current max round by `19`. |
| `Scenes/S_24.eex_new@0x1ea75` | `5d 00 34 00 00 00 04 00 50 00 00 00` | tag0 `0x0034`, mode `0`, value `80` | Set battle max round to `extraMaxRound + 80`. |
| `Scenes/S_87.eex_new@0x036f7` | `5d 00 34 00 01 00 04 00 0a 00 00 00` | tag0 `0x0034`, mode `1`, value `10` | Increase current max round by `10`. |

Status: structure is green for a numeric `SetMaxRound` / `AdjustMaxRound` battle op. `mode 0/1/2` byte behavior is native-proven, but this package only exercises `0/1`; old tag fields `0x0026/0x0034` are not named and should be preserved or ignored only after a dumper proves they are format tags rather than scenario semantics.

### 4.8.9 Inventory / Equipment Good Removal: `0x006f ScriptGoodThrow`

`0x006f` is a good-id removal operation, not a text, branch, map, or battle-position command. Native execution searches inventory and actor equipment-like good slots for the target `good_id`, removes matching goods by writing `HistoryGood::SetGoodID(-1)`, and refreshes affected actor good effects.

Field shape in old EEX:

```text
6f 00
  17 00
  <good_id:s16>
```

Native field retention:

| Native address | Hex | Decoded behavior | Interpretation |
|---:|---|---|---|
| `ScriptGoodThrow::initPara@0x0070b7ca` / `0x0070b7d0` | `34 f7 8c fc`; `28 84` | `bytesToShort(payload+0)` -> object `#0x20` | Old tag/control field; strict command records use `0x0017`. |
| `ScriptGoodThrow::initPara@0x0070b7d4` / `0x0070b7d8` | `34 f7 87 fc`; `68 84` | `bytesToShort(payload+2)` -> object `#0x22` | Target `good_id`. |
| `ScriptGoodThrow::initPara@0x0070b7da`-`0x0070b7dc` | `20 1d`; `70 bd` | returns `payload + 4` | Fixed payload length `0x04`. |
| `ScriptGoodThrow::saveScript@0x0070b7ee`-`0x0070b7f4` | `e9 5e`; `writeShort` | writes object `#0x22` after command id | Native save format keeps target good id, not old tag field `#0x20`. |

Runtime evidence:

| Native address | Hex | Decoded behavior | Interpretation |
|---:|---|---|---|
| `HandleScript@0x0070b880`-`0x0070b884` | `22 21`; `52 5e`; `03 92` | load object `#0x22` into a local target id | `#0x22` is the good id to remove. |
| `HandleScript@0x0070b944`-`0x0070b95c` | calls `HistoryGood::GetGoodID`, compares with target id, then calls `HistoryGood::isNormalGood` | inventory-list search by good id | The op scans existing goods rather than creating a new good. |
| `HandleScript@0x0070bb48`-`0x0070bb50` | `01 21`; `49 42`; `bl HistoryGood::SetGoodID(int)` | calls `SetGoodID(-1)` | Matching good slot is cleared. |
| `HandleScript@0x0070bab6` / `0x0070badc` | calls `History::minusActorWeaponLevelOfSeid` / `minusActorCoatLevelOfSeid` | weapon/coat equipment side effects | Removing equipped goods updates actor SEID-derived effects. |
| `HandleScript@0x0070bac0` / `0x0070bae6` / `0x0070bb3a` | calls `HistoryActor::clearTempHP_MP(0/1/2)` | clears temp HP/MP for affected equip slot | Equipment removal has actor-stat side effects. |
| `HandleScript@0x0070bb5e` | calls `HistoryActor::UpdataGoodEffect(1)` | refreshes actor good effects | Confirms this is not a passive text/list operation. |
| `ScriptGoodThrow::IsMaxLevel@0x0070b812`-`0x0070b840` | calls `HistoryGood::GetGoodLevel`, `HistoryGood::GetGoodExp`, compares against global max level / exp thresholds | max-level guard/helper | Quantity/source policy depends partly on inventory/equipment and max-level state. |

Strict shape scan over `Scenes/*.eex_new`:

| Shape | Matches | Files | Distribution |
|---|---:|---:|---|
| `6f 00 17 00 <good_id:s16>` | `22066` | `78` files | prefix split `R=22063`, `S=3`; `244` distinct good ids; range `29..1172`; top ids `333=1225`, `400=1170`, `332=1045`, `268=445`, `267=434`. |

Table lineage:

| Table | Evidence | Verdict |
|---|---|---|
| `json/dic_item.json` | `1199` rows with key `good_id`; all `244 / 244` distinct `0x006f` ids resolve; missing ids `0`. Example ids: `333`, `400`, `332`, `813`, `1172`, `29`, `35`. | Same table namespace; text names in the table remain mojibake, but id linkage is intact. |

Representative records:

| File offset | Hex | Decoded fields | Interpretation |
|---|---|---|---|
| `Scenes/R_00.eex_new@0x575f6` | `6f 00 17 00 2d 03` | tag `0x0017`, good id `813` | Remove/throw `dic_item.good_id=813`. |
| `Scenes/R_00.eex_new@0x6aeb0` | `6f 00 17 00 4d 01` | tag `0x0017`, good id `333` | Remove/throw `dic_item.good_id=333`. |
| `Scenes/R_00.eex_new@0x873eb` | `6f 00 17 00 90 01` | tag `0x0017`, good id `400` | Remove/throw `dic_item.good_id=400`. |
| `Scenes/S_03.eex_new@0x2460b` | `6f 00 17 00 59 00` | tag `0x0017`, good id `89` | S-side rare good-removal record. |
| `Scenes/S_60.eex_new@0x216da` | `6f 00 17 00 1d 00` | tag `0x0017`, good id `29` | S-side rare good-removal record. |

Status: structure is green for numeric inventory/equipment `RemoveGoodById` / `ThrowGood` preservation. The target id namespace is `dic_item.good_id`. The remaining uncertainty is not byte recovery; it is the exact source/quantity policy when multiple matching goods exist, max-level guard behavior, and whether old tag `0x0017` is purely a format/type marker.

### 4.8.10 Probability Condition: `0x006e ScriptTestProbality`

`0x006e` is a random-threshold condition. Native execution calls `History::getRand()`, compares the result with a threshold int, writes the boolean result into the current test-result slot, then returns according to `Script::get_test_result`.

Field shape in old EEX:

```text
6e 00
  04 00
  <threshold:i32>
```

Native field retention and execution:

| Native address | Hex | Decoded behavior | Interpretation |
|---:|---|---|---|
| `ScriptTestProbality::initPara@0x0070b6f8` / `0x0070b6fe` | `34 f7 f5 fc`; `28 84` | `bytesToShort(payload+0)` -> object `#0x20` | Old tag/control field; strict records use `0x0004`. |
| `ScriptTestProbality::initPara@0x0070b702` / `0x0070b706` | `34 f7 e1 fc`; `68 62` | `bytesToInt(payload+2)` -> object `#0x24` | Random threshold. |
| `ScriptTestProbality::initPara@0x0070b708`-`0x0070b70a` | `a0 1d`; `70 bd` | returns `payload + 6` | Fixed payload length `0x06`. |
| `HandleScript@0x0070b6b8` | `78 f7 d6 fa` | calls `History::getRand()` | Runtime random source. |
| `HandleScript@0x0070b6be`-`0x0070b6ca` | `61 6a`; `88 42`; `00 db`; `00 22` | load threshold `#0x24`; success byte remains `1` only when `rand < threshold` | Exact condition is `getRand() < threshold`. |
| `HandleScript@0x0070b6cc`-`0x0070b6d0` | `5a 55`; calls `Script::get_test_result` | writes result to current condition stack slot, then returns inverted/fail-closed value | This is a branch/test op, not a standalone action. |
| `History::getRand@0x00683cca`-`0x00683cd0` | `63 23`; `e6 60`; `23 61` | initializes lower/range state to `0` and `0x63` (`99`) on default path | Default behavior is compatible with percent-like thresholds `0..99`; keep threshold numeric if global range is altered. |

Strict shape scan over `Scenes/*.eex_new`:

| Shape | Matches | Files | Distribution |
|---|---:|---:|---|
| `6e 00 04 00 <threshold:i32>` with threshold `0..10000` | `1202` | `162` files | prefix split `S=1058`, `R=144`; threshold range `0..80`; top thresholds `50=676`, `40=339`, `25=41`, `33=35`, `0=24`, `20=20`. |

Representative records:

| File offset | Hex | Decoded fields | Interpretation |
|---|---|---|---|
| `Scenes/R_05.eex_new@0x03c29` | `6e 00 04 00 2a 00 00 00` | threshold `42` | Pass when `History::getRand() < 42`. |
| `Scenes/R_129.eex_new@0x0dc51` | `6e 00 04 00 32 00 00 00` | threshold `50` | Pass when random value is below `50`. |
| `Scenes/R_129.eex_new@0x10b89` | `6e 00 04 00 28 00 00 00` | threshold `40` | Pass when random value is below `40`. |
| `Scenes/R_129.eex_new@0x0dbfd` | `6e 00 04 00 19 00 00 00` | threshold `25` | Pass when random value is below `25`. |
| `Scenes/R_05.eex_new@0x04274` | `6e 00 04 00 00 00 00 00` | threshold `0` | Always false under default nonnegative RNG range. |

Status: structure is green for a numeric `RandomPercentLessThan` / probability gate condition. The byte behavior is proven as `rand < threshold`; the only caution is that `History::getRand` has a configurable global range, so a converter should preserve the raw threshold and treat percent labels as a default-range interpretation.

### 4.8.11 Native-Only Actor Not-Same Condition: `0x005e ScriptTestActorNotSame`

`0x005e` is implemented in `libMyGame.so`, but this MOD package does not use it as a real EEX command. Treating raw `5e 00` byte pairs as commands is wrong: the exact-end walker that matches `316 / 316` files and `1608 / 1608` sections finds `0` command-offset records for `0x005e`, while raw search hits are payload collisions.

Native field retention:

| Native address | Hex | Decoded behavior | Interpretation |
|---:|---|---|---|
| `ScriptTestActorNotSame::initPara@0x0071d29a` / `0x0071d2a0` | `22 f7 24 ff`; `28 84` | `bytesToShort(payload+0)` -> object `#0x20` | Old tag/control field. No package record proves observed tag values because command count is `0`. |
| `ScriptTestActorNotSame::initPara@0x0071d2a4` / `0x0071d2aa` | `22 f7 1f ff`; `68 84` | `bytesToShort(payload+2)` -> object `#0x22` | First actor id / actor-selector field. |
| `ScriptTestActorNotSame::initPara@0x0071d2ae` / `0x0071d2b4` | `22 f7 1a ff`; `a8 84` | `bytesToShort(payload+4)` -> object `#0x24` | Old tag/control field. |
| `ScriptTestActorNotSame::initPara@0x0071d2b8` / `0x0071d2bc` | `22 f7 15 ff`; `e8 84` | `bytesToShort(payload+6)` -> object `#0x26` | Second actor id / actor-selector field. |
| `ScriptTestActorNotSame::initPara@0x0071d2be`-`0x0071d2c2` | `20 1c`; `08 30`; `70 bd` | returns `payload + 8` | Fixed old-EEX payload length is `0x08`. |
| `saveScript@0x0071d2d4`-`0x0071d2e4` | `e9 5e`; `e9 5e`; calls `writeShort` | writes object `#0x22`, then object `#0x26` after command id | Native save format keeps the two selector fields, not old tag fields `#0x20/#0x24`. |

Runtime behavior:

| Native address | Hex | Decoded behavior | Interpretation |
|---:|---|---|---|
| `HandleScript@0x0071d326`-`0x0071d334` | `22 23`; `c5 5e`; `26 23`; `c0 5e`; `28 1a`; `42 42`; `42 41`; `50 42` | when battle/context pointer is absent, load `#0x22`, load `#0x26`, subtract, and return the nonzero test result | Simple path is `selectorA != selectorB`. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071d362`-`0x0071d36c` | `22 22`; `b0 5e`; literal `0xfffffc00`; compare `<= 4` | normalize first selector against `0x0400..0x0404` special-selector family | Same special selector family seen in position/area checks. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071d390`, `0x0071d3ca`, `0x0071d420`, `0x0071d490`, `0x0071d4cc`, `0x0071d524` | calls `History::FindActor(short)` | resolve concrete actor ids while scanning selector groups | Battle-context path expands selector/group membership rather than comparing raw shorts only. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071d3ac`-`0x0071d3b2` | `89 30`; `03 78`; `01 2b`; `4b d8` | read `HistoryActor+0x89` and accept side byte `<= 1` for one selector branch | Selector branch matching own/friend side-byte behavior. |
| `HandleScript@0x0071d3e6`-`0x0071d3ec` | `89 30`; `03 78`; `02 2b`; `2e d1` | read `HistoryActor+0x89` and accept side byte `== 2` | Enemy-side selector branch. |
| Literal pool `0x0071d5b8`, `0x0071d5c0`, `0x0071d5c4` | `00 fc ff ff`; `8c 44 01 00`; `03 04 00 00` | `-0x400`, `History+0x1448c`, and selector literal `0x0403` | Active-cursor convention is present in this handler too. |

Exact corpus negative evidence:

| Probe | Result | Evidence |
|---|---:|---|
| Exact-end walker command count | `0` | The walker still reaches `1327396` records, `9194` zero skips, `175400` child skips, and all `1608` section ends exactly. |
| Raw `5e 00` scan | `311` hits in `101` files | None are exact command offsets; samples in section 4.14 show `5e 00` inside `0x0030` / `0x0032` payload spans. |

Status: native structure is green for a future numeric `ActorSelectorNotSame` / selector-set disjoint condition, but this package contributes no real `0x005e` records. The high-level label should remain native-only until another package supplies command-offset samples with payload bytes.

### 4.8.12 PK Screen Flow Ops: `0x005f` / `0x0061` / `0x0062`

`0x005f`, `0x0061`, and `0x0062` are PK-screen presentation/flow commands. Native handlers route through `PKScreen`, not `HistoryActor::SetCurHp`, battle deployment, win/loss, or normal battle actor state mutation. They should be preserved as PK/cutscene operations rather than converted as generic battle death logic.

Field shape in old EEX:

```text
5f 00                         # ScriptPKEnd, zero payload
61 00                         # ScriptPKShowKO, zero payload
62 00 26 00 <pk_actor_slot:s16> # ScriptPKActorDie, fixed payload 0x04
```

Native field retention and execution:

| Command | Native address | Hex | Decoded behavior | Interpretation |
|---:|---:|---|---|---|
| `0x005f` | `ScriptPKEnd::initPara@0x0071d5c8` | `10 1c`; `70 47` | returns incoming payload offset | Zero old-EEX payload. |
| `0x005f` | `HandleScript@0x0071d5da`-`0x0071d5e8` | `58 f7 9d fc`; `0f 21`; `57 f7 d3 fa`; `cf f7 46 fe` | `Chess::getInstance`, `getScreenByID(0x0f)`, call `PKScreen::PKEnd` | Ends/cleans up PK screen flow. |
| `0x005f` | `HandleScript@0x0071d5ec`-`0x0071d600` | `03 21`; `57 f7 cb fa`; `01 21`; `32 f0 fe fa` | get screen id `3`, then `CommonScence::setPanelVisible(1)` | Restores common scene panel visibility after PK. |
| `0x0061` | `ScriptPKShowKO::initPara@0x0071d7f4` | `10 1c`; `70 47` | returns incoming payload offset | Zero old-EEX payload. |
| `0x0061` | `HandleScript@0x0071d806`-`0x0071d814` | `58 f7 87 fb`; `0f 21`; `57 f7 bd f9`; `cf f7 48 fd` | get PK screen and call `PKScreen::PKShowKO` | Displays PK KO presentation. |
| `0x0062` | `ScriptPKActorDie::initPara@0x0071d87a` / `0x0071d880` | `22 f7 34 fc`; `28 84` | `bytesToShort(payload+0)` -> object `#0x20` | Old tag/control field; all exact records use `0x0026`. |
| `0x0062` | `ScriptPKActorDie::initPara@0x0071d884` / `0x0071d888` | `22 f7 2f fc`; `68 84` | `bytesToShort(payload+2)` -> object `#0x22` | PK actor slot/index field. |
| `0x0062` | `HandleScript@0x0071d85a`-`0x0071d85e` | `22 23`; `e1 5e`; `cf f7 8e fc` | load `#0x22`, call `PKScreen::PKActorDie(short)` | Drives PK actor death presentation for a slot. |
| all three | handler tail at `0x0071d604` / `0x0071d818` / `0x0071d862` | `60 69`; `43 1c`; `63 61`; `01 23`; `18 1a` | increment object `#0x14`, return `1 - previousCounter` | One-shot/timing behavior; exact scheduler meaning remains a runtime-flow label, not a payload field. |

Exact-end corpus scan:

| Command | Matches | Files | Payload distribution | Common neighbors |
|---:|---:|---:|---|---|
| `0x005f ScriptPKEnd` | `185` | `99` | fixed zero payload | Usually follows PK talk/action/die plus delay; next command is `Base0` in `184 / 185` records. |
| `0x0061 ScriptPKShowKO` | `184` | `99` | fixed zero payload | Commonly follows `0x0068 ScriptPKStart` and two `0x0060 ScriptPKActorAppear` records; next commands are usually delay/action/talk. |
| `0x0062 ScriptPKActorDie` | `68` | `47` | tag `0x0026` in `68 / 68`; slot values `1=62`, `0=6` | Usually precedes delay or `0x005f ScriptPKEnd`. |

| File offset | Hex | Decoded fields | Interpretation |

| `Scenes/S_04.eex_new@0x06379` | `62 00 26 00 00 00` | tag `0x0026`, PK actor slot `0` | Alternate PK actor-slot death presentation. |

Status: these three commands are structurally green as PK-screen flow/presentation ops. The remaining uncertainty is the human label for `0x0062 #0x22` slot values `0/1` and the precise script scheduler meaning of the one-shot return counter. They are not evidence for normal battle HP, defeat condition, or actor removal semantics.

### 4.8.13 PK Screen Actor/Text/Attack Ops: `0x0060` / `0x0063` / `0x0064` / `0x0065` / `0x0066` / `0x0068`

These commands are the body of the PK-screen sequence around `0x005f/0x0061/0x0062`: start screen, introduce slots, show slot dialogue, run slot actions, and run two attack-animation phases. Native handlers route to `PKScreen`, not to `HistoryActor`, `BattleActor::setState`, win/loss checks, or HP mutation.

Field shape in old EEX:

```text
68 00 02 00 <pk_arg0:s16> 02 00 <pk_arg1:s16>                    # ScriptPKStart
60 00 26 00 <slot:s16> 05 00 <utf8-nul> 4c 00 <appear_tail:s16>   # ScriptPKActorAppear
63 00 26 00 <slot:s16> 05 00 <utf8-nul> 26 00 <talk_tail:s16>     # ScriptPKActorTalk
64 00 26 00 <slot:s16> 4c 00 <action:s16>                        # ScriptPKActorAction
65 00 26 00 <slot:s16> 4d 00 <attack_arg:s16> 26 00 <target:s16>  # ScriptPKActorAttack1
66 00 26 00 <slot:s16> 4e 00 <attack_arg:s16> 26 00 <target:s16>  # ScriptPKActorAttack2
```

Corpus scan method: strict PK tag-shaped scan over all `316` `Scenes/*.eex_new` files. Controls: `0x0060` strict count `370` and `0x0068` strict count `185` match the native exact-end walker controls from section 4.14; raw zero-payload scans for `0x005f/0x0061` produce false positives, so zero-payload commands still use the exact-end counts in section 4.8.12 rather than raw scan counts.

Strict PK-shaped corpus distribution:

Status: these six commands are structurally green as PK-screen presentation/dialogue/attack operations. Text fields are readable UTF-8 in the raw bytes; GBK/GB18030 are the wrong direct decoders for these samples. Remaining uncertainty is the human visual label for action values `0..13`, attack arg values `0..4`, PK constructor args, and whether slots `0/1` should be named left/right, attacker/defender, or another screen-local role.

### 4.8.14 Late Utility / Control Ops: `0x006c` / `0x0070` / `0x0071` / `0x0072` / `0x0073` / `0x0074` / `0x0075` / `0x0076` / `0x0079` / `0x007b` / `0x007c`

This pass fixes a probe bug before drawing conclusions: after `ELFFile(f)`, the temporary Python disassembler must `seek(0)` before reading the raw `.so` bytes. The evidence below uses the corrected buffer. Older scratch output from the unseeked buffer is discarded and is not used as evidence.

Old EEX field shape from native `initPara`:

```text
6c 00 <oldTag0:s16> <source_actor:s16> <oldTag1:s16> <target_actor:s16>
70 00 <oldTag0:s16> <source_actor:s16> <oldTag1:s16> <target_actor:s16> <oldTag2:s16> <packed_arg:int32>
71 00 <oldTag0:s16> <packed_arg:int32>
72 00 <oldTag0:s16> <mode:int32> <stringTag:s16> <utf8-nul>
73 00 <0x22 bytes of old tag/value fields>
74 00 <oldTag0:s16> <value:s16>
75 00 <oldTag0:s16> <actor:s16> <oldTag1:s16> <image_or_value:s16>
76 00 <oldTag0:s16> <packed_arg:int32>
79 00 <lhsSource:s16-tagged> <lhsValue:int32> <cmp:s16-tagged> <rhsSource:s16-tagged> <rhsValue:int32>
7b 00
7c 00
```

Status: these late commands are not one opaque blob. `0x006c`, `0x0070`, `0x0075`, and `0x0079` have recoverable structure and real runtime behavior. `0x0072` has intact UTF-8 payloads but its mode-specific helper semantics need a dedicated pass. `0x0071` and `0x0073` are structurally parseable but handler-no-op in this native build. `0x007b/0x007c` are especially important to keep fail-closed: the old EEX command has zero payload, while the handler consumes runtime/default fields, so an automatic converter cannot invent actor or good ids from surrounding bytes.

### 4.8.15 Actor Ability and Flag Writes: `0x0038 ScriptSetActorAbility` / `0x000b ScriptSetValue`

This pass pulls two high-frequency write opcodes out of the unknown bucket. Both have canonical old-EEX tag tuples whose record counts match the exact-end native-mode scan, so the rows below are command-offset evidence, not raw byte-hit guesses.

Representative `0x000b` records:

| File / offset | Hex | Decode result |
|---|---|---|
| `R_00.eex_new@0x5743c` | `0b 00 04 00 2d 01 00 00 27 00 00 00` | variable id `301`, set flag `0`. |
| `R_00.eex_new@0x57468` | `0b 00 04 00 2d 01 00 00 27 00 01 00` | variable id `301`, set flag `1`. |
| `S_00.eex_new@0x5a9a` | `0b 00 04 00 91 01 00 00 27 00 01 00` | variable id `401`, set flag `1`. |
| `S_00.eex_new@0x7ad5` | `0b 00 04 00 e6 00 00 00 27 00 00 00` | variable id `230`, set flag `0`. |

Status: `0x0038` and `0x000b` are both structure-green. `0x0038` is a high-volume actor stat/HP/MP/level/image-field mutation command; `0x000b` writes condition/global flag bytes that are later consumed by the `0x0005 ScriptTestValue` true/false lists. The remaining work is naming every variable id and the human labels for native stat names such as explosion/fortune, not recovering byte structure.

### 4.8.16 Economy, Goods, Army, and Visibility Ops: `0x0037/0x003a/0x003b/0x003d/0x003e/0x004c`

This pass separates a useful cluster of economy / goods / actor-availability commands from raw byte collisions. Canonical counts below are only promoted when the old-EEX tag tuple either matches an exact-end command count or has a native save/init shape strong enough to avoid the obvious payload collisions. `0x003e ScriptGoodSet` is now promoted only through exact command offsets from the native-mode walker: raw `3e 00` hits remain collision-heavy and must not be used as corpus semantics.

Native field shapes:

| Command | Native evidence | File payload fields |
|---|---|---|
| `0x0037 ScriptMoneyTest` | `initPara@0x00715e25` stores shorts to `#0x20/#0x22/#0x24`, int to `#0x2c`, shorts to `#0x28/#0x26`, returns `payload + 0x0e`; handler `@0x00715cfd` clears the current condition byte, source `0` calls `History::GetMoney@0x0068460d`, then compares against `#0x2c`. | `28 00 <source:u16> 04 00 <threshold:i32> 24 00 <cmp:u16>`. Comparator: `0` passes when value `>= threshold`, `1` passes when value `< threshold`, `2` passes when value `== threshold`. |
| `0x003a ScriptMoneyChange` | `initPara@0x0071667d` stores shorts to `#0x20/#0x22/#0x24/#0x26/#0x28`, int to `#0x2c`, returns `payload + 0x0e`; handler `@0x0071654d` reaches `History::GetMoney@0x0068460d` / `History::SetMoney@0x00684649` on source `0`. | `28 00 <source:u16> 34 00 <op:u16> 04 00 <value:i32>`. Op enum: `0` assign, `1` add, `2` subtract. Non-money sources remain numeric; source `2` has bounded `0..100` behavior. |
| `0x003b ScriptArmyChange` | `initPara@0x00716eb1` reads six shorts and returns `payload + 0x0c`; `saveScript@0x00716efe` writes command id plus retained `#0x22/#0x26/#0x2a` only (`38 b5 ... 22 23 e9 5e ... 26 23 e9 5e ... 2a 23 e9 5e`). R `HandleRScript@0x0071672c` consumes all three retained fields; battle `HandleScript@0x007167d8` consumes actor plus `#0x26` and did not show a direct `#0x2a` use in this pass. | `02 00 <actor-or-special:u16> 0e 00 <army-state/action:u16> 3e 00 <mode/order:u16>`. R-side `0` = `ArmyCome` path, `1` = conditional return/come path, `255` = `ArmyLeave` path; S-side `#0x26` maps to battle actor state bytes `0/1/2`. |
| `0x003d ScriptGetGood` | `initPara@0x00716f93` reads eight shorts and returns `payload + 0x10`; `saveScript@0x00716ff9` writes retained `#0x22/#0x26/#0x2a/#0x2e`; handler `@0x00717321` constructs `HistoryGood` and calls battle get-item presentation/state paths. | `17 00 <good_id:u16> 49 00 <arg0:i16> 26 00 <arg1:u16> 02 00 <actor/list:u16>`. First retained value is a `dic_item.good_id`. |
| `0x003e ScriptGoodSet` | `initPara@0x0071798d` reads twelve shorts and returns `payload + 0x18`; `saveScript@0x00717a23` writes retained `#0x22/#0x26/#0x2a/#0x2e/#0x32/#0x36`; handler `@0x00717649` calls `HistoryActor::UpdataGoodEffect@0x0068f745`, `HistoryActor::SetDefaultGood@0x0069025d`, `HistoryGood` constructors, and equipment/good level helpers. | `02 00 <actor-or-hid:u16> 3b 00 <slot0-good:u16> 49 00 <slot0-level-or-policy:u16> 3c 00 <slot1-good:u16> 49 00 <slot1-level-or-policy:u16> 3d 00 <slot2-good:u16>`. Field tags and values are separated; slot labels are still conservative. |
| `0x004c ScriptSetActorVisible` | `initPara@0x00719a79` stores shorts to `#0x20/#0x22/#0x24/#0x26/#0x28`, int to `#0x2c`, returns `payload + 0x0e`; handler `@0x007198fd` resolves `#0x26` through the negative-selector alias path when needed, clears actor active/visible fields, centers the actor, then calls `InitAbilityForRevive@0x00691a45`. | `40 00 <mode:u16> 02 00 <actor-selector:i16> 04 00 <list-index-or-arg:i32>`. |

The remaining `0x003b` work is naming actor `0`, mode/order values such as `91/4/29/30`, and the exact user-facing distinction between the R roster helper paths and S battle-list state bytes. `0x003e` remains semantic-slot-yellow: exact command offsets and field layout are isolated, and the handler clearly mutates goods/equipment/default-good state, but automatic mapping still needs human labels for slot policy, empty/default behavior, and level helper semantics. Other open work is naming non-money counters, `ScriptGetGood` auxiliary args, `ScriptGoodSet` slot policy, and `ScriptSetActorVisible` mode/list semantics.

### 4.8.17 Value Table Operations: `0x0077 ScriptValueOperation` / `0x0078 ScriptValueIntValuation`

This pass pulls the value-table evidence into a dedicated ledger. Earlier sections already proved that negative actor selectors can read the persisted `History+0x40c0` alias/value array; this section isolates the writer/valuation opcodes that mutate or classify through that same numeric state. Neither command has a string payload, so text encoding is not the risk here.

Native field shapes:

| Command | File payload fields | Native decode / runtime evidence |
|---|---|---|
| `0x0077 ScriptValueOperation` | `51 00 <targetNamespace:u16> 04 00 <targetSlot:i32> 53 00 <op:u16> 52 00 <rhsSource:u16> 04 00 <rhsValue:i32>` | `initPara@0x0070eea9` reads shorts to `#0x20/#0x22/#0x24`, int to `#0x28`, shorts to `#0x2c/#0x2e/#0x30/#0x32/#0x34`, int to `#0x38`, and returns `payload + 0x18`. `saveScript@0x0070ef27` preserves semantic fields `#0x22/#0x28/#0x2e/#0x32/#0x38`. |
| `0x0077` target and op enum | target namespace `#0x22`, slot `#0x28`, op `#0x2e` | Observed target namespace is always `2`. Native handlers for this namespace write `History+0x40c0 + #0x28*4`. `HandleScript@0x0070f066` switch table maps `#0x2e`: `0 add`, `1 subtract`, `2 assign`, `3 multiply`, `4 integer divide`, `5 modulo`. Divide calls `__aeabi_idiv`; modulo calls `__aeabi_idivmod`. |
| `0x0077` RHS source | source `#0x32`, value `#0x38` | `getNum2@0x0070efa0` selects RHS. Case `0` returns literal `#0x38`. Case `4` reads `*(History + (#0x38 + 0x1030) * 4)`, equivalent to `History+0x40c0 + #0x38*4`. Cases `1/2/3/5` are native-structural but not exercised by the current likely-record corpus scan. |
| `0x0078 ScriptValueIntValuation` | `04 00 <value:i32> 54 00 <mode:u16> 02 00 <actorSelector:i16> 55 00 <field:u16>` | `initPara@0x0070fac7` reads short/int and selector shorts through `#0x20/#0x24/#0x28/#0x2a/#0x2c/#0x2e/#0x30/#0x32`, returns `payload + 0x12`, and `saveScript@0x0070fb2f` preserves `#0x24/#0x2a/#0x2e/#0x32`. |
| `0x0078` valuation mode | mode `#0x2a`, actor selector `#0x2e`, field/classifier `#0x32` | `HandleScript@0x0071098e` calls `valuation2@0x00710241` when `#0x2a != 0`; otherwise it follows `valuation1`. `valuation2@0x00710262` switches on `#0x32`; field `32` reaches the side-byte reclassification path. Runtime classifier values `7/8/9/10` write actor side byte `+0x89/+0x8a` to `0/1/4/4` respectively, with actor field `+6` set to `1/2/0/0`. |

Canonical corpus distribution:

| Command | Raw windows | Canonical shape | Canonical count | Files | Key field distributions |
|---|---:|---|---:|---:|---|
| `0x0077` | `38514` | `(51,04,53,52,04)` | `36998` | `273` | `#0x22`: `2=36998`; op `#0x2e`: assign `30614`, add `6208`, subtract `64`, divide `62`, modulo `45`, multiply `5`; RHS `#0x32`: literal `36658`, value-table read `340`. |

Status: `0x0077` is structure-green for an integer value-table/history arithmetic op. `0x0078` is structure-green for actor/value valuation and one side-byte reclassification family. Both still need semantic labels for value-table slot namespaces, `valuation1` fields, `valuation2` field labels beyond the proven side-byte writer, and the human meaning of side byte `4`. These are naming/modeling uncertainties, not evidence that the bytes are lost or opaque.

### 4.9 Condition and Branch Runtime Evidence

Branching:

| Native address | Instruction hex | Decoded instruction | Runtime meaning |
|---:|---|---|---|
| `0x007116fe` | `3a f7 43 f9` | `bl ChoiceBox::ChoiceBox(int,char*,int)` | `ScriptShowChoice` creates a runtime choice UI from its string payload. |
| `0x0071173e` | `3a f7 23 f9` | `bl ChoiceBox::ChoiceBox(int,char*,int)` | Same constructor path for the alternate menu/bar state. |
| `0x007118f8` | `44 6a` | `ldr r4,[script,#0x24]` | `ScriptCase` reads its case value from field `#0x24`. |
| `0x0071191e` / `0x00711920` | `8c 42`; `07 d0` | `cmp r4,r1`; `beq` | `ScriptCase` compares `#0x24` against the current choice-stack value. |
| `0x00711922`-`0x0071192e` | `00 20 ... 40 42` | clear result byte, decrement stack/index, return `-1` | Non-matching case fails closed. |
| `0x00711932`-`0x00711938` | `01 21 ... d1 54` | set result byte to `1` | Matching case is structurally separable. |

Status: choice branching is now structurally green: `ScriptShowChoice` supplies UI text, `ScriptCase #0x24` is the branch value. The remaining work is flow-control reconstruction, not byte recovery.

Position and area conditions:

| Native address | Instruction hex | Decoded instruction | Runtime meaning |
|---:|---|---|---|
| `0x0071325c` / `0x0071325e` | `a9 6a`; `2a 6b` | `ldr r1,[script,#0x28]`; `ldr r2,[script,#0x30]` | `ScriptTestActorPos` reads x/y candidate fields. |
| `0x00713266` | `6a f7 9b fe` | `bl History::FindActorPosition(int,int)` | Pos test resolves the actor at that x/y. |
| `0x00713278` / `0x0071327a` | `22 24`; `2b 5f` | `movs r4,#0x22`; `ldrsh r3,[script,r4]` | Field `#0x22` is actor id / side selector. |
| `0x007133ba` / `0x007133c0` | `03 6b`; `3a 6c` | `ldr #0x30`; `ldr #0x40` | `ScriptTestActorArea` iterates y range `#0x30..#0x40`. |
| `0x007133ce` / `0x007133d4` | `bb 6a`; `ba 6b` | `ldr #0x28`; `ldr #0x38` | `ScriptTestActorArea` iterates x range `#0x28..#0x38`. |
| `0x007133ee` | `6a f7 d7 fd` | `bl History::FindActorPosition(int,int)` | Area test scans actors inside the rectangle. |
| `0x00713400` | `b8 5e` | `ldrsh r0,[script,#0x22]` | Area test uses the same actor id / side selector field. |

Selector constants are now partly native-proven:

| Selector | Native evidence | Current interpretation | Status |
|---:|---|---|---|
| `<= 0x03ff` | `ScriptTestActorArea@0x00713402` compares `#0x22` against literal `0x03ff`; direct path compares found actor id with `#0x22`. `ScriptTestActorPos@0x0071327c` does the same direct-id compare before special constants. | Direct actor id / battle actor id. | High for structure, namespace still needs battle-roster label. |
| `0x0400` | Area-only switch case: selector minus `0x0400`, jump-table case 0 reaches success after `FindActorPosition` and actor-state guard. | Any valid actor in area candidate. | Medium; not present in `ScriptTestActorPos`. |
| `0x0401` | Pos path literal `01 04 00 00`; branch reads found actor byte at `+0x89` and accepts `<= 1`. Area case 1 has the same `<= 1` side-byte test. `ScriptDispatchOwn/Friend` write side bytes `0/1`. | Own or friend side byte. | High for byte behavior and side labels `0/1`. |
| `0x0402` | Pos path literal `02 04 00 00`; branch accepts side byte `== 2`. Area case 2 has the same test. `ScriptDispatchEnemy` writes side byte `2`; native enemy/assist counters split that side by `HistoryActor+0x668`. | Enemy-side actor, including enemy and assist subsets. | High for byte behavior; subset split requires a secondary field not present in this selector. |
| `0x0403` | Pos path literal `03 04 00 00`; branch accepts side byte `== 0`. Area case 3 first loads `History+0x1448c`, requires that pointer to be non-null, requires its first halfword to equal `0x0403`, then accepts side byte `== 0`. | Position path: own side byte. Area path: own-side predicate gated by the active-actor cursor. | High for byte behavior; high-level event label still needs visual/context correlation. Do not flatten area `0x0403` to a plain own-side test. |
| `0x0404` | Pos path literal `04 04 00 00`; branch accepts side byte `== 4`. Area case 4 has the same test. | Side-byte-4 class. | High for byte behavior, human label/source still unnamed. |

`0x0403` active-cursor guard evidence:

| Native address | Hex | Decoded behavior | Interpretation |
|---:|---|---|---|
| `ScriptTestActorArea@0x00713426`-`0x0071343e` | `32 68`; `16 4b`; `d3 58`; `00 2b`; `19 88`; `15 4a`; `91 42`; `89 33`; `1b 78`; `00 2b` | Load `History*`, read `*(History+0x1448c)`, null-check it, compare its first halfword with literal `0x0403`, then require that actor pointer's side byte `+0x89 == 0`. | Area selector `0x0403` has an additional active-cursor guard before the own-side byte test. |
| Literal pool | `0x00713484 = 8c 44 01 00`; `0x00713488 = 03 04 00 00` | `0x1448c` offset and `0x0403` selector literal. | The guard is exact at byte level; it is not inferred from names. |
| `BattleScreen::nextActor@0x006cb6a8`-`0x006cb6ac` | `b3 f7 34 fb`; `b8 51` with literal `0x006cb720 = 8c 44 01 00` | Call `History::getNextActiveOwn`, then store returned pointer to `History+0x1448c`. | `History+0x1448c` is an active-actor cursor slot in battle turn flow. |
| `History::getNextActiveOwn@0x0067ed16`-`0x0067ed30` | `37 4b`; `c3 58`; `00 2b`; `59 5e`; `ff f7 66 ff` with literal `0x0067edf4 = 8c 44 01 00` | Read `History+0x1448c`; if non-null, read the cursor actor's first halfword and find its own-list index before scanning the next active actor. | The cursor participates in next-actor iteration, not just a display cache. Sibling functions `getNextActiveEnemy/Friend/Neutral` reference the same offset. |
| `ScriptBattleActorAction@0x0071b644`-`0x0071b658` | `26 4b`; `98 42`; `1a 68`; `25 4b`; `d3 58`; `18 88` with literals `0x0071b6e0 = 03 04 00 00`, `0x0071b6e8 = 8c 44 01 00` | When `#0x22 == 0x0403`, read the active-cursor actor id from `History+0x1448c` and continue with that concrete id. | Confirms `0x0403` is a context-sensitive active actor selector in action handlers. The current strict `0x0050` corpus has no `#0x22=0x0403` records. |
| Corpus shape scan | `0x0025`: selector `0x0403` = `1` record / `1` file; `0x0026`: selector `0x0403` = `4` records / `1` file; `0x0050`: selector `0x0403` = `0` records / `0` files among `7,639` strict tag-shape records. | `S_13.eex_new@0x20237`: `25 00 02 00 03 04 04 00 03 00 00 00 04 00 1a 00 00 00`; `S_139.eex_new@0x216fa`: `26 00 02 00 03 04 04 00 0a 00 00 00 04 00 12 00 00 00 04 00 11 00 00 00 04 00 17 00 00 00`. | Position/area use is real in this package; action-handler active-selector support is native-only in this package. |

Read-only native-payload shape scan over `Scenes/*.eex_new`:

| Command | Shape rule | Matches | Files | Top selectors / fields | Sample evidence |
|---:|---|---:|---:|---|---|
| `0x0025 ScriptTestActorPos` | `25 00 02 00 <selector> 04 00 <x:u16> 00 00 04 00 <y:u16> 00 00` | `1096` | `140` | selector `0x0401=992`, `0x03f9=15`, direct ids `4=11`, `36=9`, `0=7`, `0x0402=6` | `S_00.eex_new@0x22ae9`: `25 00 02 00 01 04 04 00 06 00 00 00 04 00 0d 00 00 00` => selector `0x0401`, x/y `6/13`. |
| `0x0026 ScriptTestActorArea` | `26 00 02 00 <selector> 04 00 <x1> 00 00 04 00 <y1> 00 00 04 00 <x2> 00 00 04 00 <y2> 00 00` | `583` | `115` | selector `0x0401=245`, direct ids `36=37`, `0=32`, `1=32`, `4=30`, `54=16`, `0x0402=14` | `S_00.eex_new@0x28aee`: `26 00 02 00 36 01 04 00 00 00 00 00 04 00 0b 00 00 00 04 00 01 00 00 00 04 00 0c 00 00 00` => selector `0x0136`, rect `(0,11)..(1,12)`. |

Status: coordinate/area byte shape is green. Direct actor ids and selector constants are separable. Side bytes `0/1/2` now have native dispatch evidence (`own/friend/enemy-side`). The `0x0403` area guard is byte-decoded as an active-actor cursor check through `History+0x1448c`, but its high-level scenario label remains deliberately unnamed. Side byte `4` still needs a human label.

Round, action-side, and actor-count conditions:

| Native address | Instruction hex | Decoded instruction | Runtime meaning |

| `0x0067ea66`-`0x0067ea84` | `00 29`; `0c d0`; `2f 8a`; `97 42`; `9f 42`; `6d 8a`; `9d 42`; `9d 42` | `History::getBattleOwnNum(filters)` checks actor `+0x10/+0x12` only when filter flag is nonzero | The shared count helper pattern proves `#0x38=x_min`, `#0x40=y_min`, `#0x48=x_max`, `#0x50=y_max`; filter `0` bypasses range checks. |
| `0x00717db8` / `0x00717dba` | `2e 22`; `a3 5e` | read `#0x2e` | Actor-count comparator enum. |

`ScriptTestActorNum` group selector table:

| `#0x22` | Native count API path | Interpretation |
|---:|---|---|
| `0` | `History::getBattleOwnNum` | own |
| `1` | `History::getBattleFriendNum` | friend |
| `2` | `History::getBattleEnemyNum` | enemy |
| `3` | `History::getBattleAssistNum` | assist |
| `4` | own + friend | own/friend combined |
| `5` | enemy + assist | enemy/assist combined |
| `6` | own + friend + enemy + assist + neutral | all listed battle sides |
| `7` | `History::getBattleNeutralNum` | neutral |

Read-only native-payload shape scan for `0x0041`:

| Evidence item | Value |
|---|---|
| Shape | `41 00 03 00 <group> 04 00 <threshold:u16> 00 00 24 00 <cmp> 3f 00 <filter> 04 00 <v1> 00 00 04 00 <v2> 00 00 04 00 <v3> 00 00 04 00 <v4> 00 00` |
| Matches / files | `834` matches in `136` files. |
| Group counts | `0=247`, `6=228`, `5=169`, `2=86`, `4=69`, `3=34`, `1=1`, `7=0`. |
| Comparator counts | `#0x2e`: `2=470`, `0=204`, `1=160`; native comparator semantics match round tests: `0 >=`, `1 <`, `2 ==`. |
| Filter/range fields | `#0x32`: `1=702`, `0=132`; native treats `0` as no rectangle filter and nonzero as rectangle filter. Bounds are `#0x38=x_min`, `#0x40=y_min`, `#0x48=x_max`, `#0x50=y_max`. |

Status: round/action-side/actor-count structure is green enough for a dumper. Actor-count group enum, comparator enum, threshold, and optional rectangle filter are native-proven. Remaining work is high-level trigger labeling, not byte recovery for this op.

| `0x00717ff4`-`0x00718008` | list iteration, `ldrsh [actor,#8]`, compare `#1` | scans a battle actor list for active/alive state marker | Victory also depends on all actors in one runtime list satisfying actor slot `#8 == 1`. |

Status: `ScriptTestVictory` / `ScriptTestFail` are runtime-global tests with no legacy payload beyond the command id. Exact actor-list labels and state enum names are still unknown.

Generic actor-property/state test:

- `ScriptTestActorState::HandleScript@0x00715a2d` dispatches repeatedly to `TestOneActorState@0x007154d1`.
- `TestOneActorState` switches on `#0x26` and calls `HistoryActor` getters for current/base power, defence, intelligence, explosion, fortune, base/current HP, base/current MP, and actor level.
- Representative evidence: `0x00715740` (`74 f7 1e fd`) calls `HistoryActor::GetCurHp`; `0x00715792` (`74 f7 67 fe`) calls `HistoryActor::GetCurMp`; `0x007157ee` (`74 f7 05 ff`) calls `HistoryActor::GetActorLv`.

`#0x26` property enum from the native jump table in `TestOneActorState`:

| `#0x26` | Getter / field | Current label |
|---:|---|---|
| `0` | `HistoryActor::GetCurPower` | current power |
| `1` | `HistoryActor::GetCurDefence` | current defence |
| `2` | `HistoryActor::GetCurIntellegence` | current intelligence |
| `3` | `HistoryActor::GetCurExplosion` | current explosion |
| `4` | `HistoryActor::GetCurFortune` | current fortune |
| `5` | `HistoryActor::GetBaseHp` | base HP |
| `6` | `HistoryActor::GetBaseMp` | base MP |
| `7` | `HistoryActor::GetCurHp` | current HP |
| `8` | `HistoryActor::GetCurMp` | current MP |
| `9` | `HistoryActor::GetActorLv` | actor level |
| `10` | `HistoryActor::GetBasePower` | base power |
| `11` | `HistoryActor::GetBaseDefence` | base defence |
| `12` | `HistoryActor::GetBaseIntellegence` | base intelligence |
| `13` | `HistoryActor::GetBaseExplosion` | base explosion |
| `14` | `HistoryActor::GetBaseFortune` | base fortune |
| `15` | reads 32-bit `HistoryActor+0xfc`; native image loaders consume the same field | actor image/appearance selector candidate; not used by observed `0x0036` records |

`#0x32` comparator semantics: `0` means value `>= #0x2c`; `1` means value `< #0x2c`; `2` means value `== #0x2c`.

Property `15` native evidence:

| Native address | Instruction hex | Decoded instruction | Runtime meaning |
|---:|---|---|---|

| `0x0065d66a`-`0x0065d672` | `fc 33`; `1a 68`; `9c 33`; `1a 80` | `DSaveHistoryActor::copyFrom` reads `HistoryActor+0xfc` and writes it into the save actor structure | The field is persisted at least through the save actor copy path. |

Read-only native-payload shape scan for `0x0036`:

| Evidence item | Value |
|---|---|
| Shape | `36 00 02 00 <selector> 23 00 <property> 04 00 <threshold:u16> 00 00 24 00 <cmp>` |
| Matches / files | `2749` matches in `156` files. |
