Representative old failures now explained:

| Old failure | Corrected evidence | Status |
|---|---|---|
| `R_00.eex_new` section `1` failed at `0x2864b` inside UTF-8 `玩家切换`. | Section `0x2861c..0x28aad` now exact-end. `0x28620 cmd=0x0002 ScriptChildInfo` sets the native zero-skip flag; `0x28631 cmd=0x0005 ScriptTestValue` has variable length `4 + 2*n1 + 4 + 2*n2`; `0x2863d raw0` consumes the pending skip; `0x28643 Base0` closes the subblock. | Parser bug, not corrupt text or lost structure. |
| `R_01.eex_new` section `3` failed at `0x56be` inside UTF-8 `次日……`. | Section `0x4661..0x6108` now exact-end with `261` records, `34` child/subscript skips, and one zero-skip. The surrounding `0x0069 ScriptCommonInfo` string closes cleanly before the next command. | Parser bug, not corrupt text. |
| `S_00.eex_new` section `0` formerly desynced after deployment. | Section `0x16..0x6d28` now exact-end once `0x0046` uses `20 * 0x34 = 0x410` file bytes and `0x0047` uses `80 * 0x38 = 0x1180` file bytes. | Object-memory stride had been mistaken for file payload length. |

Interpretation: physical EEX bytes are now corpus-wide enumerable. The remaining risk is semantic naming of fields/enums/id namespaces and logical list-to-branch reconstruction, not byte loss or encryption.

### 4.15 Native Logical List Reconstruction Evidence

`DecodeScenes` does more than walk bytes. It first parses physical script objects into one temporary list, while a count table records cumulative end indices for root logical sublists. It then rebuilds handler lists from those count ranges.

Native count-table evidence:

| Native address | Instruction hex | Decoded instruction | Runtime meaning |
|---:|---|---|---|
| `0x00708be8`-`0x00708bfa` | `bl bytesToShort`; `str r0,[sp,#0x34]`; `str r0,[sp,#0x3c]`; `adds r0,#1` | read section root-sublist count and allocate `(count + 1) * 4` bytes | The short at section start is the number of root logical sublists. |
| `0x00708c0a`-`0x00708c18` | allocator + zero fill; `str r0,[sp,#0x2c]` | allocate and clear the count table | `table[0]` starts as zero. |
| `0x00708e3e`-`0x00708e56` | increment `[sp,#0x40]`; if depth is zero, `str r3,[table + blockIndex*4 + 4]` | store cumulative physical record count at `table[blockIndex + 1]` | The table stores cumulative end offsets, not per-block local counts. |
| `0x00708e9a`-`0x00708eb8` | start from `table + rootCount*4`; load `table[i-1]` and `table[i]` | choose one logical sublist range | Each root sublist range is `[table[i-1], table[i])` over the physical script-object list. |
| `0x00708ebe`-`0x00708ed0` | load physical script pointer by index; call `DList::addElement` | copy that range into a new list | Physical objects become grouped logical script lists. |
| `0x00708ed2`-`0x00708f2e` | load rebuilt list size, store `size - 1` into an int vector | save per-root endpoint indices for the rebuilt list | Native keeps a companion endpoint vector for sublist boundaries. |
| `0x00708f3e`-`0x00708f48` | `this->#0x28`; call helper `0x00708a58` | append rebuilt script list to the handler | One rebuilt list is added for the current EEX section. |
| `0x00708f4c`-`0x00708fac` | `this->#0x2c`; grow array; store companion vector | append the endpoint vector | Section list and boundary vector travel together. |

Corpus root-list statistics from the exact-end parser:

| Metric | Value | Evidence |
|---|---:|---|
| Sections scanned | `1608` | All `Scenes/*.eex_new` section headers. |
| Root logical sublists | `9180` | Sum of section-start short values. |
| Average root sublists per section | `5.709` | `9180 / 1608`. |
| Sections with one root sublist | `1251` | Count of section-start short `1`. |
| Max root sublists in one section | `163` | `S_122.eex_new` section `1` and `S_123.eex_new` section `1`. |

Representative count-table samples:

| File / section | Section span | Root sublists | Cumulative count table | Evidence |
|---|---|---:|---|---|
| `R_01.eex_new` section `4` | `0x6108..0x7ee9` | `10` | `[0, 40, 57, 76, 89, 272, 288, 336, 351, 368, 392]` | Ten R-side root lists; first block starts at `0x610a`, `prefix=0x0029`, `cmd=0x0002 ScriptChildInfo`. |
| `R_00.eex_new` section `1` | `0x2861c..0x28aad` | `4` | `[0, 4, 18, 60, 74]` | Four root lists around the `玩家切换` blocks; old failure is now a clean count-table case. |
| `R_00.eex_new` section `8` | `0x3c740..0x9b3e2` | `16` | `[0, 2442, 3898, 3914, 3962, 3975, 3988, 6002, 7247, 8551, 10269, 16416, 21835, 21851, 21867, 21901, 21927]` | Large R chapter section with several huge root lists plus short option/toggle lists. |
| `S_00.eex_new` section `1` | `0x6d28..0x29319` | `59` | starts `[0, 32, 50, 68, 86, 104, 112, 128, 139, 152, 187, 6240, ...]` | Battle event section has many root trigger lists; block `0` starts at `0x6d2a`, `cmd=0x0002`, then `0x003f ScriptTestRound`. |

Interpretation: the old script has a native root-list layer above physical records. This is strong evidence for trigger/list structure, but it is not yet a complete high-level branch tree. Nested `Base1`/`Base0`, `ScriptCase`, `ScriptElse`, and handler endpoint vectors still need a semantic dump before mapping to `ScenarioRunner`.

### 4.16 Default/Base Command Context

`getScriptByCmd` returns base `Script(cmd)` for `0x0010`, `0x001e`, `0x0044`, `0x0049`, `0x0051`, and `0x006a`. Native base `Script::initPara@0x006fecac` returns the incoming payload offset, and base `Script::HandleScript@0x006fecd0` only changes global condition depth for raw `cmd 0` and `cmd 1`; for other command ids it returns `0` with no extra behavior. Therefore these command ids are zero-payload markers under the current native code, but their high-level script-authoring role still depends on context.

Exact-end corpus counts:

| Command | Count | File family | Common neighbors | Current status |
|---:|---:|---|---|---|
| `0x0010` | `0` | none | n/a | Not present in parsed scene corpus. |
| `0x001e` | `778` | R only | most often `0x0031 -> 0x001e -> 0x0009` (`516` hits) | R cutscene marker/no-op candidate; do not name semantically yet. |
| `0x0044` | `156` | S only | most often `0x0002 -> 0x0044 -> 0x0045` (`136` hits) | Battle setup marker before `ScriptSetBattleValue`; zero payload. |
| `0x0049` | `1573` | S only | most often `0x003b -> 0x0049 -> 0x000e` (`794` hits), `0x0069 -> 0x0049 -> 0x000e` (`468` hits) | Battle-fail/end separator candidate; zero payload. |
| `0x0051` | `303` | S only | often after `ScriptTestValue`, before `0x0050`, `0x004f`, `0x0009`, or `Base1` | Battle action separator candidate; zero payload. |
| `0x006a` | `0` | none | n/a | Not present in parsed scene corpus. |

Representative samples:

| Command | File / offset | Hex | Surrounding commands | Status |
|---:|---|---|---|---|
| `0x001e` | `R_00.eex_new@0x29f88` | `1e 00` | `ScriptActorDisappear (0x0031)` -> `0x001e` -> `ScriptDelaySet (0x0009)` | Zero-payload R marker; semantic label unknown. |
| `0x0044` | `S_00.eex_new@0x2f` | `44 00` | `ScriptChildInfo (0x0002)` -> `0x0044` -> `ScriptSetBattleValue (0x0045)` | Zero-payload S setup marker; semantic label unknown. |
| `0x0049` | `S_00.eex_new@0x5b1f` | `49 00` | `ScriptArmyChange (0x003b)` -> `0x0049` -> `ScriptBattleFail (0x000e)` | Zero-payload S fail/end marker candidate. |
| `0x0051` | `S_00.eex_new@0x28c3f` | `51 00` | `ScriptTestValue (0x0005)` -> `0x0051` -> `ScriptActorTalk (0x0014)` | Zero-payload S action/branch marker candidate. |

Raw base command counts under the same exact-end flow: `Base0 (0x0000)=184580`, `Base1 (0x0001)=175400`, `ScriptChildInfo (0x0002)=28034`, `ScriptElse (0x0003)=887`, `ScriptTestAsk (0x0004)=175`, `ScriptTestValue (0x0005)=69361`, `ScriptForceLimit (0x0006)=1338`, `ScriptTestStartBattle (0x0007)=143`.

### 4.17 Condition Stack and Choice Branch Evidence

The condition/branch layer is no longer just structural. Native handlers show a small condition stack and a choice-value stack. The exact high-level tree emission still needs a dumper, but the core byte roles are now separable.

Native handler evidence:

| Native address | Instruction hex | Decoded instruction | Runtime meaning |
|---:|---|---|---|
| `0x006fecd0`-`0x006fecf6` | compare base cmd `1` and `0`; increment/decrement global index | base `Script::HandleScript` | `Base1` opens/increments the condition nesting index; `Base0` closes/decrements it when possible. Other base cmd ids return without special logic. |
| `0x0070989c`-`0x007098a6` | set current condition byte to `1` | `ScriptTestValue::HandleScript` | A `ScriptTestValue` starts as pass. |
| `0x007098b0`-`0x007098d0` | loop `#0x22` entries from list `#0x24`; if referenced byte is zero, write condition byte `0` | first `ScriptTestValue` list | First list is a must-be-true variable list. |
| `0x007098d2`-`0x00709900` | if still true, loop `#0x28` entries from list `#0x2c`; if referenced byte is nonzero, write condition byte `0` | second `ScriptTestValue` list | Second list is a must-be-false variable list. |
| `0x007093f8`-`0x0070940a` | load current condition byte; `rsbs r0,r0,#0` | `ScriptElse::HandleScript` | `Else` passes only when the current condition byte is false; true branch returns `-1`. |
| `0x0071189e`-`0x007118ba` | read short tag at payload `+0`; read short/int value from payload `+2`; return `payload + 6` | `ScriptCase::initPara` | `ScriptCase` payload is `04 00 <case-int-le>`, not a raw int at payload start. |
| `0x007118f8`-`0x00711920` | read `ScriptCase #0x24`; pop/read current choice value; compare | `ScriptCase::HandleScript` | Case value is compared against the current choice stack value. |
| `0x00711922`-`0x00711930` | on mismatch, write condition byte `0`, decrement condition index, return `-1` | `ScriptCase` mismatch | Non-matching cases fail closed and skip their branch body. |
| `0x00711932`-`0x0071193a` | on match, write condition byte `1`, return `0` | `ScriptCase` match | Matching case opens a true branch. |
| `0x007117a8`-`0x00711808` | read string, then two trailing shorts | `ScriptShowChoice::initPara` | Choice record carries display text plus two short fields; text is not the branch target itself. |
| `0x007116fe` / `0x0071173e` | call `ChoiceBox::ChoiceBox` | `ScriptShowChoice::HandleScript` | Runtime UI choice is constructed from the recovered string payload. |

`ScriptTestValue` corpus shape:

| Shape | Count | Meaning |
|---|---:|---|
| `(mustTrue=0, mustFalse=1)` | `60253` | Most common: run when one condition variable is false/not yet set. |
| `(mustTrue=1, mustFalse=0)` | `7227` | Run when one condition variable is true/set. |
| `(mustTrue=1, mustFalse=1)` | `1002` | One required true plus one required false variable. |
| `(mustTrue=0, mustFalse=2)` | `263` | Two variables must be false. |
| `(mustTrue=0, mustFalse=0)` | `244` | Empty condition list; structural/default pass candidate. |

All `69361` `ScriptTestValue` records use field/tag `0x0035` for both lists. Sample:

| File / offset | Hex | Decode result |
|---|---|---|
| `R_00.eex_new@0x28631` | `05 00 35 00 01 00 02 00 35 00 00 00` | `cmd=0x0005`; first tag `0x0035`, mustTrue `[2]`; second tag `0x0035`, mustFalse `[]`. |
| `S_00.eex_new@0x6d49` | `05 00 35 00 01 00 33 00 35 00 01 00 34 00` | `cmd=0x0005`; mustTrue `[0x0033]`; mustFalse `[0x0034]`; follows `ScriptTestRound` in the first tutorial battle block. |
| `S_00.eex_new@0x28c2f` | `05 00 35 00 00 00 35 00 01 00 00 00` | `cmd=0x0005`; mustTrue `[]`; mustFalse `[0]`; precedes victory text/action marker `0x0051`. |

Choice/case corpus shape:

| Item | Count / evidence | Meaning |
|---|---:|---|
| `ScriptShowChoice (0x0012)` | `5404` records | Choice UI text is recoverable. |
| `ScriptCase case=1` | `5404` records | Every observed choice has a first case branch. |
| `ScriptCase case=2` | `5404` records | Every observed choice has a second case branch. |
| `ScriptCase case=3` | `1459` records | Multi-option choices exist. |
| `ScriptCase case=4` | `483` records | Multi-option choices extend beyond 3 choices. |
| `ScriptCase case=5..7` | `435`, `257`, `63` records | Long choice menus exist and are enumerable. |

Concrete R choice trace:

| Offset | Hex | Decode result |
|---:|---|---|
| `R_01.eex_new@0x0866` | `12 00 05 00 e6 ac a3 ... e7 bb 9d 00 02 00 00 00 60 02` | `ScriptShowChoice`; tag `0x0005`; text decodes as two options; trailing shorts `[0x0002, 0x0000]`; child skip consumes `60 02`. |
| `R_01.eex_new@0x088a` | `01 00` | `Base1`; opens a nested branch depth. |
| `R_01.eex_new@0x088c` | `13 00 04 00 01 00 00 00 d2 00` | `ScriptCase`; tag `0x0004`; case value `1`; child skip consumes `d2 00`; branch body gives money and reward text. |
| `R_01.eex_new@0x0996` | `00 00 01 00` | `Base0` then `Base1`; closes case 1 branch and opens the next case branch. |
| `R_01.eex_new@0x099a` | `13 00 04 00 02 00 00 00 74 01` | `ScriptCase`; tag `0x0004`; case value `2`; child skip consumes `74 01`; branch body diverges from case 1. |

`ScriptElse` is rarer but present: `887` records. Samples include `R_22.eex_new@0xbf5e` (`03 00 01 00`), `R_35.eex_new@0x5975` (`03 00 21 00`), and `R_37.eex_new@0x02c8` (`03 00 c3 00`). Each `ScriptElse` is followed by a child/subscript skip short under the exact-end cursor model.

Interpretation: choices and simple condition gates are now structurally green. The remaining gap is emitting a nested semantic tree from `Base1/Base0`, `ScriptCase`, `ScriptElse`, and root-list endpoint vectors without losing fallthrough/skip behavior.

## 5. What Is Decoded Now

The following can be extracted without guessing:

- EEX container framing: magic, version, header size, segment offsets.
- EEX record framing: mixed subblock-start `u16 prefix + u16 cmd` and in-subblock cmd-only records, with native `Script*::initPara` payload advancement.
- Native command class names from `getScriptByCmd` for commands `0x0002..0x007c`, including known default commands.
- Valid UTF-8 strings behind `05 00`.
- R scene title and location: `0x0018`, `0x0017` as `ScriptCommonInfo` variants.
- R/S dialogue messages: `0x0014` as `ScriptActorTalk`.
- Choice option text: `0x0012` as `ScriptShowChoice`; `ScriptCase #0x24` is the branch value, while high-level branch tree reconstruction still needs validation.
- S condition display text and success labels: `0x0019`, `0x001a` as `ScriptCommonInfo` variants.
- Player deployment records after `HEX我军设定`: `0x004b` as `ScriptDispatchOwn`, fixed legacy payload length `0x1a`.
- Player deployment x/y fields: `ScriptDispatchOwn #0x2c/#0x34 -> HistoryActor+0x10/+0x12`, and those actor slots are consumed by `History::CheckPosActor`.
- Own-force roster configuration: `0x004a` as `ScriptConfigOwnForce`, fixed payload `0x2e`, shape `04 <count:int>`, five `0x38` forced/priority selectors, and five `0x39` skip/exclusion selectors. Native `HandleScript` normalizes the ten selectors, calls `History::AddBattleOwn` for the first five when valid, then auto-fills while skipping all ten.
- Negative script actor selectors: observed `0x004a` values `-53..-66` are not corrupted bytes; native remaps them through `History* + (0x102e - selector) * 4`, yielding observed `History` offsets `0x418c..0x41c0`. The formula rewrites to `History+0x40c0 + ((-selector)-2)*4`, so these values are alias indices `51..64` in an int-slot actor-selector alias array. `History::InitHistory@0x006855b0` clears `History+0x40c0` for `0x9c3c` bytes (`0x270f` int slots). `History::getHistory@0x00684ef0` copies `0x270f` ints from `History+0x40c0` into `DSaveHistory+0x124`; `DHistoryParser::DSaveHistory::parseData@0x0065f568` reads the persisted int array into `DSaveHistory+0x124`; `History::ParseHistory@0x006860a6` restores it back to `History+0x40c0`. `ScriptValueOperation` writes live slots through `History+0x40c0 + #0x28*4`; `#0x2e` is the operation enum (`0 add`, `1 subtract`, `2 assign`, `3 multiply`, `4 divide`, `5 modulo`), and used RHS forms are `#0x32=0` literal plus `#0x32=4` history/value-table read. The observed `S_71/S_118` records sit immediately after `出战人员` text and use `#0x2e=2`, `#0x32=0`, `#0x38=2000` to assign literal `2000` into slots `50..64`; the proven `0x004a` consumers currently use the subset `51..64`. The same `0x102e` actor-selector alias table is reused by actor move/disappear/state/deployment/action/relive handlers.
- Value-table arithmetic and valuation ops: `0x0077 ScriptValueOperation` has exact canonical count `36998` with tag shape `(51,04,53,52,04)`, target namespace `#0x22=2` in every canonical record, and a native-proven op enum `0 add`, `1 subtract`, `2 assign`, `3 multiply`, `4 divide`, `5 modulo`. Observed RHS sources are literal (`#0x32=0`, `36658` records) and value-table read (`#0x32=4`, `340` records). `0x0078 ScriptValueIntValuation` has exact canonical count `15054` with tag shape `(04,54,02,55)`; mode `#0x2a=1` enters `valuation2`, and field `#0x32=32` has native evidence for actor side-byte reclassification through runtime classifier values `7/8/9/10`. Slot/classifier names remain open, but the byte fields are separated.
- Friend/enemy roster containers: `0x0046` / `0x0047`, fixed child counts, object-memory strides, and file child lengths (`0x34` / `0x38`), with actor id/index and level fields partially named. Chained deployment-parent boundaries now support `203` `0x0046` parents and `204` `0x0047` parents across S files.
- Equipment records after equipment labels: `0x0048` as `ScriptSetEnemyGoods`, fixed legacy payload length `0x18`; `#0x26/#0x2a` = weapon/id-level policy, `#0x2e/#0x32` = armor/id-level policy, `#0x36` = third equipment slot.
- Retreat/defeat condition records: `0x0036` as `ScriptTestActorState`; common retreat/death predicates are `current HP == 0`, with actor selector namespace still unresolved. Property `15` is exact at byte level (`HistoryActor+0xfc`) and consumed by native actor image/bust loaders, but it is not present in observed strict `0x0036` records.
- Battle action records: `0x004f ScriptBattleActorTurn` has actor/target/fallback-direction/timing fields; `0x0050 ScriptBattleActorAction` has actor/state/delay/tail fields and calls `BattleActor::setState`; `0x0053 ScriptBattleActorLeave` has direct actor mode plus area rectangle mode and calls `BattleActor::setState`.
- `0x0053` area leave selectors: native `getActorList` selector `0` = own side byte `0`, `1` = friend side byte `1`, `2` = enemy subset (`+0x89 == 2` and `+0x668 == 0`), `3` = assist subset (`+0x89 == 2` and `+0x668 == 1`), `4` = own+friend, `5` = enemy+assist, `6` = any actor in rectangle, `7` = side-byte-4 class. Side byte `4` has a proven script-side reclassification path through `ScriptValueIntValuation::valuation2` when resolved classifier values `9/10` are used; its human label is still unproven. In this package, area-mode `0x0053` only uses selectors `2/5/6`.
- Battle actor id namespace: `0x0046/0x0047` child `#0x22` and `0x004f/0x0050/0x0053` direct actor fields share a battle-actor id namespace for enemy/friend actors. Same-file chained roster coverage is `12746 / 20578` direct refs overall and `12372 / 13796` (`89.7%`) when likely own-force low ids `<32` are excluded. Own-force low ids are now tied to `0x004a` roster selection and `0x004b` placement; negative own selectors are tied to persisted and script-written `History+0x40c0` alias-array slots, but the route/party semantic labels for those slots remain unresolved.
- Battle actor state machine: `BattleActor::setState` writes runtime state byte `+0xe0`, normalizes `-1` to `0`, has a native jump table for states `5..27`, and now has call-site evidence for movement (`13`), disappear (`15`), get-item (`20`), and leave variants (`14/16`). `0x0050` script state args form a closed observed set `-1..12` with corpus counts and neighboring action contexts; numeric preservation is safe, but human animation labels are still not proven.
- Scripted actor movement: `0x0032 ScriptActorMove` has a fixed 30-byte tag shape and `5551` strict records in `209` files. Mode, actor/direct selector, list index, target x/y, and direction/facing are separable; battle-side execution calls `BattleActor::GenerateDefaultMove(targetX,targetY)` and then `BattleActor::setState(13)`. Numeric preservation is safe, but mode `-1/0/1` labels, the mode-`1` list identity, and direction/facing labels are still unproven.
- Actor ability/stat writes: `0x0038 ScriptSetActorAbility` has a fixed `0x12` payload and exact canonical count `266953`. Actor id, property selector, op enum, and value are separable. Native C++ setter symbols map property selectors `0..4` to current power/defence/intelligence/explosion/fortune, `5/6` to base HP/MP, `7/8` to current HP/MP with cap/floor behavior, `9` to actor level, `10..14` to base power/defence/intelligence/explosion/fortune, and `15` to direct `HistoryActor+0xfc` image/appearance-related field. Op enum is `0 assign`, `1 add/increase`, `2 subtract/decrease`.
- Economy/counter operations are now byte-decoded for `0x0037 ScriptMoneyTest` and `0x003a ScriptMoneyChange`: both have fixed `0x0e` old-EEX payloads with `28/04/24` or `28/34/04` tag shapes. Source `0` is native-proven money through `History::GetMoney` / `History::SetMoney`; comparator/op enums are separable. Source `1/2` labels remain numeric.
- Army/party availability and visibility operations are now structurally separated: `0x003b ScriptArmyChange` has a fixed `0x0c` payload and exact canonical count `4072`; R-side `0x003b` calls native `ArmyCome` / `ArmyComeReturnToLeave` / `ArmyLeave` paths by `#0x26`, while S-side `0x003b` writes actor state bytes `0/1/2` and moves battle actor list pointers. `0x004c` has a fixed `0x0e` payload and exact canonical count `5486`, resolves actor selectors through the same alias family, clears active/visible fields, centers/updates the actor, and calls `InitAbilityForRevive`. Human labels for `0x003b` mode/order policy, actor `0`, and `0x004c` modes remain open.
- Item grant and actor good/equipment setup operations are now byte-decoded for `0x003d ScriptGetGood` and `0x003e ScriptGoodSet`. `0x003d` has fixed `0x10` payload, exact canonical count `8474`, first retained value as `dic_item.good_id`, and all nonzero observed ids resolve in `json/dic_item.json`. `0x003e` has fixed `0x18` payload, exact command-offset count `249`, stable tuple `(02,3b,49,3c,49,3d)`, actor/hid values resolving in `dic_hero`, and all nonzero slot values after `3b/3c/3d` resolving in `dic_item`. Raw `3e 00` scans still collide heavily, so only exact walker offsets are valid evidence.
- Actor HP/state change: `0x004d ScriptChangeActorState` has a fixed `0x42` tag shape and `1969` strict records in `146` S files. Source mode `0/1/2`, direct/list/area actor targeting, area side selector, op enum, status mask, HP delta, and MP delta are separable. Native execution applies HP through `HistoryActor::SetCurHp`; the MP path exists through `SetCurMp` but this package has `mpDelta=0` for all strict records. Status mask bits are structured and writable, but human ailment/status labels remain unproven.
- Actor AI change: `0x004e ScriptChangeActorAI` has a fixed `0x38` tag shape and `1060` strict records in `122` S files. Mode `0` direct actor and mode `1` area/list targeting are separable; rectangle bounds, selector, AI mode enum `0..6`, AI target actor/selector, and two numeric/coordinate args are retained and written to `HistoryActor+6/+0xa/+0xc/+0xe`. Numeric preservation is safe, but human AI strategy labels and the last two arg labels remain unproven.
- Battle barrier/map-element change: `0x0058 ScriptSetBattleBarrier` has a fixed `0x20` tag shape and `924` strict records in `42` S files. Kind id, add/remove flag, tile value, x/y, delay, and post-delay are separable. Native execution constructs/appends `MapElem` on the add path, finds/removes an existing x/y element on the nonzero-flag path, and can write the tile value into a map byte table. Numeric preservation is safe, but human kind/tile labels remain unproven.
- Battle reward/bonus operation: `0x0059 ScriptSetBattleBonus` has a fixed `0x22` tag shape and `377` strict records in `155` S files. Configured money and up to three reward good ids are separable; all `45` distinct nonnegative good ids resolve to `json/dic_item.json` `good_id`, and `-1` is the empty-slot sentinel. Native execution calls `History::SetMoney`, constructs `HistoryGood` objects from the good ids, and opens `BattleBonus` / `Booty` UI paths. Numeric preservation is safe, but computed base-money policy, per-good extra fields, and the tail flag/value remain unproven.
- Battle presentation highlights: `0x005b ScriptBattleHighlightArea` has a fixed `0x1c` tag shape and `110` strict records in `56` S files; it creates `FogElem` presentation objects over a rectangle and writes visible highlight/camera state. `0x005c ScriptBattleHighlightActor` has a fixed `0x04` tag shape and `77` strict records in `48` files; it resolves a battle actor and calls `History::CenterActor`. These are presentation/focus ops, not evidence for win-condition areas, spawn, reinforcement, or gameplay state mutation. Numeric preservation is safe; only the `0x005b` tail flag's human label remains open.
- Battle max-round operation: `0x005d ScriptSetMaxRound` has a fixed `0x0a` tag shape and `28` strict records in `18` S files. Native execution calls `History::SetMaxRound`; mode `0` sets max round to `extraMaxRound + value`, mode `1` increases max round by value, and native mode `2` would decrease max round by value but is not observed in this package. Numeric preservation is safe; old tag fields `0x0026/0x0034` remain unlabeled.
- Native-only actor not-same condition: `0x005e ScriptTestActorNotSame` has native fixed length `0x08`, retained selector fields `#0x22/#0x26`, a simple no-context `#0x22 != #0x26` path, and battle-context selector expansion through `History::FindActor`. Exact-end corpus count is `0`, and all `311` raw `5e 00` byte hits are payload collisions rather than command offsets.
- PK-screen flow/presentation ops: `0x005f ScriptPKEnd` and `0x0061 ScriptPKShowKO` are zero-payload commands with exact counts `185` and `184`; native handlers call `PKScreen::PKEnd` and `PKScreen::PKShowKO`. `0x0062 ScriptPKActorDie` has fixed `26 00 <slot>` payload, exact count `68`, and calls `PKScreen::PKActorDie(short)`. These are PK-screen ops, not normal battle actor death/state changes.
- Inventory/equipment good removal: `0x006f ScriptGoodThrow` has a fixed `0x04` tag shape and `22066` strict records in `78` files, matching the exact-end command count. The target id is `dic_item.good_id`; all `244` distinct ids resolve in `json/dic_item.json`. Native execution scans `HistoryGood` inventory/equipment slots, clears matches with `HistoryGood::SetGoodID(-1)`, and refreshes actor good effects. Numeric preservation is safe; exact quantity/source priority remains open.
- Battle relive/re-entry: `0x0055 ScriptBattleActorRelive` has a fixed 30-byte tag shape and `1968` strict records in `83` S files; it resolves an actor, requires dead/inactive or leave-state context, writes absolute x/y, calls `FindNearestBlackPos`, restores abilities/state, and validates position. `0x006d ScriptRelaReviveOrMove` has a fixed 38-byte tag shape and `89` strict records in `34` S files; final flag `#0x4a=0` uses reference-actor-relative movement, while nonzero `#0x4a` calls `ActorRevive` for reference-relative relive/re-entry. Direction labels and rare list-source mode labels remain unproven.
- Choice branch structure: `ScriptShowChoice` creates the choice UI, and `ScriptCase #0x24` compares against the current choice-stack value.
- Choice/case pairing: `ScriptShowChoice` count `5404`; `ScriptCase case=1` and `case=2` both appear `5404` times, with cases `3..7` also enumerable for longer menus.
- Simple condition variables: `ScriptTestValue` has two `0x0035` variable lists, a must-be-true list and a must-be-false list; all `69361` records follow this shape.
- Condition/global flag writes: `0x000b ScriptSetValue` has a fixed `0x0a` old-EEX shape and exact canonical count `71834`; it writes byte `0/1` into a global flag table at `base + 0x19b0 + variableId`. This gives the write-side counterpart to `ScriptTestValue` flag-list reads. Variable ids are numeric and alive; human labels remain a separate namespace task.
- Else gates: `ScriptElse` reads the current condition byte and passes only when the prior condition is false.
- Position/area conditions: `ScriptTestActorPos #0x28/#0x30` and `ScriptTestActorArea #0x28/#0x30/#0x38/#0x40` resolve through `History::FindActorPosition`; direct actor ids and selector constants `0x0400..0x0404` are separable, with side bytes `0/1/2` tied to own/friend/enemy-side dispatch evidence and side byte `4` tied to `ScriptValueIntValuation` runtime reclassification. The area-only `0x0403` guard is now byte-decoded as an active-actor cursor check through `History+0x1448c`; its high-level event label remains unnamed.
- Area-condition file length: `0x0026 ScriptTestActorArea` has native fixed payload `0x1c`.
- PK sequence dialogue/actions: `0x0060 ScriptPKActorAppear`, `0x0063 ScriptPKActorTalk`, and `0x0067 ScriptChapterName` have native variable string lengths and close cleanly in the corpus.
- Round/action-side/count conditions: `ScriptTestRound #0x24/#0x2a`, `ScriptTestActionSide #0x22`, and `ScriptTestActorNum` group/count comparators are structurally separable; actor-count group selector `0..7`, threshold `#0x28`, comparator `#0x2e`, and optional rectangle filter `#0x32/#0x38/#0x40/#0x48/#0x50` are native-proven.
- Probability condition: `0x006e ScriptTestProbality` has a fixed `0x06` tag shape and `1202` strict records in `162` files. Native execution calls `History::getRand()` and passes only when `rand < threshold`; default RNG range initializes as `0..99`, so observed thresholds `0..80` are percent-like but should be preserved numerically.
- Victory/fail tests: `ScriptTestVictory` / `ScriptTestFail` are payloadless runtime-global checks for critical actor terminal state, max round, and battle actor list state.
- `DecodeScenes` raw structural flow: `cmd 0/1/2/7` special paths, base `Script(cmd)` retention, virtual `initPara` offset advancement, per-section logical sublist counts, and exact-end physical cursor coverage over all `1608` sections.
- Native root-list count tables: section-start short = root logical sublist count; count table entries are cumulative physical record end indices; all `9180` root sublists are physically enumerable.
- Late utility/control/value ops are structurally separable through `libMyGame.so`: `0x006c ScriptActorAbilityCopy` reads four shorts and copies actor fields from source to target; `0x0070 ScriptAbilityChooseCopy` reads five shorts plus one int and switches on a category arg; `0x0074 ScriptSwitchSavefile` stores a retained short into a save/history field; `0x0075 ScriptAssignSImage` mutates actor image/appearance-related state; `0x0076 ScriptSkipUncondition` passes a retained int to a list/control helper; `0x0077 ScriptValueOperation` mutates integer value-table/history slots with native-proven arithmetic ops; `0x0078 ScriptValueIntValuation` evaluates actor/value fields and can reclassify side bytes through `valuation2`; `0x0079 ScriptTestValuePlus` compares two value sources with native-proven comparators `0 ==`, `1 >=`, `2 <=`. Numeric preservation is safe, but category, visual, list-control, value-slot, and valuation field labels are still open.
- `0x0072 ScriptMsgTransmit` has intact UTF-8 string/list payloads: native `initPara` reads short, int, short, and DString, while `HandleScript` calls `GetStringList`, `SelectActor`, `CallMagic`, and `HPChange` helper paths depending on retained mode. Text bytes are alive; mode-specific helper semantics still need a separate pass.
- `0x0071 ScriptAskEffects` and `0x0073 ScriptActorProperty` are fixed structured records under old EEX, but their current native `HandleScript` paths return no-op. `0x007b ScriptHideBattleActor` and `0x007c ScriptSetGoodImage` have real handler behavior but zero old-EEX payload, so conversion must not invent actor/good ids from following bytes.
- Default/native-unsupported commands are zero-payload base `Script(cmd)` markers under this native build; `0x001e`, `0x0044`, `0x0049`, and `0x0051` have corpus contexts, while `0x0010` and `0x006a` are not present in parsed scene records.

## 6. Still Undecidable / Do Not Guess

| Item | Why unknown | Evidence needed | Impact |
|---|---|---|---|
| Logical script-tree emission | Native count-table structure and choice/case condition behavior are now known. The remaining gap is outputting a complete high-level tree that preserves nested `Base1`/`Base0`, `ScriptCase`, `ScriptElse`, skips, and endpoint vectors. | Emit a semantic dump of root ranges plus nested depth spans and `ScriptCase`/`ScriptElse` ranges; compare several R/S files. | Required before mapping old script blocks to native `ScenarioRunner` branches/triggers. |
| `0x0012` / `ScriptShowChoice` branch mapping | Option text and `ScriptCase` int values are tied to divergent branch effects in `R_01`; cases `1..7` are enumerable. The remaining gap is assigning branch bodies to a final native branch model without losing fallthrough/else behavior. | Validate `ScriptCase`/`ScriptElse` tree output across multi-option R files and compare runtime branch effects. | Required before converting choices to `ScenarioRunner` branches. |
| `0x0015` / `ScriptActorTalk2` fields | Text is clear, but the five leading shorts are not named. | Compare speaker/portrait/side fields across known dialogues and R/S contexts. | Needed for high-fidelity dialogue import. |
| `0x0016`-`0x001a` / `ScriptCommonInfo` variants | Native class is known, but variant-specific meaning is broad. | Group by command id, parent block, and UI/battle context. | Prevents mapping display text as gameplay logic. |
| `0x0036` / `ScriptTestActorState` actor namespace | The property enum is mostly named and common retreat/death predicates are current HP `== 0`, but actor selectors still mix direct ids and special/group constants. Property `15` is no longer a status-field blocker: native code reads exact `HistoryActor+0xfc`, image/bust loaders consume the same field, and current strict `0x0036` corpus has `0` property-15 records. | Establish battle-local actor table or S-script unit roster id namespace; if a future package uses property `15`, preserve it as a numeric image/appearance selector predicate until a visible label is proven. | Critical for high-fidelity death/retreat triggers; property `15` is not a current-package trigger blocker. |
| `0x0038 ScriptSetActorAbility` remaining labels | Byte structure, op enum, and native setter targets are decoded. The unresolved parts are the final human labels for native `Explosion`/`Fortune`, actor selector namespace edge cases for high ids, and the precise UI/content label for property `15` / `HistoryActor+0xfc`. | Correlate setters with hero/job/stat tables and UI labels; compare high actor ids against R/S cutscene actor pools; trace image/bust/sprite consumers of `HistoryActor+0xfc`. | Numeric `SetActorAbility` conversion is possible; polished native model labels need these names. |
| `0x000b ScriptSetValue` variable namespace labels | Write-side behavior is decoded as `globalFlag[variableId] = 0/1`, and `ScriptTestValue` reads variable lists. The unresolved part is the human meaning of the `979` observed variable ids and the reserved ranges such as `9000..9999`. | Group variable writes and tests by section, `ScriptChildInfo` labels, and nearby dialogue; compare with any editor/source labels if available. | Branch conversion can preserve numeric vars; human-readable trigger names and de-duplication need a variable dictionary. |
| `0x0037/0x003a` non-money source labels | Money source `0` is native-proven through `History::GetMoney` / `History::SetMoney`, and comparator/op enums are decoded. Sources `1/2` are real global counters but not named; source `2` has bounded `0..100` behavior. | Trace the literal/global field offsets used in `ScriptMoneyTest` and `ScriptMoneyChange`; correlate source `1/2` records with visible UI gauges, score, merit, or route counters. | Numeric counter conversion is possible; user-facing labels and native model names should stay fail-closed. |
| `0x003b ScriptArmyChange` actor `0` and mode/order labels | Payload structure, exact count, and retained fields `#0x22/#0x26/#0x2a` are decoded. R-side `#0x26=0/1/255` maps to `ArmyCome` / conditional `ArmyComeReturnToLeave` or `ArmyCome` / `ArmyLeave`; S-side `#0x26=0/1/255` maps to actor state bytes `0/1/2`. The unresolved parts are actor `0` (847 records, not in `dic_hero.hid`), R mode/order labels (`91/4/29/30/...`), and polished names for the S battle-list state bytes. | Correlate records with route-party selection blocks, `0x004a` own-force selection, visible roster changes, native `History::ArmyCome` / `ArmyLeave` internals, and UI party screens. | Automatic conversion can preserve actor/state/mode numerically and separate come/leave direction; high-level roster policy labels still need fail-closed handling. |
| `0x003d ScriptGetGood` auxiliary fields | The first retained value is a `dic_item.good_id`, nonzero ids resolve in `dic_item`, and the handler constructs `HistoryGood` / get-item presentation. The unresolved parts are `#0x26/#0x2a/#0x2e` labels, id `0` sentinel meaning, and actor/list selector semantics for values like `1025/1027`. | Correlate samples with visible inventory grants and nearby dialogue; trace the `HandleScript` branches around `BattleActor::setState(20)` and list/actor lookup paths. | Item id conversion is possible; exact presentation/source/actor labels need fail-closed numeric fields. |
| `0x003e ScriptGoodSet` slot policy and default/level helper labels | Exact command-offset corpus records are isolated: `249` records, stable tuple `(02,3b,49,3c,49,3d)`, actor/hid field resolves in `dic_hero`, and nonzero slot fields resolve in `dic_item`. The unresolved part is not byte separation; it is naming slot policy/default behavior and the meaning of `0x49` level/policy values `0/3/4` under native equipment helpers. Raw `3e 00` scans remain unsafe because they produce `36018` payload collisions. | Trace `SetDefaultGood`, equipment level helpers, and visible inventory/equipment effects for samples such as `S_01@0x34e64` and `R_129@0x0e778`. Compare against `0x0048 ScriptSetEnemyGoods`, whose slot order is runtime-proven. | Numeric actor/good slot preservation is possible; high-fidelity native `EquipDefaultGood` labels still need fail-closed policy. Raw byte hits must not drive guesses. |
| `0x004c ScriptSetActorVisible` mode/list labels | Byte structure, exact count, actor selector normalization, active/visible clearing, centering, and `InitAbilityForRevive` call are decoded. The unresolved part is the high-level label for mode `0` versus `1`, and the final int's list/index semantics. | Correlate mode/final-int values with visible actor disappearance/re-entry scenes and battle actor list state; trace the `#0x22 > 0` branch that indexes a battle actor pointer list through `#0x2c`. | Numeric visibility/inactive-state conversion is possible; polished `HideUnit` / `ReviveVisible` / list-index labels need more proof. |
| `0x0048` equipment default/random level policy | Slot order is now runtime-proven, but `<=0` level fields enter engine-derived/random helper paths. | Trace helper calls at `0x7f0258` / `0x7f00c0` and compare with equipment metadata ranges. | Equipment import can preserve explicit ids; exact original random/default level behavior needs fail-closed handling. |
| Position/area actor selector remaining labels | Direct actor ids and selector constants `0x0400..0x0404` are separable. Native dispatch evidence names side bytes `0=own`, `1=friend`, and `2=enemy-side`; enemy-side split into enemy/assist is proven where the secondary `HistoryActor+0x668` field is available. Side byte `4` is script-writable through `ScriptValueIntValuation::valuation2` when resolved classifier values `9/10` are used, but its human label is still not proven. The `0x0403` area-only guard is no longer byte-opaque: it reads `History+0x1448c`, the active-actor cursor slot used by `BattleScreen::nextActor` and `History::getNextActive*`, requires the cursor actor's first halfword to equal `0x0403`, then requires side byte `0`. The remaining gaps are the side-byte-4 human label and the high-level scenario label for this context-sensitive `0x0403` guard. | Correlate side-byte-4 classifier values `9/10` with visible event context; correlate `S_139` area `0x0403` events with the active actor / turn context; confirm whether the cursor halfword `0x0403` represents an own-turn pseudo id, current-actor selector marker, or another battle-state convention. | Required before mapping every area condition to final native trigger vocabulary. |
| `0x0032 ScriptActorMove` mode/facing labels | Byte shape and execution path are decoded: source mode, actor/direct selector, list index, x/y target, and direction/facing are separable, and battle-side movement calls `GenerateDefaultMove` then `setState(13)`. The unresolved part is the human label for mode `-1` vs `0`, the mode-`1` list source identity, and direction/facing values `0..3/-1`. | Visual/runtime correlation for several R/S samples; map rendered facing direction to numeric values; identify the list used by mode `1`. | Required for human-readable `MoveUnit` mapping; numeric fail-closed preservation is already possible. |
| `0x0055` / `0x006d` relive/re-entry labels | Byte shape and execution paths are decoded for absolute relive/re-entry and reference-relative move/relive. The unresolved parts are direction labels, the rare list-source mode used by `0x0055`, native-only list-source branch for `0x006d`, and whether separate reinforcement/spawn commands exist beyond deployment and relive/re-entry. | Visual/runtime correlation for direction values; inspect the rare `0x0055 mode=1` records; continue tracing remaining candidate spawn/reinforcement opcodes. | Numeric fail-closed `ReviveUnit` / relative `MoveUnit` candidates are possible, but full reinforcement vocabulary is not complete. |
| `0x004d ScriptChangeActorState` status flag labels | HP/MP field shape and the `SetCurHp`/`SetCurMp` execution paths are decoded, and mask bytes are separate from HP/MP deltas. The unresolved part is naming mask bits and opRaw values as human ailment/status concepts. Native code writes actor bytes including `+0xc2`, `+0xc3`, `+0xc4`, `+0xc5`, `+0xc8`, `+0x460`, and `+0xcc`, but exact labels are not proven. | Correlate mask bits and opRaw values with visible effects, `paintUnnormalState`, status UI, buff/status tables, and runtime animation/effect codes. | Numeric fail-closed HP/state-change conversion is possible; named `ApplyAilment` / `RemoveAilment` mapping must wait. |
| `0x004e ScriptChangeActorAI` AI enum labels | Direct/area targeting and actor writes are decoded: `aiMode`, `aiTarget`, `aiX`, and `aiY` are written to `HistoryActor+6/+0xa/+0xc/+0xe`. The unresolved part is naming `aiMode 0..6`, mapping every selector value through the Thumb switch helper, and proving whether `aiX/aiY` are coordinates, waypoints, or mode-specific numeric args. | Correlate AI mode values with visible enemy behavior, deployment defaults, and any UI/debug labels; resolve the switch table or compare selector effects across side groups; trace consumers of actor fields `+6/+0xa/+0xc/+0xe`. | Numeric fail-closed `SetActorAi` conversion is possible; human-readable AI strategy mapping is not complete. |
| `0x0058 ScriptSetBattleBarrier` kind/tile labels | Add/remove behavior, x/y, timing, `MapElem` construction/removal, and map-byte write are decoded. The unresolved part is naming kind ids and tile values as human terrain/barrier concepts and deciding which values are visual-only versus movement/terrain-affecting. | Correlate kind/tile values with map graphics, terrain tables, visible barrier events, and pathing/movement changes; trace `MapElem` consumers and map byte table readers. | Numeric fail-closed map-element/barrier conversion is possible; human-readable terrain/barrier mapping is not complete. |
| `0x0059 ScriptSetBattleBonus` extra/tail labels and reward-base policy | Configured money and three good-id slots are decoded, all nonnegative good ids resolve to `dic_item.good_id`, and native execution mutates money / constructs `HistoryGood` rewards. The unresolved parts are the computed base-money component added around `HistoryActor::GetActorLv`, the per-good extra fields `#0x2e/#0x36/#0x3e`, and final tail field `#0x42`. | Trace reward calculation context and UI branches; compare extra/tail values with visible reward screens, good levels, counts, and post-battle inventory changes. | Numeric fail-closed money/good rewards are possible; high-fidelity bonus policy and extra-field labels are not complete. |
| `0x005b ScriptBattleHighlightArea` tail flag label | Native role is decoded as presentation highlight / camera-visible area: it constructs `FogElem` entries, writes screen-highlight rectangle state, and calls `History::CheckPos`. The unresolved part is the human label for tail values `0/1` and exact UI lifetime/mode. | Correlate tail values with visible tutorial highlight behavior and any global highlight rectangle consumers. | Not a blocker for win-condition or reinforcement conversion; preserve as numeric presentation metadata. |
| `0x005c ScriptBattleHighlightActor` actor namespace edge cases | Native role is decoded as actor-centered presentation focus: it calls `History::FindBattleActor` and `History::CenterActor`. The unresolved part is whether R-side actor ids use the same battle actor namespace in every context. | Compare R-side focus samples with visible cutscene actors and battle roster ids. | Not a spawn/reinforcement op; preserve as presentation focus with numeric actor id until namespace labels are complete. |
| `0x005d ScriptSetMaxRound` old tag labels and unobserved decrease mode | Runtime max-round behavior is decoded: mode `0` sets `extraMaxRound + value`, mode `1` increases current max round, and native mode `2` would decrease current max round. The unresolved parts are human labels for old tag0 values `0x0026/0x0034` and why this package has no strict mode-`2` record. | Correlate tag0 values with editor/source forms or a native dumper that proves they are discarded format tags; find another package/sample with mode `2` or prove it is native-only. | Not a blocker for round-limit conversion; preserve mode/value numerically and fail closed on unseen modes. |
| `0x005e ScriptTestActorNotSame` corpus absence and selector-set semantics | Native byte behavior is decoded enough to identify fixed length, retained selector fields, simple `#0x22 != #0x26` path, and battle-context selector expansion. This package has `0` exact command records, so old tag values and real script-authoring contexts are unobserved. | Find a package with exact command-offset `0x005e` records; compare selector pairs against visible trigger behavior and side/active-cursor context. | Not a blocker for this MOD's conversion surface. For future samples, preserve numeric selector fields and fail closed until real corpus payloads prove old tag conventions. |
| PK-screen flow ops `0x005f/0x0061/0x0062` | Byte structure and screen targets are decoded: `0x005f` calls `PKScreen::PKEnd`, `0x0061` calls `PKScreen::PKShowKO`, and `0x0062` calls `PKScreen::PKActorDie(#0x22)`. The unresolved pieces are the human label for `0x0062` slot values `0/1` and the scheduler meaning of the shared one-shot return counter. | Correlate PK scenes visually; trace `PKScreen::PKActorDie(short)` and the caller that consumes `HandleScript` return values. | Preserve as PK presentation/flow ops, not normal battle death/state changes. |
| PK-screen actor/dialogue/action ops `0x0060/0x0063/0x0064/0x0065/0x0066/0x0068` | Byte structure and `PKScreen` targets are decoded: start screen args, slot-local appear/talk text, action values, and two attack phases are separable. Text is readable UTF-8. The unresolved pieces are human labels for action values `0..13`, attack args `0..4`, constructor args, and whether slot `0/1` maps to left/right, attacker/defender, or another screen-local role. The `0x0063/64/65/66` counts currently come from strict PK tag-shaped scans, with `0x0060/0x0068` matching exact-end controls; a future exact walker should emit these offsets directly. | Correlate PK scenes visually; trace `PKScreen::PKActorAppear`, `PKActorTalk`, `PKActorAction`, `PKActorAttack1/2`, and constructor consumers. Re-run the native exact-end dumper once promoted to a repo tool. | Preserve as numeric PK presentation/dialogue/attack ops; not normal battle movement, HP, actor state, or win/loss semantics. |
| `0x006e ScriptTestProbality` RNG range label | Byte behavior is decoded as `History::getRand() < threshold`, and default RNG initialization uses range `0..99`. The unresolved part is whether any script/runtime path changes the global RNG range before these tests, which would make the human label "percent" too strong in that context. | Trace callers/writers for the global range state used by `History::getRand`; compare probability records in contexts with any RNG-range setup commands. | Numeric `RandomLessThan(threshold)` is safe; label as percent only when default range is known. |
| `0x006f ScriptGoodThrow` quantity/source policy | Target `good_id` and native removal paths are decoded: the handler scans `HistoryGood`, clears matching slots via `SetGoodID(-1)`, handles equipped weapon/coat/third slots, and refreshes actor good effects. The unresolved part is exact priority and quantity when multiple matching goods exist, plus the max-level guard's high-level scenario role. | Trace global count/source fields read near `HandleScript@0x0070b864`-`0x0070b8a4`; compare before/after inventory for repeated ids and max-level goods; correlate S-side rare samples with visible rewards/equipment. | Numeric `RemoveGoodById` is possible; high-fidelity inventory semantics need fail-closed quantity handling. |
| `0x006c` / `0x0070` actor ability-copy labels | Source/target actor fields and copy handlers are decoded enough to prove these are not blobs. The unresolved part is naming copied subfields and `0x0070` category values after `#0x2c - 0x11`. | Trace the getter/setter helpers called from `ScriptActorAbilityCopy::HandleScript` and the `ScriptAbilityChooseCopy` switch targets; correlate visible actor stat/ability deltas after sample events. | Numeric fail-closed copy ops are possible; high-level `CopyAbility` labels need field/category names. |
| `0x0072 ScriptMsgTransmit` mode/list semantics | Text and record structure are intact UTF-8, and the handler reaches actor selection, magic, HP-change, and temporary battle-action helper paths. The unresolved part is the mode-specific list schema and which string-list entries are ids, display text, effect args, or helper selectors. | Trace `GetStringList`, `SelectActor`, `CallMagic`, and `HPChange`; group `0x0072` records by mode `#0x24`, list arity, and neighboring commands. | Do not map blindly to dialogue, HP change, or magic. Preserve mode/string-list numerically until helper schemas are named. |
| `0x0071` / `0x0073` no-op records and `0x007b` / `0x007c` zero-payload context | `0x0071` and `0x0073` parse cleanly but current native handlers return no-op. `0x007b` and `0x007c` handlers consume runtime/default fields, while old EEX `initPara` consumes zero bytes. The unresolved part is the producer/default-field provenance and whether these commands are editor-era markers, runtime-context commands, or package-specific disabled features. | Trace constructors/callers that seed handler fields; compare visual runtime behavior for files containing `0x007b/0x007c`; find another package with nonzero new-format payload if any. | Preserve as markers or fail closed. Automatic conversion must not invent actor/good ids from adjacent bytes. |
| `0x0075 ScriptAssignSImage` visual-state labels | Actor field and assigned value are separated, and native mutates image/appearance-related actor state before marking/updating the actor. The unresolved part is the human label for the value namespace and whether every value is a portrait, sprite, special image, or broader appearance state. | Trace image/bust/sprite loaders and compare values against visible actor appearance changes and image tables. | Numeric fail-closed `SetActorImageState` is possible; do not treat it as equipment or gameplay stat mutation without more proof. |
| `0x0076 ScriptSkipUncondition` list-control semantics | The retained int is alive on both R and battle paths and is passed to the same helper, but the target helper/list semantics are not named. | Trace helper `0x700bf2` and the caller state/list object; compare offsets with logical sublist/count-table ranges. | Cannot flatten to a native `goto` or branch target until list-control semantics are proven. |
| `0x0077 ScriptValueOperation` slot namespaces and native-only branches | Byte structure, exact count, op enum, target namespace `2`, literal RHS, and value-table RHS are decoded. The unresolved part is naming value-table slot ids such as `4072`, `5000`, `5037`, `5300`, and route/roster alias slots `50..64`; target special slot `0x1396`, RHS special slot `0x13a1`, and RHS sources `1/2/3/5` are native-supported but unexercised in this package's canonical scan. | Correlate slot reads/writes with visible route state, roster blocks, variable/value labels, and downstream consumers; find corpus examples or runtime traces for RHS sources `1/2/3/5` and the special branches. | Numeric value-table arithmetic conversion is possible; semantic variable names and fail-closed policy for native-only branches remain required. |
| `0x0078 ScriptValueIntValuation` valuation/classifier labels | Byte structure and exact count are decoded. Mode `1` plus field `32` reaches a native side-byte reclassification path, and classifier values `7/8/9/10` write actor side bytes `0/1/4/4`. The unresolved parts are the human labels for `valuation1` fields such as `9/10/16/17`, the field `32` high-level role, and side-byte-4 faction/class meaning. | Correlate field values with visible actor/party changes; trace `valuation1` branches and side-byte consumers; compare classifier `9/10` contexts with `0x0053`/area selector behavior. | Numeric actor/value valuation can be preserved; human-readable trigger/side labels and native model mapping remain incomplete. |
| `0x0079 ScriptTestValuePlus` source namespaces | Comparator semantics are native-proven (`0 ==`, `1 >=`, `2 <=`), and source selectors/int payloads are separable. The unresolved part is naming nonliteral source namespaces beyond the already observed literal/value-table patterns shared with `ScriptValueOperation`. | Trace `getNum1`/`getNum2` selector cases and find real records for selector values other than the common literal/history forms. | Numeric comparison conversion is possible; human-readable operand labels remain incomplete. |
| Default/native-unsupported cmds `0x001e`, `0x0044`, `0x0049`, `0x0051` | `getScriptByCmd` returns base `Script(cmd)`, preserving the raw short but consuming no command-specific payload. `0x0010` and `0x006a` are absent from parsed scene records; the present markers have counts and neighbors but no safe semantic labels yet. | Compare surrounding root-list labels and runtime behavior; decide whether each maps to no-op, separator, condition delimiter, or unsupported marker. | Required before declaring complete semantic coverage. |
| `ScriptTestStartBattle` / raw `cmd 0x0007` list-selection field | `ScriptTestStartBattle` is payloadless, but `DecodeScenes` has a native special path for `cmd 7` that writes an unnamed handler/global section index. | Compare section ids selected at runtime and trace the handler field written around `0x00708cac`. | Required to name battle start/list switching semantics. |
| `0x0046` / `ScriptDispatchFriend` and `0x0047` / `ScriptDispatchEnemy` remaining child fields | Child counts, file lengths, actor id/index, x/y, and level fields are now partially decoded, and chained parent boundaries are strong enough for actor-id cross-checking. AI/team/status/equipment-like child fields remain unnamed. | Cross-correlate child fields against visible deployment, actor AI behavior, and battle-local roster ids across many S files. | Required for high-fidelity enemy/friend deployment conversion. |
| `0x004a` negative own selectors | Direct `0x004a` values `>= 0` are battle actor ids and `-1` is an empty sentinel. Values `<= -2` are not byte loss: native remaps them through `History* + (0x102e - selector) * 4`, which rewrites to `History+0x40c0 + ((-selector)-2)*4`. Observed values `-53..-66` therefore use alias indices `51..64` and read `History+0x418c..0x41c0`. `History::InitHistory` clears the full alias array; `History::getHistory` saves it into `DSaveHistory+0x124`; `DHistoryParser::DSaveHistory::parseData` reads the persisted array; `History::ParseHistory` restores it to `History+0x40c0`. `ScriptValueOperation` writes live slots through `#0x28`; `#0x2e` is the arithmetic op enum; used RHS forms are literal (`#0x32=0`) and value-table read (`#0x32=4`). `S_71/S_118` assign literal `2000` into slots `50..64` immediately after `出战人员`; `0x004a` consumes the proven subset `51..64`; `ScriptArmyChange` consumes the same alias mechanism. The unresolved part is the route/party concepts these slots name, why slot `50` is set but not yet observed in `0x004a`, and the unused/native-only `getNum2 #0x32=1/2/3/5` pointer namespaces. | Correlate `S_71/S_118` writer blocks and `S_72/S_73/S_119/S_120` consumer stages with visible route/party state; look for non-`0x004a` consumers of slot `50`; find corpus examples or native users of `getNum2 #0x32=1/2/3/5`; name legacy marker fields `#0x2c/#0x30/#0x34`. | Required for exact own roster selection in route-dependent or special stages. |
| `0x004f`, `0x0050`, `0x0053` actor namespaces and remaining enum labels | File shapes and native runtime behavior are now separated: turn/action/leave are not blobs. Battle actor id namespace is strongly supported for enemy/friend ids through `0x0046/0x0047 #0x22`, and own-force low ids now have a structural source in `0x004a` plus placement through `0x004b`. Negative script actor aliases have a proven `History` remap formula and a script writer. `BattleActor::setState` numeric behavior is known; `0x0050` uses closed observed states `-1..12` with native wait evidence and corpus-neighbor examples. `0x0053 getActorList` now names own/friend/enemy/assist side filters for side bytes `0/1/2` plus secondary field `+0x668`; side byte `4` has a native script reclassification source but not a human label. Visual state labels, direction labels, and alias-slot route labels remain open. | Trace visible battle states for `0x0050`; correlate side-byte-4 classifier values `9/10` against visible event context; name `History+0x418c..0x41c0` alias slots; map fallback directions against rendered facing. | Required before a converter can emit human-readable native `BattleOp` names instead of numeric fail-closed ops. |
| `0x0023`, `0x0024`, and variable tag/list field `0x0035` | These have parser boundaries or variable-list roles, but field-level gameplay labels are not complete. | Compare audio/action contexts for `0x0023/0x0024`; compare `0x0035` variable ids with condition labels and runtime value tables. | Required before declaring complete semantic opcode coverage. |
| Battle-to-map binding | Deployment x/y values fit likely maps, but binding must be proven rather than inferred from numbering. | Locate explicit map id reference or campaign table mapping S id to terrainMap id. | Required before safe native stage import. |

## 7. Feasibility Update

This pass strengthens the prior GREEN structural verdict:

- R scripts are not just readable text; scene title/location/dialogue/choices have repeatable op forms.
- S scripts are not just readable text; deployment and equipment blocks have stable binary records.
- Win/lose text is recoverable, and at least part of trigger/event layout is separable.
- `DecodeScenes` raw structural commands, mixed physical record modes, child/subscript skips, and command payload lengths are now strong enough to walk all `1608 / 1608` EEX sections to exact end.
- Native root-list reconstruction is no longer opaque: section headers and count tables expose `9180` root logical sublists across the scene corpus.
- Condition/choice execution is no longer opaque: `ScriptTestValue`, `ScriptElse`, `ScriptShowChoice`, and `ScriptCase` have native stack evidence and corpus-wide counts.
- Condition flag writes are no longer opaque: `0x000b ScriptSetValue` has exact canonical count `71834`, writes byte `0/1` into `base + 0x19b0 + variableId`, and gives the write-side counterpart to `ScriptTestValue` true/false variable lists. Remaining work is naming variable ids and reserved ranges, not recovering flag bytes.
- Battle action execution is no longer opaque at byte level: `0x004f`, `0x0050`, and `0x0053` have native field retention, handler behavior, corpus counts, representative offsets, a decoded `BattleActor::setState` jump table, closed observed `0x0050` numeric state set `-1..12`, side-filter evidence for `0x0053 getActorList`, and strong battle-actor namespace evidence against chained `0x0046/0x0047` deployment parents plus `0x004a/0x004b` own-force structure. `0x0032 ScriptActorMove` also has fixed payload shape, x/y target fields, actor source fields, and battle-side `GenerateDefaultMove` plus `setState(13)` evidence. `0x0055 ScriptBattleActorRelive` and `0x006d ScriptRelaReviveOrMove` now cover absolute relive/re-entry and reference-relative move/relive at byte level, including native calls to `FindNearestBlackPos`, `InitAbilityForRevive`, `CheckPosActor`, and movement state `13`. Negative script actor selectors now have a proven persisted `History+0x40c0` alias-array formula, including init, save-copy, save-parser read, load restore, and `ScriptValueOperation` live writes; the observed writer records are literal assignments of `2000` to slots `50..64`, with `0x004a` currently proven to consume `51..64`. Side byte `4` now has a proven `ScriptValueIntValuation::valuation2` reclassification source. The `0x0403` area guard is also byte-decoded through the active-actor cursor at `History+0x1448c`. Remaining work is naming the alias slots, explaining slot `50`, finding any real uses of `getNum2` RHS `1/2/3/5`, naming `0x0050` visual/action labels, naming side byte `4`, labeling the `0x0403` cursor convention, naming movement/relive direction labels and rare list-source modes, and high-level op mapping, not byte recovery.
- Value-table operations are no longer opaque at byte level: `0x0077 ScriptValueOperation` has fixed `0x18` payload structure, exact canonical count `36998`, a native-proven arithmetic op enum, target namespace `2`, literal RHS records, and value-table RHS records. `0x0078 ScriptValueIntValuation` has fixed `0x12` payload structure, exact canonical count `15054`, mode/actor/field selectors, and a proven `valuation2` side-byte reclassification path for field `32`. Remaining work is naming slot ids, valuation fields, classifier labels, and native-only branch policies, not recovering bytes from a blob.
- Actor stat/ability writes are now byte-decoded for `0x0038`: fixed `0x12` payload, exact canonical count `266953`, actor id, property selector `0..15`, op enum `0/1/2`, and value field. Native setter symbols identify current/base combat stats, HP/MP, level, and `HistoryActor+0xfc`; remaining work is human stat-label polish, high-id actor namespace, and the final label for property `15`, not separating fields from a blob.
- Economy/counter tests and changes are now byte-decoded for `0x0037` and `0x003a`: both have fixed `0x0e` payloads, source fields, comparator/op enums, and int thresholds/values. Source `0` is native-proven money through `History::GetMoney` / `History::SetMoney`; source `1/2` labels remain open, not blob-like.
- Army availability and actor visibility are no longer opaque for `0x003b` and `0x004c`: `0x003b` has fixed `0x0c` payload and exact canonical count `4072`; R-side `0x003b` now has native-proven `ArmyCome` / conditional return-come / `ArmyLeave` directions, and S-side `0x003b` has native-proven battle actor state-byte writes `0/1/2`. `0x004c` has fixed `0x0e` payload and exact canonical count `5486`, resolves actor selectors through the alias mechanism, clears active/visible state, centers/updates, and calls `InitAbilityForRevive`. Remaining work is naming `0x003b` actor `0`, mode/order policy, S-side state-byte labels, and `0x004c` mode/list semantics, not recovering byte fields.
- Item grant and good/equipment mutation are structurally decoded: `0x003d ScriptGetGood` has fixed `0x10` payload, exact canonical count `8474`, live `dic_item.good_id` references, and `HistoryGood` / get-item presentation paths. `0x003e ScriptGoodSet` has exact command-offset count `249`, fixed `0x18` payload, actor/hid plus three good-slot fields, and handler evidence for goods/equipment/default-good updates. Remaining work is slot policy and default/level helper labels, not separating these bytes from a blob.
- Actor HP/state-change execution is now byte-decoded for `0x004d`: fixed `0x42` payload, `1969` strict records, direct/list/area source modes, side selector, operation enum, status mask, HP delta through `HistoryActor::SetCurHp`, and MP delta through `HistoryActor::SetCurMp`. Remaining work is status-mask human labels, opRaw names, and HP edge-case policy, not separating HP/status bytes from a blob.
- Actor AI changes are now byte-decoded for `0x004e`: fixed `0x38` payload, `1060` strict records, direct/area targeting, rectangle bounds, selector, AI mode enum, AI target, and two numeric/coordinate args written to `HistoryActor+6/+0xa/+0xc/+0xe`. Remaining work is naming AI strategy enum values and mode-specific trailing args, not separating AI bytes from a blob.
- Battle barrier/map-element changes are now byte-decoded for `0x0058`: fixed `0x20` payload, `924` strict S-script records, kind id, add/remove flag, tile value, x/y, delay, and post-delay. Native execution constructs and appends a `MapElem` on the add path, finds/removes an existing x/y element on the nonzero-flag path, and can store the tile value into a map byte table. Remaining work is naming kind/tile values and deciding which values are visual-only versus movement/terrain-affecting, not separating barrier bytes from a blob.
- Battle bonus/reward changes are now byte-decoded for `0x0059`: fixed `0x22` payload, `377` strict S-script records, configured money, three reward good-id slots, three retained per-good extra fields, and a retained tail field. Native execution contributes to `History::SetMoney`, creates `HistoryGood` objects from decoded good ids, and opens battle bonus / booty UI paths. Remaining work is computed base-money policy plus extra/tail labels, not separating reward bytes from a blob.
- Battle presentation highlights are now byte-decoded for `0x005b` and `0x005c`: `0x005b` has a fixed `0x1c` rectangle payload and constructs `FogElem` / visible highlight state; `0x005c` has a fixed `0x04` actor payload and calls `History::FindBattleActor` plus `History::CenterActor`. These are presentation/focus records, not hidden win-condition or reinforcement semantics. Remaining work is tail flag and R-side actor namespace labels, not separating highlight bytes from a blob.
- Battle max-round changes are now byte-decoded for `0x005d`: fixed `0x0a` payload, `28` strict S-script records, mode/value fields, and a native `History::SetMaxRound` target. Mode `0` sets `extraMaxRound + value`; mode `1` adds `value`; native mode `2` subtracts `value` but is not observed in this package. Remaining work is old tag labels and unseen-mode policy, not separating round-limit bytes from a blob.
- Actor not-same condition `0x005e` is native-decoded but corpus-absent: fixed `0x08` payload, retained selector fields `#0x22/#0x26`, no-context inequality behavior, and battle-context selector expansion are proven from `libMyGame.so`; the exact-end scene corpus has `0` real `0x005e` command offsets, so this MOD has no convertible `0x005e` stage event.
- PK-screen commands are now byte-decoded for `0x005f/0x0061/0x0062`: `0x005f` and `0x0061` are zero-payload calls to `PKScreen::PKEnd` / `PKScreen::PKShowKO`; `0x0062` is fixed payload `26 00 <slot>` and calls `PKScreen::PKActorDie(short)`. Remaining work is slot-label and scheduler-return labeling, not separating these bytes from a blob.
- PK-screen sequence body is now byte-decoded for `0x0060/0x0063/0x0064/0x0065/0x0066/0x0068`: `0x0068` starts a PK screen with two retained args, `0x0060/0x0063` carry slot-local UTF-8 dialogue text, `0x0064` carries a slot action value, and `0x0065/0x0066` carry source slot / attack arg / target slot. Native handlers call `PKScreen::PKActorAppear`, `PKActorTalk`, `PKActorAction`, `PKActorAttack1`, `PKActorAttack2`, or construct `PKScreen`; they do not mutate battle HP/state or define win/loss. Remaining work is naming visual action/attack/slot labels, not separating structure or text bytes from a blob.
- Probability gates are now byte-decoded for `0x006e`: fixed `0x06` payload, `1202` strict records, threshold int, and native `History::getRand() < threshold` comparison. Default RNG range initializes to `0..99`, making observed thresholds percent-like; remaining work is proving whether any contexts alter the RNG range before a probability test, not separating probability bytes from a blob.
- Inventory/equipment good removal is now byte-decoded for `0x006f`: fixed `0x04` payload, `22066` strict records, target `dic_item.good_id`, and all `244` distinct ids resolving in `json/dic_item.json`. Native execution clears matched `HistoryGood` slots with `SetGoodID(-1)` and refreshes actor good effects for equipped goods. Remaining work is quantity/source priority and max-level policy, not separating good-removal bytes from a blob.
- Late utility/control/value commands are no longer opaque at byte level: `0x006c` and `0x0070` copy actor ability/stat fields between source/target actors, `0x0072` carries intact UTF-8 string/list payloads into message/effect helper paths, `0x0074` writes a retained switch/savefield value, `0x0075` assigns actor image/appearance-related state, `0x0076` drives a list-control helper, `0x0077` mutates integer value-table/history slots with arithmetic ops, `0x0078` evaluates actor/value fields and can reclassify side bytes through `valuation2`, and `0x0079` is a native-proven two-value comparison condition with comparators `==`, `>=`, and `<=`. Remaining work is naming copy categories/subfields, `0x0072` mode/list schemas, `0x0075` visual value namespaces, `0x0076` helper semantics, `0x0077` value-slot namespaces, `0x0078` valuation/classifier labels, and nonliteral `0x0079` source namespaces. `0x0071/0x0073` are parseable no-op records in this build; `0x007b/0x007c` are old-EEX zero-payload commands whose handlers consume runtime/default fields, so they must stay fail-closed until caller provenance is proven.

But this is not yet a converter-ready opcode map. The safe next engineering step is still an offline EEX dumper/ledger, not a native content generator:

1. Promote the temporary exact-end probe into an offline dump tool that emits file offsets: subblock-start `u16 prefix + u16 cmd`, in-subblock cmd-only records, child/subscript extra-short skips, and native `initPara` payload spans.
2. Resolve `cmd -> Script*` through the corrected native table, and use each `Script*::initPara` to advance payload offsets.
3. Emit native logical sublist/count-table reconstruction with cumulative ranges and companion endpoint vectors.
4. Segment named blocks by `ScriptChildInfo` (`0x0002`) labels and header offset regions.
5. Emit nested depth spans and `ScriptCase`/`ScriptElse` groupings for branch-tree validation.
6. Emit every unknown/default marker with file, offset, surrounding hex, and parent block.
7. Only promote a command to converter mapping after cross-file evidence establishes its parameters and id namespace.

## 8. Interim Verdict

GREEN for continued semantic decoding: EEX physical structure is alive and corpus-wide enumerable.

Not green for production conversion yet: branch-tree emission/mapping, condition variable id labels, some actor id namespaces, side-byte-4 human labels, the high-level `0x0403` active-cursor convention, remaining reinforcement/spawn coverage beyond decoded deployment/relive forms, movement/relive direction labels, `0x0037/0x003a` non-money counter labels, `0x0038` property-15 / final stat label polish, `0x003b` actor-0 / mode-order / S-side state-byte labels, `0x003d` auxiliary item-grant fields, `0x003e` slot policy/default-level helper labels, `0x004c` visibility mode/list labels, `0x004d` status-mask human labels / HP edge-case policy, `0x004e` AI enum labels, `0x0058` barrier kind/tile human labels, `0x0059` reward extra/tail labels, `0x005d` old tag labels / unseen decrease-mode policy, native-only-but-corpus-absent `0x005e` sample policy, PK actor slot / scheduler labels for `0x005f/0x0061/0x0062`, PK action/attack/slot visual labels for `0x0060/0x0063/0x0064/0x0065/0x0066/0x0068`, `0x006e` RNG range policy, `0x006f` good-removal quantity/source policy, `0x006c/0x0070` ability-copy field/category labels, `0x0072` mode/list schemas, `0x0075` image/appearance value labels, `0x0076` list-control helper semantics, `0x0077` value-slot namespace labels, `0x0078` valuation/classifier labels, `0x0079` nonliteral source namespaces, and `0x0071/0x0073/0x007b/0x007c` no-op / zero-payload context policy are still undecoded. A converter written now would either discard gameplay semantics or guess them. The honest state is:

> EEX framing/native command classes/text/deployment/equipment/choice cases/simple condition gates/condition flag writes/position-area-round-count/probability conditions, economy/counter test/change byte structure, actor movement/relive, actor stat/ability byte writes, army-change come/leave direction plus battle state-byte structure, actor-visibility byte structure, item-grant and good/equipment-set byte structure, actor HP/state-change byte structure, actor AI-change byte structure, battle barrier/map-element byte structure, battle bonus money/good byte structure, battle presentation-highlight byte structure, battle max-round byte structure, native-only `0x005e` actor-not-same byte behavior, PK-screen flow/dialogue/action/attack byte structure, inventory/equipment good-removal byte structure, value-table arithmetic / actor valuation byte structure, late utility/control op byte structure through `0x007c`, exact physical cursor model, and native root-list count tables are decoded enough to walk and segment all scene sections. Full stage conversion still needs nested branch-tree emission, default marker roles, variable-id labels, remaining field enums, battle-local id namespaces, non-money counter labels, `0x003b` actor-0 / mode-order / S-side state-byte labels, visibility mode/list labels, item-grant auxiliary fields, `0x003e` slot policy/default-level labels, status-mask labels, AI enum labels, barrier kind/tile labels, reward extra/tail labels, round-limit old tag labels, `0x005e` real-corpus sample policy for future packages, PK slot/scheduler/action/attack visual labels, RNG range policy, good-removal quantity policy, value-slot/valuation/classifier labels, late utility/control op mode/category/context labels, and gameplay-op mapping.
